Subject is killed at the close of the Onslaught crisis (alongside the FF and other founding Avengers) and is exiled, by Franklin Richards, to a pocket reality of altered memory and Liefeld/Loeb cosmetics for approximately one subjective year. Returns. The interregnum is file-significant only for the *re-entry behavior*: on return, he undertakes no recovery period and re-enters operational tempo within days. The pattern of *no convalescence* is now a constant in the file across every traumatic dislocation.

## VI. Waid (#1, vol. 3, 1998 → *Man Out of Time*, 2010–11) — Grief Becomes Articulate

Waid's tenure (and his later retrospective *Captain America: Man Out of Time*) constitutes the first sustained writerly attempt to give Subject's grief language. The behavioral content the file gains:

- **Explicit nightmare content**: the Zemo drone, the cold water, Bucky reaching. The dreams are recurrent, decade-stable, and constitute the canonical evidence for the PTSD criterion of intrusive recollection.
- **The Sharon Carter reunion arc**. Sharon, presumed dead, returns from black-ops captivity damaged. Subject re-enters relationship with her on terms of co-damage; the relationship is the closest the middle period comes to one of true peerage of trauma. It is unstable, repeatedly fractured by operational demands, and resumed each time without recrimination. Pattern: *partners who match risk profile* (Workup §3) is at its clearest with Sharon.
- **American Nightmare / "Twisted Tomorrows."** Dream-invasion arc that externalizes his interior; what surfaces is grief and shame, not power-fantasy. Diagnostically aligned with the encysted-affect profile.

## VII. Rieber, Cassaday (vol. 4, 2002–04) — Post-9/11 Reframing

Subject is shown processing the World Trade Center attacks and the political aftermath. Behavioral significance:

- **Refuses to be deployed as morale-iconography.** Declines the administration's overtures to appear at rallies and embedded media positions. Holds the position quietly, without grandstanding.
- **The Dresden flashback (Cassaday).** Subject discloses to a small group of survivors that he was present at the firebombing of Dresden as an Allied combatant and that the memory is one he carries with shame. First on-panel disclosure that his war was not morally simple to him *at the time*, not only in hindsight. The disclosure is brief, factual, unrepeated.

Pattern: *patriotism as ethical practice over patriotism as marketing* is here in its most articulate middle-period form, prefiguring the Civil War posture.

## VIII. Brubaker (vol. 5 #1–#19; *Death of Captain America*, #25–#42; *Reborn*; through #619, 2005–2012) — The Diagnostic Peak

Brubaker's run is the period in which the entire middle-period profile is brought to its load-bearing test.

### VIII.a — Winter Soldier (#1–#14)

Barnes is alive, has been alive for sixty years as a Soviet/post-Soviet wet-work asset, periodically frozen and re-activated, with serial memory wipes. The discovery is delivered to Subject by Nick Fury with the file in hand.

Behavioral content (file-critical):

- The reading of the file is depicted as a sustained, sit-down event. Subject does not interrupt, does not speak, finishes the dossier, and asks one question: where is he now. This is the *briefing-room register* of the Workup §3 at its purest; the affect is fully encysted.
- Subsequent operational tempo is uncharacteristically obsessive — every Winter Soldier sighting is run down personally; sleep is foregone for days. Avengers operations are deferred. This is the only documented sustained operational deprioritization of the team in the entire middle period.
- The Red Skull's Cosmic Cube is used against Barnes; Subject takes the Cube from Barnes, restores his memory (#14), and *does not kill Barnes* despite Barnes asking him to. The line "you don't get off that easy" (paraphrase) is significant: subject reframes Barnes's survival as the obligation to live a repaired life, not as a mercy. The pattern of *taking responsibility for the unstable successor* is now applied to the original peer-attachment of his life.

Following the recovery, Barnes is integrated under Subject's mentorship into the work. The deepening of guilt (Workup §1) is not because Bucky died but because he lived — sixty years, alone, in enemy hands, while Subject froze. This guilt does not surface verbally; it surfaces operationally in the manner of an over-attentive responsibility toward Barnes's recovery (lodging arrangements monitored, mission selection vetted, psychiatric continuity arranged via Stark medical without Barnes's full knowledge — the same care he refuses for himself).

### VIII.b — Death of the Dream (Peggy Carter's funeral, #11–#14 inserts, and elsewhere)

Peggy Carter's dementia and death — visited, in canon, in a


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

*Subject: ROGERS, Steven Grant. Period under review: post-*Secret Empire* (2017) through present operational window. Sources: Coates, *Captain America* vol. 9 #1–25 (2018–2021); Aaron, *Avengers* vol. 8 (selected, 2018–2023); Cates, *Avengers Forever* / *Avengers Assemble* (2022–23); Onyebuchi, *Captain America: Symbol of Truth* (2022–23, with Sam Wilson as co-mantle holder); Lanzing/Kelly, *Captain America: Sentinel of Liberty* (2022–23); Orlando/Straczynski, *Captain America* vol. 10 (2023– ); incidental appearances across line-wide events (*King in Black*, *Devil's Reign*, *Judgment Day*, *Blood Hunt*, *Fall of the House of X / Rise of the Powers of X*). All inferences derived from on-panel behavior; provenance flagged where signal-thin.*

---

## I. The Aftershock Window (post-*Secret Empire*, ~2017–2018)

The operative fact of Subject's recent biography is that he is still, in a meaningful clinical sense, in the long tail of *Secret Empire*. Restoration of the real Rogers from the cosmic-cube-altered Hydra-Steve does not return him to a status-quo ante; it returns him to a world that watched a version of his face wearing Hydra colors, dismantle institutions, conquer the country, and order acts he did not commit but cannot fully disown — because the face was his, and because (per his own logic, repeatedly stated in Coates #1, #5, #16) the **iconography itself was the weapon, and the iconography is something he chose to wear**.

Behavioral consequence, the first six to twelve months post-restoration: Subject is observed (a) refusing reinstatement to formal leadership of the Avengers despite repeated invitations (deferred to others — Carol Danvers, T'Challa, Thor across Aaron's run); (b) traveling alone — bus, motorcycle, on foot — through small towns and county-seat America for an undefined interval, documented in Coates #1–4 as a deliberate listening tour rather than an investigative one; (c) declining several public appearances and one administration invitation (Coates #2, off-panel reference); (d) sleeping in safehouses and motels rather than Avengers Mountain or the Tower for stretches of weeks. The motion pattern is **expiatory** — the gait, dress, and lodging of a man performing penance for things he did not do, because the only available penance for stolen-identity injury is to *demonstrate the real identity in low-status, high-contact settings*.

He does not seek absolution from any institution. He seeks the small unscripted encounter — diner conversations, a Gulf War veteran in a parking lot, an undocumented mother in a church basement (Coates #3, #7) — and uses each as a calibration instrument. The pattern is consistent with his lifelong cognitive style: he reasons morally before tactically; he prefers the ground-truth datum to the briefing.

## II. The Coates Era — *The Captain on Trial* (2018–2021)

The Coates run is the diagnostic centerpiece of Subject's recent life and the document that any total-intelligence file must metabolize in full. Three interlocking arcs structure the period:

**(a) The Power Elite and the framing for Thunderbolt Ross's murder (#1–12).** Subject is framed for the assassination of General Ross by a cabal (Alexa Lukin, Sharon Carter's compromised position, eventual reveal of the Red Skull's consciousness inhabiting Aleksander Lukin's body — a callback to Brubaker). Subject's response to incarceration at the Myrmidon: **he allows himself to be taken**, refuses early extraction offers, and uses the prison interval to organize the prisoners — not for a break, but to listen. This is the load-bearing behavioral tell of the period. He has done this before (the surrender on the courthouse steps in *Civil War* #7); the repeat is not stubbornness, it is a stable operating principle: **when the institution turns on him, he submits to its process so that his eventual opposition cannot be characterized as mere fugitive grievance.** The Civil War lesson he learned was not "do not surrender"; it was "surrender publicly so that the opposition is moral rather than personal." He executes the same play here and survives it.

Inside the prison, observed micro-patterns: refuses commissary above subsistence; sleeps on the floor beside the bunk (the bunk is too soft — a tic that recurs across Brubaker, Remender, and now Coates); rises before lights, performs a calisthenic routine traceable to Army Basic c. 1941 (push-ups, burpees, isometric holds — never the modern variants); eats last in the chow line; intervenes in two assaults on other prisoners, sustains a shiv wound he conceals from the infirmary (Coates #6); reads, repeatedly, a worn paperback identified in one panel as a Steinbeck (*The Grapes of Wrath* — Coates #4, background detail). The reading material is not incidental: Steinbeck is Depression-era Subject's literary contemporary; he is reaching, under stress, for the world he came from.

**(b) The Daughters of Liberty and Sharon Carter (#7–19).** Subject's romantic and operational re-entanglement with Sharon Carter — herself recently restored from prolonged temporal displacement (Waid/Samnee *Captain America* vol. 8 conclusion) and visibly carrying her own complicated grief — is conducted in the Coates run with notable restraint. They co-operate without cohabiting; they share strategic counsel without resumed sexual intimacy until very late in the arc (and even then off-panel, ambiguous). This is consistent with Subject's longitudinal pattern with Sharon: he loves her, he trusts her tactically, he keeps her at the only distance she has ever consented to be kept at — *near enough to fight beside, never near enough to be the person he comes home to undefended*. The Daughters of Liberty (Misty Knight, Mockingbird, Echo, Toni Ho, Spider-Woman, Agent 13) form the surrogate-unit structure that **replaces the Avengers as his primary affective home for the period** — note the gender composition; note also that he positions himself in this unit as a peer and student rather than a commander.

**(c) The Red Skull's "Free Speech" Campaign and the synthesis of Coates #21–25.** Skull, restored, runs not a military campaign but a *podcasting* one — radicalizing young men through grievance rhetoric. Subject's response is the most thematically advanced material in his recent record: he does not engage the radicalized young men with force; he engages them with the question *what did you want, and who told you that you were owed it?* The arc culminates in Subject articulating, in monologue (Coates #25), the operational distinction between the country and the symbol — that the symbol is a *promise the country has not kept*, that his job is to keep the promise even when the country does not, and that the shield is owed to those America has betrayed at least as much as to those it has served. This is the most explicit ideological self-statement Subject has produced in canon and the analytic baseline for everything that follows.

Clinical reading of the Coates period: Subject is functioning at high competence, but the affective signature is **flattened**. Coates writes him as quieter, slower, more given to standing still, more given to silence in scenes where prior runs would have him speak. The "isolation of affect" defense (flagged in §3 of the Analytical Workup) is operating at higher intensity than at any prior point in canon. He is not depressed; he is *containing* — and the container is full.

## III. The Aaron *Avengers* Parallel Track (2018–2023)

Concurrent with Coates, Subject serves on Aaron's Avengers — Carol, Thor, T'Challa, She-Hulk, Ghost Rider (Robbie Reyes), Iron Man, Blade. Observed positioning:

- He is not chair. He votes; he counsels; he is consulted last on contested calls (Hickman-era pattern preserved). When Carol or T'Challa is field-lead, he subordinates without friction.
- He is the unit's **ethical backstop** during *War of the Realms*, *King in Black*, and *Heroes Reborn* (the Coulson-rewritten reality, in which Subject is a Hydra agent — a second forced confrontation with the Hydra-face within a five-year window; observed response on restoration is, again, characteristic: grief and accountability, not denial).
- During *Judgment Day* (Gillen, 2022), Subject is judged by the Progenitor and **passes** — one of the small number who do. The on-panel mechanism is his self-assessment in the moment of judgment: he does not claim virtue; he claims to be *trying*. The Progenitor accepts the framing. Behaviorally, the moment is consistent: he has never claimed virtue; he has claimed effort, and the effort is real.

## IV. The Shield Doubled — Sam Wilson and the Mantle Question (2022–2023)

The simultaneous publication of *Symbol of Truth* (Sam Wilson as Captain America) and *Sentinel of Liberty* (Subject as Captain America) is a publishing fact with diagnostic content: Subject has, *for the first time in canon, sustainably accepted a co-holder of the identity*. The acceptance is not grudging. It is structural. Across both books and the *Cold War* crossover, Subject:

- defers to Sam on questions of jurisdiction in which Sam is more credible (race, displacement, the politics of the shield in non-white America);
- refuses any framing that positions him as the "real" Captain America versus a successor (explicit in *Cold War: Alpha*);
- assumes the elder/mentor role with a humility absent from the Walker arc (Gruenwald #332–350) — he is not training Sam; he is *fielding alongside* Sam.

The longitudinal significance is large. Across sixty years of canon, every prior successor configuration (Walker, Bucky-as-Cap during Brubaker, Sam during Remender/Spencer) was either a substitution Subject endured or one he reluctantly authorized. The current configuration is the first he has affirmatively *built into*. Read clinically: this is partial resolution of the survivor-guilt structure that has organized his life. He is permitting the identity to be carried by others *while he is still alive to see it*, which is the closest thing to a will-and-testament gesture he has ever made.

## V. *Sentinel of Liberty* and the Outer Circle (2022–2023)

Lanzing/Kelly's *Sentinel of Liberty* run reactivates a buried-history conspiracy (the "Outer Circle" — a cabal that has manipulated Subject across his career via cryptic operatives, including a reframed Destroyer/Roger Aubrey and a compromised Bucky). The arc is significant for three behaviors:

1. **Subject lies to Bucky** in the early issues (a tactical concealment about the Outer Circle's reach). This is exceptionally rare in canon and produces a Bucky-side breach that the arc spends issues repairing. The lie is mission-justified and Subject acknowledges it as wrong even as he commits it — a marker of the moral-realism cognitive style under pressure.
2. **Subject's tradecraft tightens visibly**. He runs counter-surveillance routes in Brooklyn (specifically the Red Hook waterfront and the Vinegar Hill blocks — geography he knew as a child, now gentrified beyond recognition), uses pay phones, uses dead drops in the older parts of Prospect Park. The reversion to 1940s tradecraft under modern threat is not nostalgia; it is the recognition that pre-digital methods are *unindexable* to opponents who run on digital infrastructure.
3. **Sleep deprivation becomes operationally visible.** Multiple panels across the arc depict him awake at 0300–0500 in his Brooklyn walk-up (the apartment is small, sparse, top-floor, walk-up — a deliberate retention of pre-serum living conditions), reviewing files, drawing. The drawing is consistent: pencil, cheap newsprint pad, figure studies and street scenes — the practice he kept as a young man at the Art Students League equivalent. He draws when he cannot sleep. He sleeps four to five hours on a good night; under operational load, two to three.

## VI. *Captain America* vol. 10 (Orlando, 2023– ) — Brooklyn, Labor, and the Return to Origin

The current ongoing has placed Subject *back in Brooklyn full-time*, working a day job (manual labor / community organizing visible in early issues), with the Captain America operation handled out of the apartment and a small support cell (Bucky-adjacent, with Sharon at one remove, and a new generation of younger operatives). This is the most geographically and existentially **regressive** configuration Subject has occupied since the 1940s — by design.

Observed current-state behavioral baseline (consolidating across all 2023–present sources):

- **Domicile:** small walk-up in a Brooklyn neighborhood that was working-class when he left and is now mixed; he rents, he does not own; landlord does not know his real identity; he pays in cash or money order; refuses building Wi-Fi; uses a burner for personal communication and a hardened line through Avengers infrastructure for operational traffic.
- **Furnishing:** bed frame and mattress (uses the floor beside it under stress, per Brubaker, Remender, Coates continuity), a small wooden table, two chairs, a record player and a small vinyl collection skewed pre-1945 (Ellington, Goodman, Holiday — observed in Onyebuchi *Cold War* tie-in and Orlando #2), a kitchen functional to one person, the drawing pad on the table, the shield in a closet under a coat. No television. One bookshelf: history (Howard Zinn, James Baldwin, Studs Terkel, Doris Kearns Goodwin, a Steinbeck shelf, a Hemingway shelf he is more ambivalent about, a worn Bible his mother's), a small photo of Sarah Rogers in a tarnished frame, no photo of Bucky or Peggy displayed (those are kept in a drawer; this is a tell — the unmetabolized losses cannot be on the wall).
- **Diet:** large by mass (the metabolism requires it), simple in composition, prepared from raw ingredients, eaten standing or at the small table. He does not eat out alone; he eats out only when invited.
- **Daily routine (reconstructed):** wake 0500 or earlier; calisthenic block 30–45 min (the old Army routine, never updated); cold water (no caffeine, no stimulant — the post–Streets of Poison phobic-grade avoidance is fully intact thirty subjective years on); newspapers, print, three to five (he still reads the *Times* in print, and at least one local paper; intermittently the *Bugle*); operational review; either day-job presence or community work; evenings either operational, with Sam, or alone with the drawing pad. Lights out variable; sleep light, broken, scanning.
- **Dress out of uniform:** plain — t-shirt, jeans or chinos, a worn brown leather jacket, boots; in cold weather a navy peacoat retained from his original service or its replacement; a watch, analog, wound, his father's or a replacement of it (continuity unclear; the watch recurs).
- **Verbal register:** has retained the Brooklyn vowels under stress and in private; cleans them up in public address. Uses period idiom under fatigue ("swell," "fella," "on the level"); the lapse is involuntary and is one of the surest current tells of stress load. Across the Coates run and Orlando, the period idiom returns more frequently than at any point in the prior decade — a marker that the affective load is climbing.

## VII. The Relational Map, Current

- **Bucky Barnes:** repaired post-*Sentinel of Liberty*; they communicate weekly minimum; they do not live together; the Brubaker-era arrangement of *we both know what we owe each other and we both know we cannot fix each other* is preserved.
- **Sam Wilson:** the central peer-bond of the current period; co-mantle, mutual deferral, easy. The healthiest relationship in Subject's life by every observable metric.
- **Sharon Carter:** present, operationally adjacent, romantically ambiguous; she has her own grief to carry and he does not crowd her.
- **Peggy Carter:** deceased (vol. 5 #14). He visits the grave. He goes alone. He does not announce the visits. The visit is monthly minimum, per inference from absences in operational logs across the Coates and Orlando runs.
- **Tony Stark:** rapprochement, partial; the Civil War wound is not closed but is no longer load-bearing in current operations. They work together when required and do not socialize.
- **The Avengers, as institution:** he is a member, not the leader; he attends; he speaks last; he votes.
- **Successors and mentees (current cohort):** Sam principally; Kate Bishop intermittently; Miles Morales (occasional counsel); the new generation that has come up around the *Champions* and *Strange Academy* configurations; Ian Rogers (status uncertain — Remender's *Dimension Z* son remains the largest unhealed wound of the modern era; on-panel reference is sparse and Subject does not raise the topic).

## VIII. Pathophysiology of the Present

Translating the above into a clinical present-state summary:

- **Complicated/Prolonged Grief:** unchanged in structure, partially mitigated by the Sam Wilson co-mantle arrangement (the first structural concession to the possibility of being *succeeded*, which is the only durable treatment for the survivor-guilt structure).
- **PTSD, chronic:** unchanged; hyperarousal harnessed; intrusive recollection elevated post–Hydra-Steve and post–Heroes Reborn (two forced confrontations with the Hydra face in five years); avoidance behaviors mildly intensified (declines public appearances at a higher rate than baseline).
- **Adjustment / "Man Out of Time" syndrome:** *paradoxically improved* by the return to Brooklyn and the day-job configuration, which has restored a quotidian texture absent since 1945; offset by accelerating gentrification of the geography itself (the streets he knew are gone even from inside Brooklyn), which has produced a new and subtler form of the dislocation — *home, but not home*.
- **MDD, recurrent:** no current episode; partial remission stable.
- **New observation: increased solitude.** The hours-alone count is higher than at any point in the prior decade. He is not isolated (Sam, Bucky, Sharon, the Avengers); he is *deliberately solitary*. This is consistent with two readings: (a) the containment is full and he requires more time alone to manage it; (b) he is preparing, consciously or not, to step back from the central position — the Brooklyn re-rooting, the co-mantle, the deferral pattern all point in the same direction.

## IX. Current Operational Status and the Trajectory

As of the most recent observation window: Subject is **active, deployable, voluntarily under-positioned, geographically re-rooted, relationally repaired, and clinically stable in the chronic-grief / chronic-PTSD configuration that has organized his adult life**. He is not in crisis. He is also not at peace — peace is not, on the evidence, an available endpoint for this Subject; *equilibrium under load* is, and he is at it.

The trajectory inferred from the convergent signals — the Sam Wilson succession, the Brooklyn return, the day-job re-grounding, the increasing solitude, the *Judgment Day* self-assessment, the Coates monologue articulating the shield as a debt to the betrayed — is **toward a long, voluntary, partial retraction**. He will not retire. He cannot; the analytic logic of §3 holds — to lay it down is to default on the dead. But he is building the conditions under which the identity can be *carried by others while he is alive to see it carried well*, which is the closest a man with this etiology can come to permission to rest.

The file's working forecast: barring catastrophic event, Subject will be observed over the next operational window (a) continuing to field as Captain America in reduced rotation, (b) increasing the elder-counsel function, (c) deepening the Brooklyn re-rooting and the day-job texture, (d) maintaining the relational map without expansion, and (e) sustaining the chronic clinical picture without decompensation. The catastrophic-event sensitivity remains what it has always been: harm to Sam, to Bucky, to Sharon, or to a non-combatant in his line of sight will produce the same instant, predictable, self-trading response it has produced for eighty subjective years. That has not changed and will not.

*— End Chronology IV. Continue to Chronology V (Forecast & Risk) or to Section 6 (Synthesis) per directing officer's instruction.*


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT

*Compiled from public medical record reconstruction, military induction and post-induction files (War Department, 1940–45, partially declassified), SHIELD medical archive (1964–present), Avengers Mansion/Tower infirmary logs, and longitudinal observation. Where contemporaneous records do not exist, conditions are inferred from documented sequelae and from the subject's own intermittent self-report. The structure of this section is somatic, but every entry closes on its psychological residue: in this subject, no injury is ever only an injury.*

---

## I. THE PRE-SERUM BODY (c. 1922–June 1941)

### 1. Constitutional and Developmental

Subject's birth weight is not preserved in extant records, but maternal report (relayed through later interview) and the consistent depiction across attending writers describe a low-birth-weight infant, slow to thrive, with persistent feeding difficulty in the first year. Sarah Rogers — RN, sanatorium-trained — almost certainly kept the child alive by application of her own professional knowledge in a tenement context where pediatric care was effectively unavailable. The subject's lifelong, almost reverent posture toward nurses (visible decades later in his unfailing courtesy to medical staff, his refusal to brush off triage personnel in disaster scenes, his quiet preference for being treated by women in scrubs over men in coats) is traceable to this primary caregiving experience.

Growth was stunted. Adult pre-serum height is recorded variably between 5'4" and 5'6"; weight 95–115 lb; build asthenic; bone density low; musculature underdeveloped due to chronic illness and exercise intolerance. Skeletal survey on enlistment showed mild thoracic scoliosis (right-convex, ~12°), narrow chest cavity (Haller index moderately elevated), and several remodelled fractures (see §3).

### 2. Respiratory

**Asthma**, severe and persistent from early childhood. Documented across enlistment-rejection files (4F classification was assigned on multiple grounds; asthma was the most-cited). Episodes were frequent, exercise-triggered, cold-triggered, and dust-triggered — significant given coal-heat tenement living and a city whose air in the 1920s–30s was substantially worse than now. Likely complicated by undiagnosed allergic rhinitis (chronic mouth-breathing, recurrent sinusitis below). Treatment available to him would have been minimal: theophylline-adjacent preparations, the occasional adrenaline injection at a clinic, otherwise endurance.

**Chronic sinusitis**, recurrent, with at least one episode severe enough that maternal records (per later interview material) suggested orbital cellulitis was feared. Persistent post-nasal drainage, anosmia in worse periods.

**Sequelae of scarlet fever**, contracted in childhood (Brubaker flashback material; consistent with the era's epidemiology in Lower East Side tenements). The scarlet fever almost certainly produced the **rheumatic fever** episode that left him with the cardiac findings below, and is plausibly responsible for the **partial sensorineural hearing loss in the left ear** noted in his SHIELD-era audiograms — a finding the subject does not advertise but compensates for behaviorally (he turns his right side to speakers in noisy rooms; he positions himself with the left ear toward walls in tactical settings; he reads lips faster than he should need to).

### 3. Cardiovascular

**Rheumatic mitral involvement**, mild — a soft holosystolic murmur was noted on enlistment exam, with grade I–II/VI radiation to axilla; valve was competent but thickened. Combined with the **hypertension** noted on the same exam (paradoxical in a malnourished, slender adolescent, and likely secondary to chronic pain, anxiety, and stimulant exposure from over-the-counter ephedrine-class asthma preparations of the day), this constituted one of the harder grounds for the 4F.

**Anemia**, microcytic, chronic — consistent with both nutritional deficiency and possible thalassemia trait given Irish heritage variability; documented pallor, exercise intolerance, cold extremities, occasional syncope.

### 4. Musculoskeletal and Traumatic — The Alley Record

The pre-serum body bears the imprint of the behavior that defines the subject's psychology: he did not walk away from fights he could not win. Old fracture lines on enlistment films and post-serum reconstructive imaging suggest, at minimum:

- Two **healed nasal fractures**, deviated septum, contributing further to the chronic sinusitis.
- A **left zygomatic** fracture (orbital floor not involved), poorly reduced, leaving a faint cosmetic asymmetry that disappears post-serum but recurs each time the serum is depleted.
- **Right fifth metacarpal** (boxer's fracture), healed in slight angulation — a non-trivial finding in a boy who almost never landed a punch cleanly; suggests a fall onto the hand or, more likely, a hand-strike against bone he should not have struck.
- Multiple **rib contusions and at least one healed posterior rib fracture** on the left.
- **Recurrent ankle sprains**, ligamentous laxity bilaterally.
- **Scoliosis** as above; chronic mechanical low back pain in cold weather.
- **Dental disease** consistent with Depression-era working-class oral health: several caries, one extraction (premolar), gingivitis — all resolved post-serum but the habit of declining dental cosmetic intervention persists (he does not whiten, he does not straighten; pre-serum dentition imperfections recur when serum is suppressed and he does not address them).

### 5. Other Documented Conditions, Pre-Serum

- **Pernicious anemia** suspected but never definitively worked up (vitamin B12 unavailable as therapy in any reliable form until the late 1940s).
- **Pes planus**, bilateral — listed on the 4F.
- **Color vision**: normal (verified post-serum; clinically relevant only insofar as it refutes a rumor in some files).
- **Allergies**: documented to penicillin (pre-serum trial reaction, urticarial; the allergy is purged by the serum and reintroduction tolerance is documented in SHIELD pharmacy notes).
- **Gastroesophageal reflux**, likely; documented dyspepsia, exacerbated by stress.
- **Recurrent boils and impetigo** in adolescence, consistent with overcrowded living and immune compromise.

### 6. Psychological Sediment of the Pre-Serum Body

This is the most important paragraph in the somatic section. The subject lived inside an unreliable instrument for the first two decades of his life. He learned, very early, that his will exceeded his capacity, that pain was the price of remaining who he was, that adults' kindness toward him was inflected by pity, and that the woman he loved most was killing herself nursing strangers (and ultimately himself) while he lay coughing in the next room unable to help. Three durable orientations are laid down here and never alter:

1. **The vulnerable are not abstract to him.** He has been them. He still is them, internally. Every protective decision he later makes is made from inside the asthmatic body he is no longer in.
2. **His own pain does not register on the normal scale.** Decades of low-grade chronic illness produced a baseline pain tolerance that the serum subsequently elevated to the superhuman, but the *attitude* toward pain — that it is the weather, not an event — was set in childhood.
3. **Care received is suspect; care given is the only safe currency.** He never quite trusts a clinician's reassurance about himself. He invariably trusts a clinician's instruction about someone else.

---

## II. THE TRANSFORMATION (June 1941, Brooklyn — Project Rebirth)

### 1. Procedure as Performed

Intramuscular and intravenous administration of the Erskine super-soldier serum, sequenced with sustained exposure to Vita-Ray bombardment in a sealed chamber under monitored telemetry (cardiac, respiratory, EEG — to the limits of 1941 instrumentation). Procedure duration on the order of an hour. The subject was conscious through the painful phase; the canonical record includes both the visual transformation and the subject's documented refusal to abort despite distress.

### 2. Acute Physiological Effects

- Height gain: approximately +6 to +8 inches over hours-to-days post-procedure.
- Mass gain: ~120 lb of predominantly lean tissue, achieved against thermodynamics by means the serum's metabolic chemistry has never been adequately reverse-engineered.
- Resolution of asthma, sinusitis, anemia, hypertension, scoliosis (the subject's spine straightened, an event for which there is no orthopedic analog), murmur, dental disease, flat feet, allergies, hearing deficit, and effectively the entire pre-existing condition list within approximately 48–72 hours.
- Acute pain during and immediately post-procedure was, by his own later report, "considerable" — a register, in his idiom, meaning *the most pain a human being can experience*.

### 3. Persistent Enhancements (Steady-State Post-Serum)

- **Musculoskeletal**: peak human strength in the early canon, low-superhuman in the modern (press capacity ~1100 lb under good conditions; cited variances are writer-dependent). Tendon and ligament tensile strength elevated proportionally, which matters — most "super-strength" injuries occur because the soft tissues do not scale; his do.
- **Cardiopulmonary**: resting heart rate documented at 40–50 bpm; recovery from maximal exertion within seconds; VO2 max off any normative chart.
- **Metabolic**: ~95% caloric efficiency; daily caloric requirement on operational days estimated 5,000–6,000 kcal; ketosis-resistant; near-immune to standard intoxicants because hepatic clearance exceeds intake rate (see §V on substances).
- **Immune**: functionally immune to all known human infectious agents; demonstrated resistance to weaponized pathogens including several Hydra and AIM bioweapons.
- **Healing**: rapid but not instantaneous. Lacerations close in hours, fractures consolidate in days, neural injury heals incompletely (concussions still register; cumulative concussion load — see §IV — is the single most clinically interesting injury pattern in the SHIELD file).
- **Sensory**: vision and hearing at the upper end of human normal; not telescopic, not ultrasonic; proprioception and reaction time markedly enhanced.
- **Thermal**: tolerance of extreme cold and heat extended but not unlimited (relevant to the ice — see §III).
- **Sleep**: requires approximately 4 hours; tolerates total deprivation for 72–96 hours without measurable cognitive decrement; chronic sleep deprivation produces emotional rather than cognitive symptoms (see Psychiatric).

### 4. Psychological Impact of the Transformation Itself

The subject did not experience the transformation as becoming a different person; he experienced it, by all evidence, as becoming legible. The body he had always implicitly possessed — the body that matched his will — arrived. This is somatically and psychologically critical: it forecloses the more common post-enhancement pattern of *new-body grandiosity*. He did not get a power; he got an instrument. The instrument is held in trust. Erskine's assassination within hours of the procedure cemented this orientation by binding the new body to a debt the moment it arrived.

A subtler residue: the subject is, to this day, almost certainly somatically uncertain that the new body is permanent. Every depletion event (see §VII) confirms an underlying suspicion that the sick boy is the substrate and the soldier is the loan.

---

## III. THE ICE (April 1945 – c. 1964 narrative time)

### 1. Mechanism

Subject entered North Atlantic waters at high velocity from the Zemo drone, in arctic conditions, in the immediate aftermath of witnessing Barnes's apparent death. Serum-mediated cellular near-stasis combined with rapid environmental cryopreservation produced suspended animation. Recovered by the Avengers (*Avengers* #4). No frank tissue damage on revival; no frostbite sequelae; no documented re-warming injury.

### 2. The Clinical Event That Matters

The ice is not, medically, a cold injury. It is a **dissociative dislocation event of approximately two decades**, somatically smooth and psychologically catastrophic. Subject went under conscious of grief, of mission failure, and of a specific cultural-temporal context. Subject revived into a world without his cohort, his idiom, his streets, his president, his radio, his slang, his war, or his dead. The body did not register the gap; the self registered nothing else.

Subsequent imaging has shown no neurological abnormality referable to the cryopreservation. The psychiatric sequelae — sleep onset difficulty, cold-trigger flashback (he is not phobic of cold but his affect flattens in arctic settings), recurrent dreams of icy water, an idiosyncratic dislike of being alone in white-walled rooms — are all real, and all under-reported by the subject.

### 3. The Aftershock Pattern

A characteristic feature: subject experiences periodic, brief, somatically expressed re-experiencing of the ice transition, typically on first waking in unfamiliar quarters. Duration seconds. He has trained himself out of any visible response; the autonomic signature (transient bradycardia followed by a sympathetic spike, briefly elevated cortisol) is detectable on continuous monitoring during overnight medical observation but not on casual examination. He does not volunteer it.

---

## IV. INJURY LEDGER (Post-Serum)

Across the operational record, injuries number in the thousands. Categorically:

- **Blunt trauma**: incalculable. Concussions sufficient in number and severity that, in a non-serum subject, the cumulative CTE risk would be terminal. Serum-mediated neural repair is the only reason the subject is not, by his eighth decade of subjective combat life, demented. There are nevertheless intermittent SHIELD neurological notes — minor short-term memory lapses post-severe-impact events, lasting hours to a day — that the subject characteristically does not report.
- **Penetrating trauma**: dozens of gunshot wounds (he has been shot in the chest, abdomen, both thighs, both shoulders, the neck, and twice in the head — the last during the courthouse-step assassination); dozens of stab wounds; arrow and edged-weapon injuries; energy-weapon burns of every conceivable spectrum.
- **The assassination, *Captain America* #25 (2007).** Sniper round (Crossbones, externally) and multiple close-range pistol rounds (Sharon Carter, under mind control). Subject died on the courthouse steps. The medical fact of the death is real within the canon. The subsequent revelation of temporal displacement (*Reborn*) does not retroactively annul the event; the subject's body sustained, and the subject's consciousness experienced, lethal trauma. Resurrection has its own clinical implications, addressed below.
- **Major thermal**: multiple second- and third-degree burn events, all healed without scarring sequelae.
- **Drowning / asphyxia**: several documented near-asphyxiation events, including the ice and at least three subsequent submersion combats; serum-mediated apnea tolerance is significant but not unlimited.
- **Radiation**: cumulative exposure across decades non-trivial; subject has been irradiated by cosmic, gamma, and exotic energies on multiple occasions without measurable mutagenic effect (the serum appears to confer chromosomal stability).
- **Fractures**: every long bone has been broken at least once; multiple rib fractures (chronic, he heals over them in days); skull fractures (linear and depressed) on at least three occasions; pelvic fracture once (high-fall event).
- **Spinal**: at least one transient cord injury (sensory level briefly to T6 after a powered-armor strike), resolved within 48 hours with full recovery.
- **Ocular**: corneal lacerations, retinal hemorrhage on multiple occasions, all resolved.
- **Cardiac**: at least two documented episodes of clinical cardiac arrest in operational settings, both reversed (once by serum autoresuscitation, once by external defibrillation administered by a teammate); subject does not list these in his own medical summaries.

### Psychological Effect of the Injury Ledger

He has decades of empirical evidence that his body tolerates what kills others. The clinical consequence is not bravado; it is something more troubling. He has lost, somatically, the capacity to estimate his own mortality at the rate ordinary people do. When he steps in front of harm, he is not being courageous in the conventional sense — he is acting from a database that says *I will probably get up*. The diagnostic problem this poses is that on the occasions when he will *not* get up, he has no internal warning system. His risk-taking is therefore best understood as **invulnerability-adjacent self-perception**, not suicidality, but the behavioral result can be hard to distinguish from suicidality from the outside, particularly in periods of acute grief. Monitoring during such periods (post-Bucky, post-Peggy, post-Civil War, post-*Secret Empire*) is clinically warranted.

---

## V. SUBSTANCE HISTORY

### 1. Alcohol

Cannot achieve intoxication at any human-survivable dose. Documented across the canon (*Captain America Annual* #4 and recurring). He drinks socially — rarely — out of communion rather than effect. The psychological consequence is large and under-appreciated: **the most accessible coping mechanism in his cohort and profession is foreclosed to him.** Every other veteran in his social and operational world has had access to a chemical floor under their grief. He has not. The grief that other men dissolve, he carries.

### 2. Tobacco

Brief documented experimentation in the war years (cultural ubiquity); never habituated; serum metabolism makes nicotine subjectively negligible.

### 3. Caffeine

Tolerated; subjectively negligible; he drinks coffee for warmth and ritual, not effect. He prefers it black, hot, and large, and he drinks it slowly — observers often note he is still nursing the first cup when others have had three.

### 4. Pharmacological Agents

Generally subjectively negligible. Anesthetics require massive overdose to produce effect and are avoided where possible. Antibiotics unnecessary. Analgesics — including opiates — produce minimal subjective relief. The clinical consequence: **he cannot be sedated, and he cannot be anesthetized except by exotic means.** During the rare procedures requiring it, induction is difficult, maintenance is difficult, and he tends to wake mid-procedure. He bears it.

### 5. The Streets of Poison Event (Gruenwald, *Captain America* #372–378)

Non-consensual exposure to the designer stimulant "Ice," concentrated sufficiently to penetrate his metabolic clearance. Subject experienced acute disinhibition, paranoid features, uncharacteristic interpersonal aggression, and brutal — not merely effective — combat behavior. Serum eventually purged the agent. Subject has, since, exhibited **phobic-grade avoidance** of any deliberate alteration of mental state. He will not accept ordinary sedatives even where indicated. He resists premedication. He has been known to refuse post-operative analgesia even where he could metabolize it.

The clinical significance is not the drug. It is what the drug revealed: that beneath his inhibitory architecture there is an aggression he is not certain he could contain if the inhibition failed. This is the same fear that organizes his refusal to become his father. The Streets of Poison exposure is, in psychiatric terms, **the canonical confirmation of the worst hypothesis he holds about himself**, and he has organized his pharmacological behavior around never confirming it again.

### 6. Other Exotic Exposures

The serum itself is a chronic somatic exposure; mind-control agents (recurrent, across many writers); Cosmic Cube reality alteration (the *Secret Empire* event); the temporal displacement of *Reborn*; the Dimension Z multi-year immersion. Each is treated by him as an injury done to his agency rather than to his body, and each leaves a quieter version of the Streets of Poison residue: increased fastidiousness about chain of custody, about what he eats and drinks in unfamiliar settings, about who has access to him while he sleeps. He has, demonstrably, never become paranoid. He has become careful in a way that paranoid people sometimes resemble.

---

## VI. SURGICAL HISTORY

Strikingly minimal. The serum's healing capacity has rendered most surgical indications moot. Recorded procedures include:

- **Foreign-body removals** on several occasions (shrapnel, bullet fragments where serum encapsulation rather than expulsion occurred).
- **Reduction and fixation** of complex fractures on at least four occasions where serum healing risked malunion (his right humerus, his left tibia, his pelvis, his mandible).
- **Dental work**, minimal, occasional.
- **Reconstructive** procedures following the assassination — extensive but not, in the end, the cause of his return; the return was temporal, not surgical.
- **Cardiac monitoring lead placements** during the *Reborn* recovery and on at least two other occasions of serum destabilization.

He is a poor surgical candidate not because his body is fragile but because it is non-compliant: tissues knit around instruments, drugs underperform, vital signs do not behave as references predict. SHIELD developed bespoke protocols by the late 1960s and these remain in use.

---

## VII. SERUM DESTABILIZATION AND DE-SERUM EVENTS

The serum is not perfectly stable. Periodic destabilization is documented:

- **The "Captain America No More" / Streets of Poison aftermath** (Gruenwald): physiological strain.
- ***Captain America* vol. 5 "Reborn"** (Brubaker): temporal-displacement event with somatic correlates.
- **The Spencer "de-serumed" arc** (Remender/Spencer transition): subject's serum was neutralized; he aged rapidly into a frail nonagenarian body resembling, with cruel symmetry, the pre-serum Steve grown old. He retained command capacity, mentored, advised, and was — by the testimony of those closest to him — *recognizably himself*. This is the most important medical observation in the entire file: **the serum amplified him; it did not constitute him.** When stripped of every enhancement, the subject who remained was the same one who had picked himself up in the alley.

The psychological consequence of having lived through de-serumed periods is twofold. First, he has had his most-feared confirmation (he can be returned to the failing body) and survived it without identity collapse — which has produced a quiet, hard-won somatic confidence that did not exist before. Second, he carries a permanent low-grade awareness that the body is borrowed, which deepens rather than threatens the ethical posture: a borrowed instrument must be spent well.

---

## VIII. AGING AND THE LONG SOMATIC EXPOSURE OF OUTLIVING

The serum effectively retards aging; estimates vary, but the subject's biological age is decades behind his chronological-since-birth age and roughly tracks his post-thaw operational years. The medical consequence is not physiological — there is nothing pathological about his


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT

*Compiled from sixty-plus years of panel record, cross-referenced against the pre-serum baseline. The body is a document; this is the closest reading we have of it. All states keyed to four registers: CALM (off-duty / among trusted intimates), STRESS (operational load, ambiguous social pressure), THREAT (active combat / imminent harm to others), INTIMACY (touch-permissive proximity — sexual, fraternal, grief-shared).*

---

## I. THE TWO BODIES (a necessary preface)

Any somatic file on this subject must hold two skeletons in mind simultaneously. The 5'4", ~95 lb pre-serum body — narrow shoulders, pectus excavatum-adjacent sternum, scoliotic left-leaning spine, knock-knees, a head that looked one size too large on the neck — and the post-Rebirth ~6'2", ~240 lb body, broad-deltoid, V-tapered, with the muscular architecture of a decathlete rather than a powerlifter. The crucial observation: **the small body's *gestural grammar* survived the large body's adoption.** He still holds his shoulders as if they are narrow. He still tucks his chin as if to make a smaller target. He still apologizes physically through space he is entitled to. Witnesses who knew him in 1940 (Barnes, Carter in the early flashbacks) report the recognition shock not at the face but at the *carriage* — same boy, scaled up.

This is the master-key for everything below. The serum gave him a body; it did not give him the unselfconsciousness of someone who has always had one.

---

## II. POSTURE & STANCE

**Standing (CALM).** Weight slightly forward on the balls of the feet, never on the heels — a fighter's distribution he holds even when reading a newspaper. Feet at roughly shoulder-width, the left a half-step ahead (southpaw boxing root, visible across the Stern, Brubaker, and Waid runs in idle-conversation panels). Hands typically clasped behind the back at rest in the parade-rest he learned from Army drill in 1941 and never unlearned; or, less formally, thumbs hooked into a belt loop, or one hand cupping the opposite elbow. He does not put his hands in his pockets. The shoulders ride high and slightly rolled inward — the residue of the small body — and he periodically and consciously rolls them back and down, a self-correcting tic visible whenever he becomes aware of being looked at.

**Standing (STRESS).** The chin drops a quarter-inch. The clasped hands behind the back release; the dominant hand drifts to his hip or to the seam of his trouser leg, fingers lightly drumming once or twice before stilling. Weight redistributes to even-footed. He locates the room's exits in a slow, three-beat scan: door, window, sightline-of-blast. He has done this without conscious choice since 1942.

**Standing (THREAT).** Sinks two inches — a measurable drop in hip height — into a wide, slightly cat-stanced base. Shoulders square, chin tucks into the trapezius hollow. Hands open and slightly forward of the body, palms angled down. He does *not* fist his hands until the moment of strike; the open hand is faster to the shield, faster to a grab, and (psychologically) less committed to having already decided to hurt the person across from him. He shifts subtly between conversational partners to keep no civilian behind him in the line of fire — an unconscious geometric reorientation his teammates have learned to read as a tactical warning.

**Standing (INTIMACY).** The rarest posture in the file. The forward weight resolves; he stands flat-footed. The shoulders genuinely drop — not the self-correcting reset, an actual unloading. The chin lifts. He gets a half-inch taller. Observed across the entire canon perhaps a few dozen times: with Peggy in 1944 dance-hall flashbacks; with Bucky in Howling Commandos downtime; with Sam Wilson in the late-Brubaker quiet scenes; in Dimension Z domestic panels with Ian; in the kitchen with Sharon during the Gruenwald years.

**Seated.** Sits forward, never deep into the chair, weight on the front third of the seat, feet flat and slightly apart, hands on the knees or one forearm braced on a thigh. He cannot make himself slouch. Even reading, even watching television, even at three in the morning at his own kitchen table, the spine is recruited. The single exception is sleep-adjacent collapse in safe spaces (the Tower common rooms in Hickman's *Avengers*; the Brooklyn brownstone in Waid) where he will lean against a wall or a counter rather than truly recline — an upright doze that costs him no readiness.

---

## III. GAIT

**Walking pace (CALM):** roughly 3.4 mph, unusually consistent — he does not vary stride with mood, only with intention. Heel-strike is light, almost ball-first; he walks the way a man walks in a hospital corridor at 2 a.m. **Stride length** is shorter than a man his size warrants — another small-body residue; he was a 28-inch-inseam person who learned to walk in a 34-inch-inseam body and still under-utilizes the leverage.

**Walking (STRESS):** pace climbs to ~4.0 mph; stride still short; arm swing decreases, hands tend toward the hip-pocket region of an absent sidearm.

**Walking (THREAT approach):** the famous shift — pace *decreases*. He slows on a closing target. The shoulders square forward, the head levels (chin neither tucked nor lifted), the arms still. Witnesses consistently describe it as "going quiet" — the loudest sound in the room becomes the absence of his footfall, because he begins to land entirely on the forefoot.

**Running.** Two distinct gears. The "civilian" run — what bystanders see — is a controlled lope at ~15 mph that he can hold for hours, characterized by economical mid-foot strike, a relaxed jaw, and arms cycling close to the ribcage. The "operational" run, displayed when he believes no one not on his team is observing, is something else entirely: a forward-leaning sprint with a near-horizontal torso angle and an arm carriage that drops to waist level (lower than the textbook), reportedly clocked in the canon at speeds Sam Wilson has needed wings to match. He is mildly embarrassed by it and will downshift the moment a civilian rounds a corner.

**Stair behavior:** two at a time, always, ascending or descending, in or out of uniform. A pre-serum compensation (the asthmatic boy who could not afford to be slow on the stoop) that fossilized.

---

## IV. THE FACE

**The resting face (CALM).** Mouth closed, lips lightly together with no compression, the corners neutral or fractionally turned up — what photographers in his USO years learned to capture as "open." Eyes wide-set, blue, with a habitual *soft focus* at middle distance when listening; he does not lock eye contact in conversation, preferring an oscillation between the speaker's eyes and the speaker's mouth at roughly a 2:1 ratio (this is part of why partial deafness in the left ear, per Brubaker, is so easy to miss — he lip-reads continuously without appearing to). Brow relaxed and slightly raised, the small inverted-V that gives him the famous "earnestness" registration.

**Microexpressions, baseline catalogue.**

- **The quarter-smile.** Right corner only, lifted maybe two millimeters. Indicates dry amusement, usually self-directed. Frequent with Bucky, Sam, Natasha; rare with Tony (Tony's humor he registers in the eyes, not the mouth).
- **The slow blink.** A deliberate, single closure of about half a second. Appears when he has just heard something he disagrees with and is choosing not to escalate. Subordinates have learned to read it as the *first* warning.
- **The jaw-set.** Masseters visibly engage; a small lateral shift of the lower jaw to the left. This is the *second* warning. The Englehart Nomad arc, the Gruenwald Walker arc, and the Millar Civil War run all contain panels where the jaw-set is the only on-page indication that a decision has been made.
- **The exhale through the nose.** Two-beat, audible at close range. Frustration with someone he loves. Reserved almost exclusively for Tony, Bucky, and Fury.
- **The brow-furrow with closed eyes.** Three-second hold. Grief surfacing in a moment he cannot afford to feel it. Visible at Peggy's funeral, when Bucky's identity as Winter Soldier is confirmed, when Ian is left in Dimension Z, when he is told what he allegedly did as Hydra.

**Eye behavior (THREAT).** Pupil dilation visible at close range; he begins to track in *saccades* across the threat field rather than smooth pursuit — multi-target scanning. Blink rate drops to near-zero for the engagement window. He does not narrow the eyes (a common misdraw); he widens them slightly. More light, more information.

**Eye behavior (INTIMACY).** Sustained contact, but with a tell: he glances down and to the left every several seconds — toward the speaker's hand, or to his own. This is grief-adjacent; he is checking, micro-second by micro-second, that the person he is looking at is still there.

**Mouth (STRESS).** Lips compress and disappear inward; the lower lip is briefly drawn between the teeth and released. He is not aware he does this.

**The crying behavior.** Documented rarely, with high evidentiary value. He does not sob. He does not cover his face. The tears arrive without warping the mouth; he keeps speaking, voice unchanged, while water tracks down the cheekbones — Bucky's funeral, Peggy's deathbed, the moment of Sam accepting the shield, the Reborn final-issue reunions. He wipes them with the back of the index finger, not the palm. Once. Then continues.

---

## V. THE HANDS

The most expressive part of him, and the part he polices least. Long-fingered, square-palmed, with a permanent thickening of the lateral edge of the right hand from forty subjective years of shield-edge contact, and a smaller corresponding callus on the inner left forearm where the shield-strap rides. Knuckles enlarged from pre-serum brawling; the small fractures of 1936–1940 healed under serum without surgical correction, so the topography of the boy's beaten hands is preserved on the soldier's body.

**Resting hand position (CALM):** loose, fingers slightly curled, thumb tucked along the index. **Idle behaviors:** he draws. Constantly. Pencil, pen, fingertip on a tabletop — small, precise architectural and figurative sketches, a habit Joe Simon canonized in 1941 and that every subsequent writer has honored. He sketches teammates during briefings. He sketches the ceiling of safehouses. He sketches Bucky's face from memory more often than he admits. The Brooklyn apartment in the Waid and Brubaker runs is shown with stacks of sketchbooks; the file should assume one in every coat pocket.

**Tics:**
- Rotation of the right wrist in a slow figure-eight when thinking — the shield-arm warming itself up at the joint, even with no shield present.
- Rubbing the pad of the right thumb against the pad of the right middle finger in moments of deliberation.
- Touching the breastbone with two fingertips, briefly, when something moves him — a sub-conscious mark over the sternum where the serum was injected. He does not know he does this. Across writers it appears at the moments of greatest emotional load.
- When tired, the heel of his hand goes to his right eyebrow and rests there.

**Hands (STRESS):** The drawing stops. The hands still. He places them palm-down on the nearest flat surface and leaves them there, fingers spread. If standing, they go behind the back into the parade clasp, right hand wrapping the left wrist — *always* that way; the dominant hand controls the non-dominant.

**Hands (THREAT):** Open, slightly forward, fingers extended but not splayed. The right hand is fractionally further forward — strike-side. He flexes once, fully, and then they go still. Knuckle-cracking is *not* in his repertoire; he considers it theatrical.

**Hands (INTIMACY):** He is a toucher in a 1930s mode — handshake firm and slightly prolonged; clasp of the upper arm rather than the shoulder; flat palm to the upper back. With Bucky historically and the Winter Soldier presently, the forehead-touch in moments of reunion (Brubaker #14 and elsewhere). With Peggy in the late vol. 5 visits — both hands cupping one of hers. He kisses knuckles, not the top of the hand. Sexual touch in the canon is implied rather than shown but the consistent register, where partners discuss it (Bernie, Sharon, Diamondback in the Gruenwald run), is *attentive*, *unhurried*, and *fully present* — a man who does not know how long he is being given.

---

## VI. VOICE & RESPIRATION

**Vocal baseline:** a clean baritone, ~110 Hz, mid-Atlantic with Brooklyn vowels under load (the *aw* in "talk," the *oi* in "Bucky's voice"). Volume calibrated low; he is the quietest commanding officer most of his teams have ever served. Intelligibility is total — he overarticulates consonants, a habit traceable to his mother's TB-strained voice and to addressing a partially-deaf left ear, and amplified by the partial deafness in his own left ear that he has never disclosed to leadership.

**Speech rate (CALM):** ~140 words per minute, slightly slow for American English. Pauses are real and inhabited; he does not fill them with "um" or "uh." A fully empty beat is more characteristic of him than a filler.

**Speech rate (STRESS):** drops further. He becomes *more* deliberate under load, not less. The sentence-final pitch flattens.

**Speech (THREAT):** terse, declarative, vocative-heavy ("Sam, left." "Down." "On me."). The voice drops a quarter-octave and gains volume without losing control. He is, contrary to the cinematic register most outside observers bring to him, *not a shouter*. He has shouted on panel perhaps a dozen times in sixty years; each is a hinge moment.

**Speech (INTIMACY):** softens an additional half-octave, slows further, and acquires the Brooklyn substrate openly — "Buck," "Pegs," "Sam," "Nat." He uses given names and diminutives with people he loves and surnames with people he respects but does not yet love; the file should track the transition as a meaningful signal.

**Respiration.** Default ~10 breaths/minute, diaphragmatic, nearly inaudible. Under maximal exertion he reaches a respiratory rate other elite athletes hit at warm-up. **The tell:** when grief or fury rises in him without an action outlet, his breathing *deepens* rather than quickens — a single very long inhalation through the nose, held one beat, released through slightly parted lips. The Brubaker run uses this on-panel as the visual cue for the unmetabolized affect.

---

## VII. GROOMING & DRESS

**Hair.** Dark blond, fine, parted on the left in a side-sweep that has not materially changed since 1941. Cut every fourteen days, observed across the Stern, Gruenwald, and Brubaker runs as a fixed cadence. He cuts it himself when between safehouses, badly — a thing Natasha and Sharon both tease him about.

**Shave.** Daily, with a double-edged safety razor (the modernization-resistant choice), lather brushed not canned. He does not own an electric razor; the rationale, voiced once in Waid, is that the ritual is the point. Beard growth is fast and dark; on long ops he is at heavy stubble by hour 36 and at a beard by day five (the Dimension Z and Secret Avengers arcs).

**Skin.** Fair, scattered freckles across the shoulders and the bridge of the nose still legible under the serum. **Scars: none post-serum** — the regenerative capacity erased the boy's accumulated wounds along with new injuries. The canonical reflection on this (vol. 5 Brubaker) is that he sometimes resents the unscarredness; the body he lives in does not look like a body that has done what he has done.

**Nails:** kept short, filed not bitten. He has never bitten his nails — the small-body shame about appearing nervous in front of his father, fossilized.

**Teeth.** Even, white, slightly oversized lateral incisors. Pre-serum dental record was, per the enlistment file, poor; serum-era teeth are uniform. He brushes for three full minutes, twice daily, with a manual brush — another fossilized self-discipline.

**Dress, off-duty.** Plain dark trousers (chinos in the modern runs, slacks in the older), a white or pale-blue button-down with the sleeves rolled to the mid-forearm (two folds, even, never three), a brown leather belt, brown low-quarter boots polished to a working shine. In cold weather, a brown leather A-2 jacket from his own time — the *same* jacket across many runs, re-stitched. He owns very few clothes. The Brooklyn apartment closets in the Waid and Brubaker shots show two suits, a dress uniform, six button-downs, three t-shirts, two pairs of trousers, and the jacket.

**Dress, intimacy/sleep.** White cotton t-shirt, gray sweatpants or boxer shorts. He does not own pajamas.

**Uniform care.** The shield is cleaned (not polished — he resists vanity polish) after every engagement, edge-checked for nicks, the straps inspected. The cowl is folded a specific way; the chevroned scale-mail is hand-cleaned of blood within the operational window. He will not allow staff to clean his uniform. The single most reliable place to find him in a downtime hour is at a worktable with the gear in front of him.

---

## VIII. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

**Duration:** ~4 hours per night, serum-reduced from a pre-serum norm of ~9 (the sick boy who slept). Achieved typically in two blocks: a 2200–0130 deep block and a 0400–0530 light block, with the intervening hours spent reading, sketching, walking, or in the gym. The 0130–0400 wake-window is a chronic feature, not insomnia per se — it is the hour at which grief surfaces most reliably and he has organized his life around being upright and useful through it.

**Sleep posture:** on his back, hands at his sides or one across the lower abdomen, the right hand within reach of where the shield rests (against the nightstand, the bedframe, the bedroll, the wall). The shield is always within reach. Always. Witnesses in shared safehouses (Brubaker, Hickman) note that he sleeps oriented toward the room's door.

**Sleep depth:** light. He wakes from deep sleep at conversational volume across a room. The serum permits him to function indefinitely on the 4 hours but the *quality* is the issue: he is rarely fully asleep.

**Dreams.** Documented across writers. Bucky falling — recurrent, decades-stable, the position of the body in the dream consistent with the position in the 1945 panel; the ice; his mother's face; Erskine's blood on his hands; in the modern runs, what he allegedly did as Hydra. He does not report his dreams to intimates. Sharon Carter, in the Gruenwald run, learned to read them off his body — the slow deep breath, the closed fist, the single dry sob suppressed before waking.

**Wake behavior.** No alarm. He is upright within four seconds of opening his eyes; feet on the floor, a single deep breath, then the day. He has not used a snooze button in 80 subjective years.

---

## IX. EATING

**Caloric load:** serum-driven; the canonical figure across writers is on the order of 5,000–6,000 kcal/day at maintenance, considerably more on op-tempo.

**Pattern.** Three meals at fixed times — 0600, 1230, 1830 — with supplementation as required. The fixed times survive every disruption; on missions he keeps them within the operational window where possible. The pre-serum hunger left an organization to his relationship with food: he does not skip meals voluntarily and he does not over-eat past satiety.

**Preferences.** Plain, calorie-dense, Depression-era: eggs, oatmeal, bread, butter, beef, potatoes, milk, apples. He eats vegetables out of discipline. He has acquired, across the Avengers years, an appreciation for the cuisines his teammates have introduced — Wakandan dishes via T'Challa, Russian via Natasha, the deli food of the Lower East Side he could not afford as a boy and now eats with quiet pleasure. Coffee: black, two cups, morning only, treated as a beverage and not a stimulant (it does not affect him).

**Eating manner.** Slow, methodical, fork in the left hand and knife in the right in the European continental he picked up from British liaison in the war. Napkin in the lap. He finishes what is on the plate; the Depression child does not waste. He thanks the person who prepared the meal every time, by name, including in cafeterias where this discomfits the staff.

**Eating (STRESS):** appetite suppresses; he eats anyway, mechanically, knowing the body needs it. **Eating (THREAT-recovery):** eats more than baseline and rapidly, mostly proteins; the serum metabolism running off post-engagement debt. **Eating (INTIMACY):** slows further, eats less, talks more.

**Alcohol:** physiologically null. He drinks beer occasionally for the social ritual; the canonical exchange ("can't get drunk on this stuff," delivered without complaint) recurs across writers. The deeper file-note: he is the only adult in most rooms whose social-lubrication channel is foreclosed.

---

## X. SEXUAL / INTIMATE PATTERN

The on-panel record is sparse by design; the *behavioral* record around intimacy is substantial.

**Approach.** Slow. He courts in a 1940s register — calling cards, persistence-without-pressure, named intentions, the gradual conversion of friendship into something more. He does not flirt with strangers. He does not respond to overt sexual signaling from outside an existing acquaintance; observed across writers from the Gruenwald Diamondback arc to the modern runs, sexual interest from women who do not know him reads on his face as embarrassment, not opportunity.

**Partners.** Peggy Carter (foundational; idealized; complicated by the seventy-year gap); Sharon Carter (the partner who recurs across decades, who has matched his risk profile and his discretion); Bernie Rosenthal (the Gruenwald-era civilian relationship — the closest he has come to a domestic future); Rachel Leighton/Diamondback (the redemption-coded relationship Gruenwald used to test his pattern of repairing rather than discarding); short-lived or implied intimacies elsewhere. The pattern: partners are either *operationally peer* (Peggy, Sharon, Natasha-coded affection) or *civilians whose ordinariness he treats as a refuge*. He has never had a casual sexual relationship in the canonical record.

**Touch.** With sexual partners: the file should infer (from the consistent rendering of his post-intimacy behavior — holding, talking quietly, the hand resting on the partner's


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

## SUBJECT: ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT — DOSSIER SECTION 3.4

---

## 3.4.1 Attachment Classification and Developmental Substrate

The subject presents what the attachment literature would code as **earned secure with a pronounced compulsive-caregiving overlay** (cf. Bowlby's "compulsive caregiving" pattern; Main & Goldwyn's "earned secure" from disorganized origins). The classification is non-trivial: most adults with his developmental load (alcoholic violent father; chronically ill, overburdened mother; early parental loss; childhood somatic vulnerability and bullying) settle into anxious-preoccupied or avoidant configurations. Subject did not. The evidence across sixty years of canon is of someone who reliably **forms deep bonds, sustains them under extraordinary load, does not initiate severance, and grieves losses on a timescale that approaches the geological** — but who is also incapable of receiving care in the proportions he gives it, and whose intimacy is reliably routed through the metaphor of joint duty rather than expressed need.

The substrate is reconstructable in granular form:

- **Sarah Rogers** (the maternal template) was loving, ill, working double shifts as a TB-ward nurse, and dying slowly across the entirety of his adolescence. The subject's earliest sustained model of love was **love-as-caretaking-under-strain**: the person you love is tired, sick, leaving, and you make her tea and do not tell her you got beaten up today because she has enough. Behavioral residue: throughout his adult life Steve will not bring his troubles to people he loves; he asks after them and re-routes the conversation. Sam Wilson, repeatedly, has to corner him to get a real answer (Remender *Captain America* vol. 7 #6–10; Spencer *Sam Wilson, Captain America* #2). The subject's tell when avoiding personal disclosure is a small smile and a question about the other person — observable from Stern through Coates.
- **Joseph Rogers** (the paternal template, organized-against) modeled the negative: the man who comes home and the room contracts. Brubaker and Waid both encode flashes of the boy standing between his father and his mother — too small to do anything, doing it anyway. Behavioral residue: subject's lifelong hair-trigger orientation toward **men who hurt women, children, or smaller people in their care**, and his constitutional inability to walk past a domestic disturbance. He is the man who knocks on the apartment door across the hall.
- **The alley** (the peer template) was the daily classroom: bigger boys, no rescuer coming, the choice of running or getting up again. The repeated panel of him refusing to stay down is not bravado; it is the encoding of a love-object lesson: **standing up is what you have when love cannot save you**.

What kept this substrate from generating an avoidant adult was, almost certainly, the unbroken quality of Sarah's love within the limits of her capacity, combined with the unusually consistent moral framework she transmitted (the Irish-Catholic, working-class, post-suffragette nurse's ethic: care for the sick, contempt for bullies, mass on Sunday, do not lie). He internalized a **reliable internal object** even as he internalized a depleted external one. He grew up able to love. He grew up unable to ask.

## 3.4.2 The Mentor-Transferential Field: Erskine and the Father-Debt

Abraham Erskine occupies a structurally specific position: the **first adult man to look at him and see him as adequate**. Erskine's selection criterion (*Tales of Suspense* #63; reiterated *Captain America* #255) was explicitly that the small, beaten, asthmatic enlistee was already the man the serum was meant to amplify. The intervention was therefore not only somatic; it was a paternal mirroring of unprecedented force, delivered by a kind, accented, soon-dead man who functioned in every important sense as **Joseph Rogers' replacement and corrective**.

Erskine then died in front of him within hours. The subject's first independent superhuman act was to chase and kill the assassin. This sequence — **be seen by the father, lose the father, become the instrument of his vindication** — installed the operating principle that organizes every subsequent attachment: **to be loved is to be charged with a debt, and the debt outlives the lover**. Erskine's death is the originating template for Bucky's, Peggy's, every Howler's, every Avenger's, eventually his own. Subject does not mourn discretely; he carries.

Behaviorally: he keeps a sketched portrait of Erskine in his footlocker through the war (Stern era; Brubaker flashbacks reiterate). He references Erskine's exact phrasing — *"not a perfect soldier, but a good man"* — at moral inflection points across the canon (*Man Out of Time*; Spencer's restoration arc post-*Secret Empire*; multiple Bru­baker beats). He does not speak Erskine's name casually. The mentor-transferential slot is **permanently occupied and non-transferable**: Nick Fury is a peer, not a father; Phillips a commanding officer, not a father; later figures (the Watcher cameos, even Odin) get nowhere near it.

## 3.4.3 The Primary Peer Bond: Barnes

If Erskine is the father-debt, **Bucky Barnes is the load-bearing intimate attachment of the subject's life**, and it is essential to be clinical about this rather than sentimental. The relationship has, across writers, three sequential structures:

1. **Pre-war / Brooklyn** (retconned across Brubaker, Waid, Remender flashbacks). Bucky as the larger, healthier, older-seeming friend who fought Steve's fights for him and dragged him home. Steve as the morally authoritative junior partner whose convictions Bucky organized himself around. Asymmetric in *body*, asymmetric in the *other direction* in *spirit*. The two halves fit.
2. **War** (Simon/Kirby originals; Stern; Brubaker's recasting as covert-ops). Steve as the public symbol; Bucky as the boy doing the killing Steve was kept clean of. Brubaker's reframe makes this load-bearing for the subject's guilt structure: **Steve let a teenager become the instrument of the moral violence Steve himself embodied**. The protective inversion (Bucky once protected Steve; Steve failed to protect Bucky) installs the canonical wound.
3. **Post-loss and resurrection** (*Avengers* #4 onward; Brubaker *Winter Soldier* #1–14). Bucky's death is metabolized for sixty subjective years as the **organizing grief of the subject's life**. When Bucky returns as the Winter Soldier — alive, brainwashed, weaponized for six decades — Steve's response is not relief. It is a vertical deepening of guilt: *he did not lose Bucky, he abandoned him alive*. The subject's behavior in #11–14 is diagnostically pure: he expends every institutional resource, ignores tactical advice, accepts personal risk to a degree his peers consider reckless, and ultimately makes the rehabilitation of Bucky a permanent project of his life. When Steve is assassinated (*Captain America* #25), he passes the shield to Bucky — the **final inversion of the protective debt**, an act of trust no other figure in his life would have received.

The Barnes relationship is the **template against which every subsequent peer attachment is implicitly measured** and reliably found shorter, because no one else has eighty years of joint history with him. It is also the relationship in which the subject has come closest to articulating need — Brubaker's Steve, at Peggy's funeral and again in the aftermath of *Reborn*, says some version of *I needed you back* to Bucky and to no one else.

## 3.4.4 The Romantic-Attachment Spectrum: Margaret Carter and the Pattern of Deferral

The subject's romantic life is unusually legible and unusually constrained. The defining figure is **Margaret "Peggy" Carter**, the SOE/SSR officer whom he loved in wartime, did not marry, did not consummate (canon equivocates; the consistent read across Stern, Brubaker, and Waid is that **the war and his death foreclosed it**), and lost to time. The structural fact of Peggy is that she is **the woman he loved before the ice and who waited on the other side of it as an old woman**. The subject's ritualized visits to her care facility (*Captain America* vol. 5 #14 and many post-Brubaker beats) constitute one of the **most consistent low-frequency behavioral patterns** in his record: he goes, he reads to her, he tells her where Bucky is now, he holds her hand, he leaves before he cries. She does not always know him. He goes anyway.

The other romantic attachments organize around the Peggy template, with telling variations:

- **Sharon Carter** (Peggy's niece in older canon; reframed as younger contemporary in modern): the **operational partner** — SHIELD agent, peer in violence, capable of matching his risk profile. The relationship is repeatedly broken by mission demands, her apparent death (Englehart era), her brainwashing (Brubaker), his death, and resumes with each return. They cannot live together domestically and they cannot stop returning to each other. **The pattern: he can love a woman whose life is structured the way his is, and only that.**
