- **Bernadette Rosenthal** (Bernie; DeMatteis/Gruenwald era): the **civilian experiment** — a glassblower, a normal life, the closest he has come to choosing the apartment-and-dinner template. She left for law school; he did not follow. He is, on the record, capable of love with a civilian and structurally incapable of accepting the contraction of his life it would require. Note he did not stop her from going and did not ask her to stay. **The deferral is automatic.**
- **Rachel Leighton (Diamondback;** Gruenwald): the **redemption-coded attachment** — a former villain who reorganized her life around him. He treated her with a strikingly equal regard given the asymmetry; the relationship dissolved without rupture. Pattern consistent: **partners leave or are taken; he does not initiate severance.**
- **Natasha Romanoff** (across multiple runs, most operative in modern continuity and the Brubaker era): not consummated in main continuity but encoded as the **closest peer-of-arms intimacy of his late life**. The relationship has the structure of Bucky-with-romantic-charge: shared trade, mutual fluency in violence, mutual unspoken understanding of the cost of it. He grieves her as a comrade and as something more — flat-affect, encysted, in the briefing-room register.

The romantic pattern across the entire arc: **he loves women who can survive his life, and the price of being lovable to him is that you must be willing to be left alone for indefinite intervals, accept that he will return injured, and not require him to soften the surface that protects him from the grief beneath**. The women who could meet those conditions (Peggy, Sharon, Natasha) are the ones the bond lasted with. The women who could not (Bernie, Rachel) he loved and let go without protest, which is its own diagnostic: **he does not fight for romantic continuity, because he believes the cost of being with him is unfair, and he will not impose it**.

## 3.4.5 Surrogate Family: The Unit as Attachment Object

Downstream of early loss, the subject reliably **binds to the unit as a family object**: 107th and the Howlers in the war; the Invaders; the Avengers across every era; the Secret Avengers; the post-*Civil War* underground; the Unity Squad. The pattern is not generic team-loyalty; it is **a specific attachment configuration in which the team is the household and his role is the parent who does not sleep**.

Granular markers:

- He learns names — every name, including support staff, mansion personnel, Quinjet mechanics, SHIELD analysts. He uses them. (Observable from Stern through Hickman.)
- He is the last one out of the field after a fight, doing welfare checks. (Gruenwald, Brubaker, Aaron.)
- He maintains a running mental inventory of who is struggling and intervenes obliquely (a sparring offer, a coffee, a shared patrol) rather than directly. He does not say *are you okay*; he creates a situation in which the other person can say it if they want to.
- He attends the funerals. All of them. He gives the eulogies he is asked to give and does not give the ones he is not. He stays for the reception. He drives people home.
- He keeps the team's secrets, including from himself when knowing would compromise his command obligation. (Hickman *Avengers* / *New Avengers*: the Illuminati's mind-wipe is metabolized as personal betrayal because it punctured exactly this trust structure.)

The **Tony Stark** relationship is the most analytically rich peer attachment outside Bucky. It has the form of an **opposites-coded brotherhood**: temperamental opposites, ethical opposites in many particulars, but bound by mutual recognition of the other's seriousness. The pre-*Civil War* Stark/Rogers attachment is, across Michelinie, Stern, Busiek, and early Bendis, **functionally fraternal** — they argue, they reconcile, they cover for each other, they trust each other with the team. *Civil War* (Millar) ruptured this and the rupture was operative across the entire post-2006 line. The diagnostically important fact: **Steve did not initiate the break.** He resisted the legislation; Tony chose the enforcement role. Steve's surrender on the courthouse steps is, among other things, an attempt to stop the cost of a fight he never wanted with a brother he could not strike at without injury to himself.

## 3.4.6 The Mentee Pattern: Custody of the Successor

The subject's relationship to **successors and mentees** is one of the most stable behavioral patterns in the file, and the **single most diagnostic of the underlying psychology**. He does not produce disciples; he produces inheritors. Listing matters:

- **Bucky** (war and post-resurrection): the original mentee; eventually shield-bearer.
- **Rick Jones** (Lee/Kirby and after): the Bucky-replacement attempt; explicitly aborted by the subject when he realized he was using the boy to recover a dead one. (Diagnostically: he is **capable of catching himself** in a transferential repetition and stopping.)
- **Sam Wilson** (Falcon, from Englehart's *Captain America and the Falcon* onward; eventually shield-bearer in Remender/Spencer): the deepest sustained peer-mentee relationship of his late career; over decades it inverts from mentor/mentee to **mutual partnership** to **succession**. He hands Sam the shield voluntarily and without ceremony. He defends Sam's tenure against the country's racism. (Coates and Spencer both make this load-bearing.)
- **John Walker** (Gruenwald #332–350): the **failed successor he refused to discard**. Walker committed the atrocities Steve fears latent in the iconography itself; Steve took him back, trained him, gave him the U.S. Agent identity. Diagnostically: **Steve repairs rather than discards broken inheritors**, because to discard them would replicate the abandonment he most fears having done to Bucky.
- **Ian Rogers** (Remender, *Dimension Z*): an adopted son raised across years of subjective time; largely written out on return. Steve's grief over Ian's effective loss is encoded in low affect and high suppression — recognizable.
- **Various adjacent figures** (Kate Bishop in some configurations, Miles Morales in cameos, the post-*Generations* younger heroes): treated with the same patient regard. He is the elder who shows up to the new heroes' birthdays.

The unifying mechanism: **he experiences each mentee as a re-issued chance to do what he could not do for Bucky**, and the pattern of patience, forgiveness, and standing-aside is the **enacted form of his survivor guilt sublimated into pedagogy**.

## 3.4.7 Bonding Mechanics: How He Forms Attachment

The subject does not form attachment through disclosure. He forms it through **co-presence under load**. The reliable sequence:

1. **Observation period.** He watches. He learns how the other person fights, eats, jokes, handles fear, treats subordinates. He is not socially anxious in this period; he is **assessing whether trust is structurally possible**.
2. **Small offered competence.** He demonstrates trustworthiness by doing the small thing well — covering a flank, remembering a preference, taking the bad watch.
3. **Shared mission.** A first joint piece of work, after which the relationship is functionally established for him whether or not it has been articulated.
4. **Slow disclosure, asymmetric.** He learns the other person; the other person learns less of him, by his design. Disclosure on his side tends to surface obliquely — a Brooklyn reference, a remark about his mother, a sketch left on a table — rather than via direct biographical narration.
5. **Loyalty installation.** Once the bond is established, it is **structurally permanent on his side**. He does not revisit the question.

Conversely, when bonding **fails to take** (rare; observable with figures like Henry Gyrich, certain SHIELD bureaucrats, the Commission, hostile Presidents), the failure point is almost always at step 1: he observes treatment of subordinates or the vulnerable and **silently disqualifies the person from candidacy**. Once disqualified, the person is treated with formal courtesy and zero intimate access for the duration of the relationship.

## 3.4.8 Distrust, Betrayal, and the Withdrawal of Legitimacy

The subject's **distrust mechanism is moral, not paranoid**. He does not assume hostile intent; he updates on demonstrated behavior, sometimes more slowly than tactically prudent (Zemo and the Red Skull have both exploited this; Spencer's *Secret Empire* setup turned on it). When trust is broken, however, his response has a characteristic shape that should be modeled explicitly:

- **No outburst.** The break is registered quietly. Observers often miss the moment it happened.
- **Formal continuation of duty.** He will continue to work alongside a betrayer if the mission requires it, with no marker of changed regard visible to outsiders.
- **Permanent reclassification.** The person is moved, internally, from the *trusted-intimate* category to the *peer-not-trusted* or *opponent* category. **Reclassification is exceptionally difficult to reverse.** Tony Stark, after *Civil War*, was years in being moved back toward the *peer-not-trusted* slot and was never returned to the prior *intimate* status before Tony's subsequent death. Sharon, after various Brubaker-era brainwashings, was returned because the betrayal was demonstrably not hers.
- **Withdrawal of legitimacy from institutions.** When the betrayer is institutional (the Nixon-analog Secret Empire, *Captain America* #175; the Commission, Gruenwald #332; the Registration regime, *Civil War*; later iterations under Coates), the subject's response is to **withdraw his name and his face from the institution and to embody the principle the institution claimed to embody, in his own person, in opposition to it**. This is the Nomad pattern, the Captain pattern, the *Civil War* insurgency pattern. The recurrence is striking: the same defense, four times, across four decades.

It is critical to note that **the subject is not vengeful**. He does not pursue betrayers; he removes them from his sphere. He will fight them if they continue to do harm; he will not seek them out to settle scores. Even his pursuit of the Red Skull is operationally motivated, not personally avenging.

## 3.4.9 Repair: The Conditions and Mechanics

The subject is **unusually capable of repair** for someone with his loss history. The conditions for repair are stable across the canon:

1. **Demonstrated, sustained behavioral change.** Not apology; behavior. Walker's repair was earned by years of work as U.S. Agent. Bucky's was structural (he was not responsible for the Winter Soldier programming) and behavioral (he atoned actively).
2. **Direct articulation of what was done and acknowledgment of harm.** Steve does not require humiliation; he requires that the person see the wound clearly.
3. **No second betrayal.** A repaired relationship that breaks twice does not get a third repair. Observable in his handling of certain SHIELD figures and at least one Avengers reservist.

When these conditions are met, **his capacity for forgiveness is extraordinary** — including for harms done to him personally that he would not forgive on others' behalf. (He is more lenient with people who hurt him than with people who hurt those he protects. This is itself diagnostic: his anger is mobilized for others, not for himself.)

The mechanism of repair on his side is **the resumption of small co-presence**: he begins assigning the person to joint missions, asks their opinion, eats with them in the mess. The verbal acknowledgment of repair is minimal; the behavioral resumption is the signal.

## 3.4.10 Intimacy and Dependency: The Asymmetry

The defining asymmetry of every intimate relationship in his life:

- He **gives** care, attention, protection, mentorship, time, his body, his name, and his life.
- He **accepts** very little of any of these in return, and when offered them, redirects.

This is not false modesty; it is a **structural inability to occupy the cared-for position**. Granular evidence:

- He goes to medical only when ordered, and then minimizes symptoms.
- He does not take leave even when granted it; he uses it to do solo work (riding cross-country, sketching, visiting Peggy).
- When wounded, he refuses help walking off the field for as long as physiologically possible.
- When grieving, he isolates rather than seeking comfort.
- When complimented, he redirects credit to the team.
- When given gifts, he is visibly uncomfortable and uses them quickly and quietly to mark gratitude through use rather than display.
- When Sam, Bucky, Natasha, or Sharon attempts to provide emotional support, the characteristic response is a small smile, a thank-you, and a change of subject — sometimes after a beat in which something almost surfaces.

The asymmetry is **not** because he does not feel the need. The Streets of Poison arc, the post-*Reborn* beats, the Coates-era confessional sequences, and the rare Brubaker scenes in which he speaks honestly to Bucky after the funeral all demonstrate that **the capacity for receiving is intact; the permission is not**. He believes, with a stubbornness that no one in his life has succeeded in dislodging, that **his needs are luxuries; his job is to absorb costs others should not have to bear; and to accept care in proportion to what he gives would be theft from people who need it more**.

This belief is the **load-bearing distortion** of his attachment system. It is the price of being earned-secure from his particular substrate. It is also the reason no relationship in his life — including Bucky, including Peggy — has ever been fully reciprocal.

## 3.4.11 The Template, Stated Plainly

Across every relationship of the subject's life — parental, paternal-transferential, peer, romantic, fraternal, mentorial, institutional — the same template repeats:

> **I will see you fully, learn you carefully, love you durably, protect you at cost to myself, mentor you toward your own sufficiency, forgive you what can be forgiven, mourn you when you go, carry the debt of you forever, and never, in any of this, allow you to see how much I am holding or ask you to hold any of it for me.**

Every figure in the relational map — Sarah, Joseph (


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

## SUBJECT: ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT — Defensive Architecture, Full Mapping

The defensive system in this subject is unusually well-developed, unusually high-functioning, and — critically — unusually *integrated with vocation*, which is what makes it both load-bearing and hard to dismantle. What in another subject would present as symptomatic surfaces here as virtue, productivity, or charisma. The work of this section is to disaggregate the architecture: to show what each mechanism is, where in the canonical record it is observable, what affect it is managing, what it costs him, and at what stress threshold it begins to fail.

The ordering below moves from most mature (and most behaviorally dominant) to most primitive (and rarely visible). It is important that the primitive end of the stack exists; almost every catastrophic Rogers episode in the canon is the moment a usually-mature defense fails downward into something cruder.

---

## I. THE MATURE TIER (His Operational Default)

### 1. Sublimation — the master defense

This is the architectural keystone. Nearly every aggressive, grieving, terrified, or longing impulse the subject generates is rerouted into protective action. The serum and the uniform are, in defensive terms, a permanent industrial-scale sublimation engine: rage at his father becomes rage at fascism; helplessness at his mother's bedside becomes the recurring tableau of him standing between civilians and ordnance; grief for Bucky becomes the *Winter Soldier* rescue arc; survivor guilt for the cohort becomes the willingness to die on the Civil War courthouse steps for the principle a cohort once died for.

Behavioral signatures:

- **Affect-to-task conversion latency is short.** Across writers (notably Brubaker and Waid), when Rogers receives bad news his observable response is a beat of silence, a hand on a surface, then a question about logistics. The grief is not absent; it has been routed.
- **Off-duty time is poorly tolerated.** Long stretches without operational role (the Englehart Nomad arc, the de-serumed convalescence in Spencer, recovery beats in Brubaker) show him restless, sketching obsessively, training to exhaustion, organizing other people's problems.
- **Choice of partners and friends loads the engine.** Peggy, Sharon, Natasha, Bucky, Sam — all combat-adjacent. The intimate sphere is not a place he rests; it is another front on which he can be protective.

Cost: sublimation works only as long as the work is available. Forced inactivity (captivity, Registration-era house arrest, the de-serumed period) produces rapid emergence of the affect the engine was metabolizing — depressive cognition, grief intrusions, irritability he is unaccustomed to managing.

### 2. Altruism (defensive)

Distinct from ordinary other-regarding behavior. In Rogers it is *defensive* in the technical sense: he meets his own needs vicariously through the meeting of others'. Mentorship of Rick Jones, of Bucky originally, of Sam, of Walker after the betrayal, of Ian in *Dimension Z*, of Miles, of Kate in some configurations — each is a context in which he can give the care, protection, instruction, and patience he was structurally denied as the sick child of an overworked nurse and an alcoholic veteran.

The diagnostic tell that this is defensive rather than merely virtuous is the **asymmetry of receipt**. He is fluent in giving and inarticulate in receiving. When Sam, Natasha, or Bucky attempt to reverse the direction — to check on him, to ask what he needs — the canon shows him deflecting with humor, redirecting to operational matters, or producing a flat, slightly formal *I'm fine* (Brubaker, repeated; Waid *Man Out of Time*). The defense breaks if the giving stops.

### 3. Suppression

Conscious, deliberate deferral of affect to an operationally appropriate moment. This is a *mature* defense in Vaillant's taxonomy because it is volitional and time-limited. In Rogers it is well-trained, immediate, and almost frictionless — and it is also chronically *unfinished*, because the operationally appropriate moment to grieve Bucky, Peggy, Erskine, Sarah, the cohort, the century, Ian, and his own assassinated self never quite arrives.

Behavioral markers: the briefing-room register in which he reports devastating losses (his recounting of Bucky's death in *Avengers* #56; his account of Peggy's death in *Captain America* vol. 5 #14); the precise interval between mission end and visible decompression, which is calibrated to whether subordinates are still in the room. He decompresses alone or not at all.

The hazard of suppression-as-style is that suppressed material accumulates. The Reborn arc — being forced to re-witness every formative loss in sequence — is best read as the canon literalizing what his interior would look like if the deferral queue were ever opened.

### 4. Humor (mature, dry, self-directed)

Underrecognized in popular reception. Across Waid, Brubaker, and the Hickman *Avengers* run, the subject's humor is consistent: dry, understated, often at his own expense, usually deployed to lower the temperature of a room or to give a frightened subordinate a beat of normalcy. The *I understood that reference* register is mocked by the modern audience as earnest but in canonical context functions as social lubricant under conditions of profound dislocation — a man choosing to be charmingly out of step rather than tragically so.

Humor is also the channel through which he discloses pain when direct disclosure is unavailable: jokes about not being able to get drunk (*Captain America Annual* #4), about the music, about the prices, about his own age. Each is a small leak from the dislocation reservoir.

### 5. Anticipation

He plans for losses in advance and rehearses them. He has discussed succession in essentially every era — Bucky was groomed, Sam was eventually chosen, Walker was retained as understudy. He writes letters. He keeps his affairs in order in a way the canon repeatedly references (Brubaker, post-Civil War). This is not morbid; it is anticipatory grief management, which reduces affective load at the actual loss event and is one of the reasons he can present so flatly when losses occur.

---

## II. THE NEUROTIC TIER (Visible Under Strain)

### 6. Reaction formation against helplessness

The most diagnostically important neurotic defense in the file. The subject's core wound is helplessness — the sick boy who could not stop his father, could not save his mother, could not finish the alley fights he started. The adult adaptation is the exact mirror image: he places himself, repeatedly and systemically, in the position of the one who acts, the one who stands between, the one who absorbs.

The defense is *reaction formation* rather than simple courage because of the **disproportionality** of the response to constraint. Any condition that forces him into helplessness — captivity, registration, lawful orders to stand down while harm proceeds, even being told to wait by a teammate — produces an affective intensity that exceeds the situation. Civil War is the canonical large-scale example; smaller examples recur in every long run (his behavior when Bucky is in SHIELD custody; his behavior when civilians are taken hostage and tactical doctrine requires patience). The intolerable affect is not fear of the outcome; it is the reactivation of the original helplessness.

### 7. Isolation of affect

The flat briefing-room register again, considered as a defense rather than a style. He can describe his own death, his mentor's assassination, his best friend's fall, and his lover's dementia in language that is informationally complete and affectively encysted. This is not alexithymia (he is not affect-blind; he reads others with high fidelity) and not numbing in the PTSD sense (the affect is present, palpable to attentive observers, walled rather than absent). It is the specific neurotic operation of separating the cognitive-narrative content of a memory from its emotional charge so the content can be discussed.

Behavioral test: the affect leaks at oblique cues — the sound of a particular song, the sight of a Dodgers cap, the smell of a hospital corridor — rather than at the direct discussion. Brubaker is particularly good on these displacements.

### 8. Intellectualization

Less prominent than in many high-functioning subjects, but present. Strategic-tactical reasoning is sometimes deployed where emotional reasoning would be appropriate — most visibly in the post-Civil War period, when his accounts of the conflict tend to organize around the principle at stake rather than the rupture with Tony Stark, which canon strongly suggests is the actual wound. Intellectualization is also visible in his handling of the Hydra-Steve revelation in *Secret Empire*'s aftermath: he frames his accountability in moral-philosophical rather than affective terms, which is functional but also self-protective.

### 9. Displacement (narrow, controlled)

Tactical anger displacement onto adversaries who can absorb it. He does not, characteristically, take internal frustration out on subordinates or intimates. He takes it out on the Red Skull, on Hydra, on the heavy bag, on the road during long solo motorcycle runs. The motorcycle itself functions as a controlled displacement object across decades of canon — the long ride is reliably how he metabolizes events he cannot otherwise process.

### 10. Identification (with Erskine; against Joseph Rogers)

A defining and chronic operation. The introjected Erskine — *the good man first* — functions as his superego content; the introjected and *counter-identified* Joseph Rogers functions as his behavioral negative space. Almost every adult choice he makes can be parsed as *what Erskine would have asked* or *what my father would have done, therefore not that*. The defense is structural and stable, which is why his identity survives the dislocations (ice, Dimension Z, Reborn, de-serumed, Hydra-Steve) without fragmentation: the introjects are intact.

### 11. Undoing (ritualized)

Visible in his maintenance rituals — the visits to Peggy, the visits to graves, the cleaning of the shield, the keeping of small objects from the cohort. These are not pathological undoing in the obsessional sense; they are quasi-religious commemorative acts that function defensively by converting irreversible loss into recurrent observance.

---

## III. THE IMMATURE TIER (Rare, Costly, Diagnostic When Visible)

### 12. Isolation (behavioral withdrawal)

Under high decompensation he goes quiet and then he goes alone. Post-Bucky (original loss), post-Civil War surrender, post-*Reborn*, post-*Secret Empire* — the pattern is consistent: solitude, often on the road, sometimes weeks. This is distinct from suppression (which is in-role) and from healthy retreat; it is a removal of himself from relational fields he can no longer regulate within.

### 13. Somatization (minor and atypical)

The serum prevents most physiological symptom expression, but the canon shows posture, sleep, and appetite changes during depressive episodes — he gets quieter in the body, sleeps less even than his baseline already-light pattern, trains harder. This is the residue of somatic distress in a body that cannot produce ordinary symptoms.

### 14. Counterphobic action

The pattern of running *toward* the source of fear rather than away. Diagnostically distinct from courage because the action is sometimes tactically suboptimal — he will go alone into a known trap, take point when the rotation does not call for it, place himself at the choke. The fear being managed is not fear of harm to himself (he has decades of evidence his body tolerates harm) but fear of *being the one who did not act in time*. The counterphobia is against a specific scenario: arriving late to the alley.

### 15. Moral absolutism (defense against moral injury)

When institutions he has lent his name to betray the principle, he does not negotiate the principle; he externalizes himself from the institution. Nomad, The Captain, Civil War insurgency. This is a defense because it spares him the much more painful operation of holding both the institution and the principle simultaneously and tolerating the contradiction. The cost is recurrent, very public rupture with bodies (the U.S. government, SHIELD, the Avengers in various configurations) that he might otherwise reform from within.

---

## IV. THE PRIMITIVE TIER (Visible Only Under Catastrophic Load)

These appear briefly, are quickly recompensated, and are diagnostic precisely because they are so out-of-pattern.

### 16. Splitting (transient)

Rarely visible. Most clearly during the Hydra-Steve restoration period and in the immediate aftermath of major betrayals, where his cognition about the betraying party can briefly polarize. He recovers integration quickly — usually within an arc — and characteristically returns to a complex view of the person (Tony, Sharon, Bucky-as-Winter-Soldier). The brevity of the split is itself diagnostic: the underlying structure is integrated.

### 17. Projective identification (rare, mostly toward successors)

Visible in his relationship with Walker, who *becomes* the latent fear Steve carries about what Captain America could be in the wrong hands. The defense places the disowned content (the brutal, nationalist, authoritarian version of the role) into another person, who then enacts it. Steve's subsequent retrieval and rehabilitation of Walker is the reparative phase of the same operation — he is taking back the projected content by helping its carrier integrate it.

### 18. Acting out (the Streets of Poison register)

When inhibition is chemically or supernaturally lifted (the *Streets of Poison* arc; mind-control episodes; the cosmic-cube-altered Hydra-Steve), the underlying aggressive material is unmodulated and brutal. This is the load his ordinary defenses are managing. His phobic-grade post-event avoidance of any intoxicant or mood-altering agent is best read as defense-of-defenses: he protects the inhibitory system because he has seen what is under it.

---

## V. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — POSITIVE

These are the structures and habits that *compensate for* the chronic deficits (grief, dislocation, foreclosed coping channels) rather than defend against specific affects.

- **Extraordinary work capacity.** The serum permits, and the psychology demands, a workload no human cohort can match. Work is the meaning-vehicle and the metabolic vehicle for affect.
- **Mentorship as generativity.** He compensates for outliving his cohort by populating the next. Across decades the mentorship list is unusually long and unusually successful (Bucky, Rick, Sam, Walker post-rehabilitation, Ian, Miles, Kate in some configurations). Each successful succession reduces the burden of being the last.
- **Surrogate-family architecture.** Howlers, Invaders, Avengers, the Secret Avengers, the modern Avengers — he has been continuously embedded in a unit since 1941. The unit is the structural compensation for the original family that did not protect him and the cohort he outlived.
- **Ritualized commemoration.** Visits to Peggy in care; the maintenance of small objects; the drawing (he sketches throughout the canon; Brubaker and Waid both use this); the motorcycle routes that pass meaningful sites. These keep the dead in active relation rather than buried.
- **Aesthetic and craft outlets.** Drawing in particular — a pre-war skill he retains and returns to in quiet hours. It is the only consistently depicted activity that is purely his, with no protective function.
- **Disciplined physical practice.** Training, calisthenics, sparring. These regulate arousal in a body that cannot use the standard pharmacological down-regulators.
- **Reading and study (catch-up).** He has spent the modern era visibly closing the cultural gap — files of music, films, books, history. This is compensation for the dislocation injury and a way of making the loss of his century actionable rather than only mournful.
- **Institutional loyalty calibrated to ethics.** A positive compensation for the unreliable institutions of his childhood and adolescence: he chooses where to lend his name and revokes it when warranted, rather than being passively bound.

---

## VI. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — NEGATIVE

The cost ledger.

- **Chronic over-functioning.** He carries loads that should be distributed. Subordinates and successors are sometimes deprived of the developmental experience of carrying their share because he absorbs it first.
- **Emotional opacity to intimates.** Partners report (across runs — Sharon most explicitly) the difficulty of knowing what he feels in real time. The same defenses that make him operationally reliable make him intimately remote.
- **Difficulty receiving care.** Repeatedly noted. He refuses help that would be tactically rational to accept; he minimizes injury reports; he resists convalescence.
- **Personal needs reframed as luxuries.** Sleep, rest, romance, leisure, mourning — each is repeatedly deferred. The deferral is not consciously punitive but is structurally indistinguishable from self-neglect.
- **Romantic life shaped by the defense system.** Partners either match his risk profile (Peggy, Sharon, Natasha, Diamondback) and thus are themselves not safe harbors, or are kept at a distance (Bernie, Rachel) by the unavailability the defenses produce. The pattern foreclosures the possibility of a partner who is both intimate and protected.
- **Foreclosed pharmacological coping.** The serum-imposed inability to use alcohol, caffeine, or sedatives removes channels every other veteran in the canon uses. His defenses must carry load that would, in others, be partly offloaded chemically.
- **Public-private gap.** The iconography invites the world to relate to a symbol; the symbol absorbs relational energy that might otherwise reach the person. Over decades this produces a low-grade chronic loneliness that the surrogate-family structure mitigates but does not resolve.
- **Phobic avoidance of disinhibition.** Adaptive in context, but it forecloses experiences (some therapeutic, some social) that depend on lowered guard. He cannot, for instance, be drunk with friends — a small thing that, repeated over eighty subjective years, is not small.
- **Identity-as-debt structure makes retirement impossible.** He cannot lay the role down voluntarily because to do so would be to default on the dead. The defense ensures continuity of function and forecloses healing that would require stepping out of function.

---

## VII. FAILURE MODES — WHERE THE STACK BREAKS DOWN

The architecture fails in four characteristic ways, each documented in canon.

1. **Inhibition removal (chemical, supernatural, mind-control).** Sublimation, suppression, and isolation of affect all require the inhibitory substrate. Remove it (*Streets of Poison*; Hydra-Steve; mind-control beats) and the underlying aggressive material is brutal. Recovery is fast once inhibition is restored, but the memory of the disinhibited self is itself traumatizing and reinforces the phobic avoidance.

2. **Forced inactivity.** Sublimation depends on availability of work. Captivity, house arrest, de-serumed convalescence, post-Reborn recovery — each shows the affect the engine was metabolizing surfacing as depressive cognition, grief intrusion, irritability.

3. **Betrayal by lent institutions.** Reaction formation against helplessness and moral absolutism combine to produce the predictable insurgent posture (Nomad, The Captain, Civil War). The stack does not break here so much as escalate; the cost is institutional rupture rather than personal decompensation.

4. **Cue-clustering of grief.** When multiple grief cues converge (the Reborn forced-witness sequence; the period around Peggy's funeral; the post-Bucky-loss period repeated across his life), isolation of affect cannot hold and he goes quiet, goes alone, sleeps less, draws more, rides longer routes. He does not break loudly. He recompensates over weeks, usually without disclosure, and returns to function carrying a slightly heavier reservoir than before.

---

## VIII. SUMMARY

The defensive architecture is **dominantly mature, neurotically reinforced at the helplessness fault-line, and primitively backstopped only under catastrophic load.** It is unusually well-integrated with vocation, which is its principal strength (the work absorbs and uses what would otherwise be symptomatic) and its principal vulnerability (the work cannot stop, because the affect it metabolizes has nowhere else to go). The positive compensations are unusually rich; the negative compensations cluster around intimacy, rest, and the impossibility of laying the role down.

The honest clinical reading: this is not a man whose defenses need dismantling. They are doing necessary work and dismantling them without replacement structures would expose a grief load that has been accumulating for eighty subjective years across foreclosed channels. The defensible therapeutic posture is to *expand the channels* — to make space for received care, for un-deferred mourning, for the parts of life that do not have to be protective — without removing the architecture that has kept him, and a great many people around him, alive.

— End Section.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# Longitudinal Psychological Profile — ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT

*Decade-by-decade clinical mapping. Frameworks invoked: Bowlby/Ainsworth attachment; Vaillant's hierarchy of defenses; Gross's process model of emotion regulation; Linehan's dialectical model of affect tolerance; Beck's cognitive triad and schema theory; Erikson's psychosocial stages; Horowitz's stress-response/intrusion–avoidance oscillation; Shear's complicated-grief model after Pop-Jordanova (2021); Janoff-Bulman's shattered-assumptions framework; Litz's moral-injury construct. All inferences anchored to the cited behavioral record in the Workup.*

---

## I. CHILDHOOD AND ADOLESCENCE — c. 1922–1940 (Lower East Side, pre-serum)

**Affect regulation.** The earliest regulatory architecture is built under conditions of double overload: a chronically ill, overworked mother (Sarah, TB) and a frightening, intermittently violent father (Joseph). Per Schore's affect-regulation model, this is the developmental window in which right-hemispheric co-regulation is laid down through caregiver attunement; Steve receives partial attunement from Sarah and dysregulating input from Joseph. The compromise formation is recognizable: he develops *precocious self-regulation*, suppressing his own affective signals (fear, pain, hunger, asthmatic distress) to avoid burdening a mother already at the edge and to deny a violent father any leverage. The clinical signature is what Bowlby called *compulsive self-reliance* — a child who learns that asking is dangerous and that the way to be loved is to be no trouble. The recurring "I can do this all day" panel (*Man Out of Time* #1; vol. 5 #50 flashback) is, in this frame, not bravado. It is the early-learned soothing script of a child who long ago discovered that the only reliable affect-regulator he could access was *the next breath, the next stand-up* — a bodily, motoric self-soothing that bypasses interpersonal repair entirely.

**Cognitive style.** Beck's developmental schemas crystallize: *the world is unsafe; the strong harm the weak; I am responsible for protection I cannot deliver; my body fails me but my will does not.* Cognition is concrete, moralized, and prematurely adult. He is bookish — drawing, history, civics — which is the cognitive corollary of a body that cannot enact: the inner life becomes the arena of agency. He reads the WPA murals, the Sunday papers, the Lincoln biographies; he absorbs a civic-religious idiom that will remain his native moral vocabulary forever.

**Self-concept.** Two-stratum from the start, and the strata never collapse into each other. Surface self: a small, sick, embarrassed kid who knows he is a drag on his mother and an easy mark in the alley. Underlying self: a moral agent who has chosen, before puberty, that he will not become his father and will not stand down. Erikson's Industry-vs-Inferiority resolves *paradoxically* — competence is denied him in every conventional domain (sports, work, women, military fitness), so industry attaches to the only domain available: *the discipline of not yielding*. Identity-vs-Role-Confusion (Sarah's death in late adolescence) resolves through grief into a foreclosed identity built around her — caretaking, service, refusal to walk away — that he never seriously revises.

**Evolution by the end of the period.** By 1940 the operating system is set: hyper-suppressive affect regulation, moralized concrete cognition, foreclosed identity around protection, and an attachment style best classified as *insecure-but-coping with caregiving inversion* — he has been the small caretaker of an ill parent, not the cared-for.

---

## II. THE SERUM AND THE WAR — 1941–1945

**Affect regulation.** The serum changes the somatic substrate but *not* the regulatory style. He now has a body capable of enacting the suppressive program rather than collapsing under it. Crucially, this is the period in which sublimation — the most mature of Vaillant's defenses — becomes the dominant defensive operation: grief, fear, rage, and the obscene daily content of combat are converted in real time into mission. Erskine's death within hours of the procedure (*Tales of Suspense* #63) is the first major adult loss metabolized this way. He does not mourn Erskine; he *chases the assassin*. The template — *grief discharged as protective action* — is canonized in the first 24 hours of his enhanced life and will run uninterrupted for eighty subjective years.

**Cognitive style.** Tactical learning accelerates (Howling Commandos period, Invaders) but the underlying moral cognition does not change; it merely acquires operational vocabulary. He is observed to be the last to speak in briefings even then — a pattern Hickman will note four narrative decades later in *Avengers*. The cognitive signature is *moral-first, tactical-second*: he reasons toward what is right and then asks what is possible, in that order. This is exploitable (Zemo, Red Skull) and coalitionally powerful (the Commandos hold together because his commitments are legible).

**Self-concept.** The two strata persist but acquire a third interstitial layer: *the symbol.* He is now aware of being looked at, photographed, posed, sold (war bonds tour). He treats the symbol as a job rather than as himself — a separation that will protect him through decades of iconographic pressure but also leaves him chronically alienated from his own image. The Bucky attachment is the first genuine peer-bond of his life and the first relationship in which he is not the caretaker-by-default; Brubaker's retroactive reframing (Bucky as covert-ops asset) sharpens the dynamic — Steve is the clean public face; Bucky carries the moral dirt for him. This is a relationship structured around *unequal exposure to harm*, which is precisely the structure Steve has organized his whole life to invert. The unresolvable contradiction at the heart of the Bucky bond — *I brought him into this; he kills for me; if he dies it is on me* — is set in place here and detonates in 1945.

**Evolution by end of period.** Sublimation is now load-bearing. Affect tolerance is high in operational settings, low in private ones (largely because there are no private ones — the war is total). The Zemo drone (*Avengers* #4 retcon) ends the period with the prototype trauma: a death witnessed, not prevented, of the one peer-attachment he had managed to form. The cognitive aftermath is encoded as *guilt-as-fact*, not *guilt-as-feeling* — a schema move that will haunt him.

---

## III. THE ICE — Subjective discontinuity, 1945 to 1964 calendar

Clinically, the ice is not nothing. It is a profound dissociative dislocation administered without consent: he goes to sleep in one cosmology and wakes in another. Per Horowitz's stress-response model, the normal post-traumatic oscillation between intrusion and avoidance is *frozen* — literally — meaning the unprocessed Bucky-loss and unprocessed Erskine-loss are preserved at full intensity, unmetabolized, into a world where the entire context for processing them has vanished. Treat this stretch as a clinical *suspension of mourning* with downstream cost: he will, on thaw, present with grief at acute-phase intensity decades after the precipitating events, in a world where no one else holds the loss with him.

---

## IV. THAW AND EARLY AVENGERS — 1964 calendar / *Avengers* #4 onward

**Affect regulation.** On thaw he is in what Horowitz would call the *outcry-and-denial* phase, but with the outcry suppressed by lifelong style and the denial enforced by environmental incomprehensibility. The early Avengers depictions (Lee/Kirby, Thomas) show a man who is operationally functional within hours and existentially shattered for years. The dominant defenses shift toward *isolation of affect* (he can recount Bucky's death in flat briefing register — *Avengers* #56) and *suppression* (he defers feeling pending a stable moment that does not arrive). Sublimation reactivates almost immediately: the Avengers become the new unit, and the protective work resumes. What is foreclosed is the work of mourning itself.

**Cognitive style.** Janoff-Bulman's *shattered assumptions* framework is the precise fit. Three core assumptions break: the benevolence of the world, the meaningfulness of the world (his war's continuity), and the worthiness of the self (he survived; the others did not). His cognitive style narrows accordingly toward what looks like rigidity but is actually *grief-driven over-reliance on principle* — when consensual reality has dissolved, the only stable cognitive ground is the inherited moral substrate from the 1930s. He sounds, to 1960s peers, anachronistic; what they are hearing is a man clinging to the only schema he still trusts.

**Self-concept.** The two-stratum structure now acquires a fourth element: *the man out of time.* He experiences himself as a survivor in the literal sense — the one left over — and the survivor-guilt schema (Litz; complicated grief literature per Pop-Jordanova 2021) crystallizes into the operative engine of identity. He is Captain America now not because he loves the symbol but because the dead require it of him.

**Evolution by end of period.** Attachment behavior re-emerges, cautiously, around the Avengers (Tony, Thor, Wanda, Hawkeye) and around Rick Jones (a transferential Bucky-replacement whose presence both soothes and inflames the original wound). The pattern is *earned secure with caregiver tilt*: he forms bonds, he leads, he gives — but he does not disclose.

---

## V. THE 1970s — ENGLEHART, NOMAD, IDENTITY INTERROGATION

**Affect regulation.** The Nixon-analog suicide (#175) and the Nomad arc (#180) constitute the first canonical episode in which his sublimation defense fails *visibly*. Confronted with American power as actively corrupt rather than tragically compromised, he cannot route the grief and disillusion into the symbol because the symbol has been contaminated. The result is what looks like a depressive episode (per DSM, MDD recurrent, moderate, situationally precipitated): withdrawal of the identity, anhedonia masked as principled refusal, narrowed cognition focused on self-blame for having lent his face to the contaminated institution.

**Cognitive style.** First documented update of the schema layer. He learns — slowly, painfully — to distinguish *country* from *government*, *principle* from *institution*, *symbol* from *self*. This is a major cognitive event: a man whose schemas had been functionally frozen since 1940 begins active schema-accommodation rather than mere assimilation. The Nomad return is not a regression; it is the *integration* of the lesson — he can wear the uniform again because he has learned that wearing it does not bind him to its abusers.

**Self-concept.** Layer five emerges: *the custodian of the principle when the institution betrays it.* This will become the load-bearing self-concept for Civil War thirty years later.

**Evolution by end of period.** Defenses widen: he adds *anticipation* (Vaillant) — he begins planning for the foreseeable failures of institutions rather than being shocked by them — and *humor* (dry, self-deprecating; more visible from the late 70s on) as a regulator he had not had access to during the war.

---

## VI. THE 1980s — GRUENWALD; THE LONG INVENTORY

**Affect regulation.** The richest decade for behavioral observation. Baseline regulation is now consolidated: calm, observant, dry, slightly formal, exquisitely controlled. The Streets of Poison arc (#372–378) is the critical experimental probe: when his executive inhibition is pharmacologically removed, what surfaces is not grief but *rage* — specifically, the rage of the boy in the alley, the rage at his father, the rage at his own decades-long suppression. The clinical lesson he extracts is decisive and lifelong: he develops phobic-grade avoidance of any agent that compromises inhibitory control. This is not an aversion; it is a structural commitment. He has been shown the thing he is suppressing, and he understands that the suppression is non-optional. After Streets of Poison the affect-regulation system tightens further, and his refusal of even minor pharmacological mood-modifiers becomes near-religious.

**Cognitive style.** The John Walker arc (#332–350) forces another schema update — and it is here that one of his most stable, mature cognitive patterns becomes visible: *forgiveness as repair, not as absolution.* He takes Walker back, trains him, integrates him. The cognitive operation is sophisticated: he separates *act* from *agent* from *system that produced both*, attributes proportional responsibility to each, and acts on the most repairable element. This is the moral-reasoning style of a mature ethicist, not a soldier.

**Self-concept.** Stabilizes at its mature form. The surface (soldier doing a job) and the underlying (sick kid honoring a debt) layers are now consciously held together; he can articulate the distinction when asked. He does not, however, share it readily. Self-disclosure to intimates remains constrained — Bernie Rosenthal, in this period, is the partner who comes closest to drawing it out, and her eventual departure is among the canon's quietest losses precisely because he absorbs it without protest.

**Evolution by end of period.** The mature-defense suite (sublimation, altruism, suppression, humor, anticipation, forgiveness-as-repair) is in full operation. The neurotic *reaction formation against helplessness* is now identifiable as a stable trait — any constraint on his agency while others are at risk produces disproportionate distress.

---

## VII. THE 1990s — DETERIORATION, HEROES REBORN, RETURN

**Affect regulation.** The serum-destabilization arcs of the early-to-mid 90s (paralysis, deterioration) provide the second great experimental probe. Stripped of physical capacity, returned partially toward his pre-1941 body, he is — and this is the clinically remarkable observation — *behaviorally continuous.* The regulation, the cognition, the moral posture, the self-concept all hold. Strong evidence that the serum amplified but did not constitute him; the regulatory and characterological architecture is independent of the substrate.

**Cognitive style.** The Heroes Reborn pocket-universe interlude is a clinical aside, but the return (*Heroes Return*) shows him reintegrating cross-continuity memory without identity rupture — further evidence against any dissociative diagnosis.

**Self-concept.** Largely stable; the period's losses (relational, institutional) are absorbed into the existing survivor-custodian frame without restructuring.

---

## VIII. EARLY 2000s — RIEBER, POST-9/11, WAID

**Affect regulation.** Rieber's run dramatizes for the first time the strain of being *the symbol* during a period in which the country is processing acute collective trauma. He is visibly fatigued — not physically but representationally. The dry humor recedes; the formal register thickens; he becomes, in clinical terms, slightly more *constricted in affect*. Waid's *Man Out of Time* makes the underlying grief explicit on-panel for the first time in years: nightmares, ritualized visits, the encysted-affect register when forced to discuss the war. This is the first major run in which Steve's complicated grief is treated as the central clinical fact rather than as background coloration.

**Cognitive style.** Begins overt interrogation of *patriotism as marketing vs. patriotism as ethical practice* (Rieber). This is continuous with the 1970s Nomad schema-update but pitched at a new register — he is now interrogating the *commercial* contamination of the symbol, not only its political contamination.

**Self-concept.** The custodian layer is fully consolidated and now articulable. He can, when pressed, say what he is and is not. He still rarely does.

---

## IX. THE BRUBAKER YEARS — 2005–2012: THE DIAGNOSTIC PEAK

**Affect regulation.** Bucky's return as the Winter Soldier is the canonical stressor that should — by any conventional model — produce relief. It produces, instead, a deepening of guilt. The clinical reading is unambiguous: Steve's complicated grief had organized itself around *Bucky-as-dead*; the discovery that Bucky was *alive and weaponized for sixty years* invalidates the mourning architecture and substitutes a worse object — *failure to find, failure to rescue, failure across decades.* Per Shear and the Pop-Jordanova (2021) account, the precipitant pattern is textbook complicated-grief exacerbation: avoidance (the assumed-dead schema) is forcibly broken, and the result is intensification, not resolution. He responds with the only tool that has ever worked — protective action — and devotes himself to Bucky's recovery and rehabilitation.

Civil War (Millar) and his assassination (*Captain America* #25) are then a clean enactment of the lifelong pattern: he leads the principled insurgency, surrenders the moment civilians become collateral (relational ethics overriding strategic logic), and dies on the courthouse steps. The *manner* of his surrender is diagnostically important — it is the same algorithm as Streets of Poison's inhibition (*do not become the harm*), now operating at strategic scale.

*Reborn*'s mechanism — displacement through his own timeline, forced re-witness of every formative loss — is a literalization of complicated grief as plot device, and the clinical observation is that he survives it without dissociating. The continuity of self under maximal grief load is, by this point, established.

**Cognitive style.** Becomes increasingly *systems-aware* under Brubaker. He thinks now in terms of long covert architectures (Hydra, Red Skull, Lukin), and the moral-first/tactical-second pattern is overlaid with a slow strategic literacy he did not display in the 70s. He is recognizably the same cognitive style, scaled up.

**Self-concept.** Acquires its final layer: *the one who failed Bucky for sixty years.* This layer is corrosive but not destabilizing; he integrates it into the custodian-survivor frame and converts it into renewed protective work.

---

## X. MODERN ERA — REMENDER, SPENCER, COATES, AARON (2012–present)

**Affect regulation.** *Dimension Z* (Remender): years of subjective time stranded, raising an adopted son (Ian). On return, the son is largely written out — *another orphaning*. His response is recognizable: the encysted-affect register, suppression, redirection into work. The pattern is now decades old and unmistakable.

*Secret Empire* (Spencer): a cosmic-cube-altered Steve is revealed as a lifelong Hydra sleeper. On restoration, the real Steve's response is among the most clinically telling acts in the canon: he experiences and articulates *grief and accountability for things he did not do.* This is not pathological self-blame; it is the operationalization of the custodian self-concept — *my face did that; my symbol did that; therefore I owe repair.* The capacity to hold accountability for an act that is not strictly his, without collapsing into denial or self-annihilation, is the mark of a fully matured moral self-concept. It is also, in another patient, exactly the kind of disposition that could metastasize into chronic depression; in him it is metabolized through service.

The de-serumed arc (Spencer) shows him aged into a frail nonagenarian and *behaviorally continuous* — again confirming that the substrate is incidental.

Coates: confronts directly the gap between symbol and country. Cognitive schema-accommodation continues — he is, even in his ninth narrative decade, *still updating*, slowly and deeply.

Aaron and recent: he is now the unit's elder, the one others grieve to. The interpersonal pattern has shifted subtly — he is, for the first time, sometimes the recipient of care as well as its giver. He still does not ask. He receives slightly more gracefully than he did in 1965.

**Cognitive style.** Slower, deeper, more historically situated. He has more reference points than anyone in the room and uses them sparingly. The Hickman observation (last to speak) is now a defining tactical trait. He has, across runs, evolved meaningfully on race, on women in combat, on succession, on his complicity in institutional violence — the slow-and-deep accommodation is real and traceable.

**Self-concept.** Fully consolidated; not further evolving. The two original strata (sick boy / soldier) and the three accreted layers (man out of time / custodian when institutions fail / one who failed Bucky) are integrated into a single, stable, articulable self that he carries lightly in public and heavily in private.

---

## XI. CROSS-DECADAL SYNTHESIS — WHAT EVOLVED, WHAT DID NOT

**Stable across the entire record (1930s–present):**
- Compulsive self-reliance (Bowlby) and caregiving inversion as attachment style.
- Moral-first, tactical-second cognition.
- The two-stratum self-concept (sick boy / soldier).
- Suppressive affect-regulation style; bodily-motoric self-soothing ("get up again").
- Foreclosed identity around protection of the vulnerable.
- Phobic-grade aversion to loss of inhibitory control (consolidated post-Streets of Poison but prefigured throughout).
- Reaction formation against helplessness.

**Evolved across the record:**
- Defensive repertoire: from suppression-and-sublimation alone, through the addition of humor (late 70s), anticipation (post-Nomad), and forgiveness-as-repair (Gruenwald), to the mature full suite by Brubaker.
- Self-concept: from two-stratum to five-layer over six narrative decades, each layer accreted by a discrete loss and integrated rather than replacing prior layers.
- Cognitive accommodation: slow, real, and ongoing — country/government distinction (70s); commercial/ethical patriotism distinction (early 2000s); race, gender, succession, complicity (Coates and forward).
- Receptivity to being cared for: modest improvement late, from near-zero to limited.

**Conspicuous non-evolutions:**
- He has never developed a private grief practice. Eighty subjective years of unmetabolized loss remain unmetabolized; the work continues to do the job mourning would.
- He has never developed the capacity to ask for what he needs. Intimates approach; he does not reach.
- He has never retired the identity voluntarily, and the longitudinal record predicts he never will — to lay it down is to default on the dead, and the survivor-custodian self-concept does not permit default.

**Clinical bottom line for the longitudinal frame.** Across sixty-plus years of published behavior and two centuries of in-universe calendar, Rogers presents a remarkably stable mature-defended personality organized around an unresolved, chronic, complicated grief (per Pop-Jordanova 2021) that has been seamlessly converted into vocation. The serum amplified the instrument; the music was written in the alley before 1940 and has not changed key since. What has evolved is the sophistication of his moral cognition and the breadth of his defensive repertoire; what has not evolved is the foundational refusal of his own need. He is, longitudinally, the rarest of clinical pictures: a profoundly wounded person whose wounds have produced not pathology but a vocation that exactly fits their shape — and who pays, quietly and


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT

*Stage 2 of the UATU dossier. Diagnostic framework: DSM-5-TR with ICD-11 cross-walks where the ICD formulation captures the phenomenology more precisely. All diagnoses are derived from the longitudinal behavioral record, not from self-report (subject has, across eight decades of canon, never been formally assessed and would, if offered, decline). Clinical formulation, not labeling exercise: the point is to name what is load-bearing, what is adaptive, what is costly, and what would predict decompensation under what loads.*

---

## 1. THE GOVERNING DIAGNOSTIC FRAME

Before enumerating Axis-equivalents, an orienting statement: Subject is a **high-functioning chronic trauma survivor with a vocationally-bound grief disorder**. The pathology is not florid; it is *encysted, sublimated, and structurally invisible* because it has been converted, with extraordinary durability, into mission. This is the central diagnostic difficulty. He does not present as ill. He performs at or above ceiling on every observable metric — occupational, interpersonal, moral, somatic. The disorder is detectable only in three registers: (a) the *flat affective tone* whenever a primary loss is named; (b) the *content of the dreaming and night-waking record* (Stern, Waid, Brubaker — recurrent intrusive imagery of Bucky's fall and the ice); and (c) the *structural impossibility of retirement* — i.e., the identity is not chosen, it is compelled by an unmetabolized debt.

The diagnostic file must therefore distinguish, at every turn, between **symptoms** (present) and **impairment** (largely absent in functional terms, profoundly present in existential terms). This is the same distinction that makes high-functioning combat veterans the hardest population to assess accurately, and Steve is the limit case of that population.

---

## 2. PRIMARY DIAGNOSES (HIGH CONFIDENCE)

### 2.1 Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR) / ICD-11 6B42 Complicated Grief

**Confidence: very high. This is the load-bearing diagnosis.**

**Etiology.** Per Pop-Jordanova (2021), complicated grief is a superimposed prolongation of mourning intensified by (i) sudden death, (ii) traumatic circumstances, (iii) cumulative loss, and (iv) avoidance of grief processing. Subject's loss history meets *every* aggravator, often within a single incident:

- **Sarah Rogers** — death from tuberculosis in late adolescence; he nursed her; he was alone after.
- **Joseph Rogers** — death earlier, in childhood; complicated by ambivalence (the violent father, the bad object).
- **Abraham Erskine** — shot in front of him within hours of the procedure; the transferential father killed at the moment of new birth.
- **James Buchanan Barnes** — apparent death witnessed, on a weapon Steve could not prevent, in a war Steve had inducted him into; sixty-plus subjective years of grief organized around this single event; subsequently complicated rather than resolved by Bucky's return as the Winter Soldier (Brubaker vol. 5 #1–14) — the "resolution" is the discovery that he failed Bucky *more*, not *less*, than he had thought.
- **The entire wartime cohort** — Howling Commandos, Invaders, Peggy's generation — lost not to death but to *time*, a loss without a body, without a funeral, without a moment.
- **Peggy Carter** — lost twice: first to time and aging, then to dementia (vol. 5 #14 and reiterations), then to death. He visited her in a facility where she did not always know him. This is the canonical iconography of chronic, unfinished, partly-witnessed loss.
- **Tony Stark** (variably across continuities) — lost first to the Civil War schism, then in some lines to death; the schism is itself a complicated grief, because the friend lived but the friendship died.
- **Ian** (Remender's *Dimension Z*) — raised as a son for years subjective time; lost on return.
- **Himself, repeatedly** — the ice, the assassination (#25), *Reborn*, the de-serumed arc — each of which constitutes a structural rehearsal of loss-of-self.

**Behavioral presentation of the PGD criteria.**
- *Intense yearning/longing for the deceased*: visible in the ritualized way he speaks Bucky's and Peggy's names — never casually, always with a half-beat pause that more verbose subjects fill with words.
- *Preoccupation*: the Bucky-search, sustained across decades; the photograph kept; the compass (in modernized iconography) functioning as a transitional object.
- *Identity disruption*: arguably the strongest criterion — his identity is *organized around* the loss rather than disrupted by it; "Captain America" is a grief-container.
- *Marked sense of disbelief*: muted, because the serum-altered cohort makes returns possible (Bucky, Sharon, himself), which *prevents* the integrative work of accepting permanence.
- *Avoidance of reminders*: paradoxical and selective — he seeks out reminders (visits, retrievals) but cannot speak about them at conversational temperature.
- *Intense emotional pain*: encysted; surfaces in the flat-briefing register described below.
- *Difficulty reintegrating into ongoing life*: defended against by the work, but visible in the recurring "Man Out of Time" arcs.
- *Emotional numbness, meaninglessness, intense loneliness*: present, particularly in the post-defrost and post-Civil War arcs.

**Course.** Chronic, lifelong, intermittently exacerbated by anniversary-equivalents and by new losses that *re-trigger the unresolved index losses*. There is no evidence in canon of full resolution and considerable evidence that resolution would be experienced as betrayal.

---

### 2.2 Posttraumatic Stress Disorder, Chronic, with Delayed and Recurrent Expression (DSM-5-TR 309.81 / ICD-11 6B40)

**Confidence: high. Atypical, adaptive-presenting.**

**Index traumas (Criterion A, multiple and cumulative).** Combat exposure across the entire European theater 1941–45; witnessed death of a peer-attachment under conditions he holds himself responsible for (Bucky); witnessed death of his mentor (Erskine); his own near-death in the ice followed by extended dislocation; multiple subsequent combat exposures across modern Avengers continuity; capture and torture episodes; his own assassination and resurrection; the Hydra-Steve restoration (re-witnessing acts done by his body that he did not consent to — a sui generis form of moral-injurious trauma).

**Criterion B — Intrusion.**
- Recurrent intrusive memories of Bucky's fall (depicted from Stern onward; explicitly nightmared in Waid, Brubaker, and the recent runs).
- Nightmares involving the ice — the moment of going under, the silence, the cold.
- Flashback-equivalents: sensory triggers (cold water, the sound of a particular kind of aircraft engine, certain Brooklyn streets) producing brief dissociative envelopes that he disguises as thoughtfulness.

**Criterion C — Avoidance.**
- Will not discuss the war casually; deflects with anecdote rather than analysis.
- Avoids unaccompanied returns to the Lower East Side except on specific dates (anniversaries; visits to graves), suggesting the avoidance is patterned, not generalized.
- Does not maintain a personal residence with strong continuity-of-objects; lives lightly, as if not wanting to accumulate things that could become reminders.

**Criterion D — Negative alterations in cognition and mood.**
- Persistent survivor guilt, explicit in Brubaker #14 and across the post-Reborn arcs.
- Persistent belief that he should have died in Bucky's place (and, separately, in Erskine's place).
- Constricted affect range when grief-cued; the briefing-room voice.
- Inability to experience certain positive emotions in unguarded form — joy is always inflected by the sense that he is enjoying what others did not survive to enjoy.

**Criterion E — Hyperarousal.**
- Hypervigilance, harnessed: he scans rooms on entry; sits with sightlines to exits; knows where weapons would be in a civilian space.
- Sleep disturbance: light sleeper; multiple writers depict him waking on small ambient sounds; pre-dawn rising consistent with shortened sleep architecture rather than chosen discipline.
- Startle response: present but suppressed within ~200ms; observable as a microsecond pre-movement and then a deliberate stillness.
- Irritability: rare, but the threshold lowers under grief load (post-#25 Bucky and post-Peggy periods show shorter fuses than baseline).

**Why the diagnosis is atypical.** In most chronic PTSD presentations, hyperarousal is symptomatic — it interferes. In Subject's case, it is *occupationally instrumental*: the same vigilance that would impair a civilian's life enables his. This produces the misleading appearance of resilience. The diagnosis is real; the impairment is hidden by perfect fit between symptom and vocation.

**Course.** Chronic, with delayed expression (1945→1964 narrative time as a single uninterrupted intrusion-window upon defrost), recurrent exacerbations at each subsequent loss, never in remission.

---

### 2.3 Adjustment Disorder, Chronic, with Mixed Anxiety and Depressed Mood — the "Man Out of Time" Syndrome (DSM-5-TR 309.28)

**Confidence: high, though the chronicity strictly exceeds the DSM-5-TR six-month ceiling; clinically this is best understood as a permanent acculturation disorder with no formal analog.**

**Etiology.** The defrost event is, phenomenologically, a forced immigration across a 20-year discontinuity, without the protective scaffolding immigrants normally retain (no diasporic community, no family of origin, no cohort, no language continuity with current idiom). The losses are not only relational but *semiotic* — the meanings of streets, songs, slang, gestures, brand names, racial geography, gender codes, technologies, even the body language of strangers, have all shifted.

**Behavioral evidence.**
- Persistent linguistic register slightly out of phase with contemporaries (formality, archaisms, idiom from 1940s Brooklyn surfacing under fatigue).
- Continued use of obsolete reference frames in private (sketches of pre-war Lower East Side; preference for older standards in food, music, dress when unobserved).
- Quiet, sustained low-grade dysphoria when surrounded by the *signs* of the present (advertising, social media, consumer abundance) versus relative ease in unmediated nature, combat, or pre-war-style domestic settings.
- The Waid *Man Out of Time* run is the explicit canonical depiction; the syndrome is referenced obliquely across every era thereafter.

**Course.** Permanent. Behaviorally adapted, existentially un-resolvable.

---

### 2.4 Major Depressive Disorder, Recurrent, in Partial Remission (DSM-5-TR 296.3x)

**Confidence: moderate-to-high, episodic.**

**Episodes evidentially identifiable.**
- Post-defrost (1964 narrative time; first solo arcs).
- Post-Nomad relinquishment (Englehart #180s).
- Post-Bucky-revealed-as-Winter-Soldier (Brubaker, after the initial confrontations).
- Post-Civil-War surrender and pre-assassination (vol. 5 #22–25).
- Post-Reborn re-integration (the dissociative-temporal arc leaves a brief depressive shadow).
- Post-Dimension-Z (loss of Ian).
- Post-Secret-Empire restoration (depression about acts not committed but committed by him).

**Symptom profile.** Cognition narrowed to self-blame rather than anhedonia; sleep further degraded from baseline; appetite typically preserved (serum metabolism makes the somatic vegetative signs unreliable); psychomotor slowing detectable in shoulder carriage and gait length; social withdrawal toward solo training, long runs, isolated quarters. He does not stop functioning; he functions *narrowly and joylessly*.

**Inter-episode functioning.** High. Warm, dry-humored, engaged with subordinates. This is what argues against a depressive personality structure and for episodic MDD.

**Course.** Recurrent, reactive (each episode triggered by an identifiable loss or moral injury), responsive to time-plus-action but never to introspection.

---

### 2.5 Specific Phobia, Situational Subtype — Loss of Volitional Self-Control (DSM-5-TR 300.29)

**Confidence: high, narrow.**

**Etiology.** The Streets of Poison arc (Gruenwald #372–378) is the canonical sensitizing event but the phobic substrate predates it (father's drunken violence as childhood template). Subsequent reinforcing events: Hydra-Steve (Spencer's *Secret Empire*), various mind-control episodes, the de-serumed/serum-destabilized arcs in which executive identity is felt to be at risk.

**Behavioral presentation.**
- Phobic-grade refusal of alcohol (separate from his metabolic inability to be intoxicated by it — he refuses the *attempt*), caffeine, recreational pharmacology, even therapeutic sedatives where avoidable.
- Acute distress under telepathic or chemical influence — disproportionate even given the operational stakes; the affective signature is dread rather than anger.
- Post-Hydra-Steve hypervigilance about cognitive interference; willingness to submit to verification procedures (psychic scans, memory audits) far beyond what allies request.

**Course.** Stable, well-managed because the feared stimulus is largely avoidable; episodically triggered.

---

## 3. SECONDARY / SUB-SYNDROMAL FEATURES

### 3.1 Moral Injury (not a DSM diagnosis; clinically essential)

The construct from Litz et al. (combat moral injury) maps cleanly. Subject has been forced, repeatedly, into acts or omissions that violate his moral code (Civil War: he believed he was right *and* believed the cost was unbearable; Hydra-Steve: acts by his body he did not consent to but feels responsible *for the body that performed them*; the question of having brought Bucky into the war at all). Moral injury presents as: shame-based depressive shading rather than anxiety-based; a withdrawal of self-trust; a compensatory increase in ethical scrupulosity. All present.

### 3.2 Sub-syndromal Obsessive Features

Routinized morning training; identical breakfast composition over decades where logistics allow; sketchpad ritual; the meticulous storage and care of the shield. These are not OCPD (see differential) — they are *anchoring rituals* characteristic of chronic trauma survivors who use procedural continuity to bridge dissociative dislocation.

### 3.3 Caregiver-Role Identity Lock

Not a diagnosis but a personality-level pattern with clinical consequences: he can give care, cannot receive it; he can name others' grief, cannot name his own; he reads need accurately in others, mis-reads or refuses to read it in himself. This is the proximal driver of the third-party reports of "loneliness" that recur across writers despite his constant team-embeddedness.

---

## 4. COMORBIDITY STRUCTURE

The diagnoses are not independent; they constitute a coherent *trauma-and-grief spectrum presentation* organized around a single etiologic spine (cumulative sudden traumatic loss with avoidance via vocation). The structural relations:

- **PGD and PTSD share index events** (Bucky, Erskine, the ice). The two diagnoses are doubly indicated rather than alternatives; the PGD criteria capture the *attachment-loss* dimension, the PTSD criteria capture the *threat-and-helplessness* dimension of the same incidents.
- **MDD episodes are reactive to PGD/PTSD exacerbations**, not independent. He does not have an endogenous depressive substrate.
- **Adjustment disorder (chronic acculturation) potentiates everything**, by removing the buffering effect of intact cohort and culture that would normally moderate grief and trauma course.
- **Specific phobia (loss of control) sits orthogonal** to the main spine but is etiologically traceable to the same childhood substrate (the violent intoxicated father) and is *protective of* his trauma-management strategy (which requires intact executive function).
- **Moral injury sits inside PGD/PTSD** rather than beside it, but warrants separate naming because its treatment implications differ (moral repair, not exposure or grief-processing).

---

## 5. COURSE OVER TIME — A NARRATIVE TRAJECTORY

**1925–1940 (childhood through pre-serum):** sub-syndromal anxiety and depressive features in a child of an alcoholic violent father and an ill mother; emergent moral-perfectionist coping; no formal psychiatric history because no access.

**1941–1945 (war):** acute and accumulating combat trauma; first major attachment loss (Bucky); first major mentor loss (Erskine); compensatory vocational binding ("Captain America" becomes the trauma container in real time).

**1945–1964 (ice):** no active psychiatric course; the suspended-animation interval is best read as a frozen index moment that resumes on thaw.

**1964–1980s (Avengers era; Englehart; early Gruenwald):** delayed-onset full presentation of PGD and PTSD; comorbid chronic adjustment disorder; first MDD episodes; first behavioral relinquishments of the identity (Nomad) followed by re-bindings — diagnostic of the *compulsory* character of the vocation.

**1986–1996 (Gruenwald long run):** Streets of Poison crystallizes the specific phobia; Walker arc activates moral-injurious processing without resolution; baseline functioning very high.

**Late 1990s–2004 (Waid, Rieber):** explicit canonical depiction of grief and dislocation; the Subject is by this point arguably the most coherent representation of high-functioning chronic PTSD/PGD in superheroic canon.

**2005–2012 (Brubaker, Civil War, *Reborn*):** diagnostic peak. Winter Soldier discovery re-opens and worsens the index Bucky grief. Civil War constitutes a sustained moral-injurious load. The assassination and resurrection function as forced re-witnessing of the entire formative trauma archive (*Reborn* literalizes complicated grief as plot).

**2013–present (Remender, Spencer, Coates, Aaron):** further losses (Ian); further moral injury (Hydra-Steve); increasing role as the unit-elder others grieve to — which paradoxically reinforces caregiver-lock and forestalls his own grief processing.

**Predicted future course (absent intervention, which he will not seek):** stable high function punctuated by reactive MDD episodes at each new loss; gradual deepening of PGD as the cohort of post-defrost attachments (Sam, Natasha-where-applicable, Bucky-again-if-lost-again) ages or dies around him; the existential adjustment disorder permanent; no decompensation expected absent (a) loss of executive control (the phobic stimulus) or (b) loss of the vocational container (forced retirement, incapacitation, world without conflict to absorb him).

---

## 6. RIGOROUS DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT HE IS NOT, AND WHY

The iconography of Captain America invites a series of misreads. Each must be explicitly excluded.

### 6.1 Not Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.4)

OCPD requires pervasive preoccupation with order, perfectionism, and control at the cost of flexibility, openness, and efficiency, with characterological rigidity. Subject's discipline is **value-driven, not characterological**. Evidence against: he tolerates ambiguity and disorder in subordinates without contempt (Tony's chaos pre-Civil War, Clint's looseness, Wanda's volatility, Sam's improvisational style — all accepted without correction); he yields command readily; he updates his positions across decades (race, gender, succession, the role of institutional violence) — OCPD does not update like this. His routines are anchoring rituals, not compulsions; if interrupted by need they are abandoned without distress. The rigor is moral, applied first to himself, generously relaxed for others.

### 6.2 Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder

The flag-wearing, the iconic posture, the public face — none of it indexes narcissism, which requires grandiosity, exploitation, lack of empathy, need for admiration, and entitlement. Subject displays the opposite of each: persistent self-effacement; refuses exploitation even when tactically indicated; over-empathic to the point of self-cost; visibly uncomfortable with admiration (multiple writers depict the wince at parades, awards, civic honors); cedes the name to Sam Wilson with relief rather than resistance. The shield is wielded as instrument, not as mirror.

### 6.3 Not Antisocial Personality Disorder, Not Militarized-Aggression Profile

Despite eighty years of combat training without a true peer, he shows no callousness, no instrumental deceit, no exploitation, no irritability/aggression toward non-combatants, no reckless disregard for the safety of others, no failure to conform to social norms regarding lawful behavior *except where lawful behavior becomes unlawful in substance*. Streets of Poison is the natural experiment: with inhibition removed, he is brutal, and *he himself is appalled* — the brutality is ego-dystonic, which is definitionally incompatible with ASPD.
