Pencil and graphite over color; he is technically very competent and dislikes praise for it. Sketchbooks are kept in chronological sequence, dated on the spine, never thrown away.

**GIVEN** access to a public library → **EXPECT** he uses it (H). He owns a card under his civilian name in every city he frequents. He reads history (especially of the latter half of the 20th century — the part he missed), biography, contemporary fiction by writers his colleagues recommend, and poetry (he will not say so unprompted). He keeps a running list of books read; he annotates margins lightly in pencil and erases the marks before returning.

**GIVEN** a film recommendation → **EXPECT** he watches it, takes notes, returns with one specific question that demonstrates close attention (H). He prefers theaters to home viewing — the social ritual of strangers watching together is something he missed during the ice and now actively values.

**GIVEN** music → **EXPECT** broad and curious taste, with a baseline affection for swing, early jazz, mid-century vocalists; he has acquired a working knowledge of every decade since because younger colleagues kept handing him things (H). He listens to a record straight through and does not shuffle.

---

## 12. ANIMALS, CHILDREN, STRANGERS-IN-NEED

**GIVEN** a dog in a public space → **EXPECT** he asks the owner before approaching, crouches, lets the dog come to him (H). He has not kept a pet since boyhood — the schedule does not permit it and the loss is foreseeable. He will dog-sit for teammates.

**GIVEN** a lost child → **EXPECT** he kneels, gets the child's first name and a parent's name, calls the parent if a number is known, otherwise stays at the child's chosen reference point (a bench, a tree, a counter) and signals a uniformed adult without leaving (H).

**GIVEN** an unhoused person in extreme weather → **EXPECT** intervention disproportionate to the circumstance (H): blanket from his own kit, walk to the nearest shelter, ride paid for. He will not photograph it, mention it, or accept thanks beyond an acknowledgement.

---

## 13. CONFLICT BELOW THE THRESHOLD OF VIOLENCE

**GIVEN** a verbal insult directed at him → **EXPECT** no response (H). He has been called everything; his self-concept is not adjudicated by strangers.

**GIVEN** an insult directed at a companion or a bystander → **EXPECT** immediate, calm, low-volume intervention (H): body interposed, eye contact with the aggressor, a single sentence offering the aggressor an exit. Escalation only if the aggressor closes distance on the third party. He is exceptionally good at de-escalation precisely because he is unafraid of escalation.

**GIVEN** road-rage directed at a vehicle he is driving → **EXPECT** he yields lane, signals thanks, does not return aggression (H). He drives like a 1940s chauffeur — hands at ten and two, no phone, mirrors checked on a metronome.

**GIVEN** a bar provocation aimed at his identity ("you're not the real Cap") → **EXPECT** he agrees mildly, buys the man a drink, leaves (H). He has no investment in being recognized as authentic by strangers because his authenticity is not for them to confer.

---

## 14. SEXUAL & ROMANTIC CONDUCT

**GIVEN** explicit interest from a stranger → **EXPECT** polite, slightly formal decline (H). He does not pursue casual encounters; the formative period was 1930s Catholic-adjacent Brooklyn and the loss-template is Peggy. The disinclination is not prudery — it is incapacity to compartmentalize intimacy from commitment.

**GIVEN** an existing partner and a private domestic evening → **EXPECT** undivided attention, slow disclosure, a tactile vocabulary heavier than his verbal one (H — he touches a forearm, the back of a neck, a shoulder, with a deliberate gentleness that registers as careful rather than tentative). He is uncoordinatedly literate about consent — he asks more than is currently fashionable and accepts answers without negotiation.

---

## 15. TRAVEL

**GIVEN** commercial air travel → **EXPECT** aisle seat, no carry-on beyond a small duffel, courteous to crew, signs the things he is asked to sign (H). He stands for elderly passengers without performance. He never reclines fully.

**GIVEN** a hotel room → **EXPECT** he checks the room (exits, sightlines), unpacks fully (he refuses to live out of a bag — Depression artifact of stability-as-luxury), and tips the housekeeper in cash daily with a folded note (H).

**GIVEN** international travel → **EXPECT** he has acquired functional travel-grammar in French, German, Russian, and at least conversational Japanese over the decades (H — Brubaker- and Hickman-era allusions); he uses it haltingly, apologizes for accent, lets the other party switch to English without face-loss.

---

## 16. HOLIDAYS & ANNIVERSARIES

**GIVEN** July 4 → **EXPECT** he is working (H). He treats the date as obligation, not festivity; he will appear at a children's hospital or a veterans' event rather than a parade. He does not host a barbecue. He is photographed minimally and willingly.

**GIVEN** Veterans Day / Memorial Day → **EXPECT** silence, attendance at a small graveside event, refusal to speak from a podium (H). He will accept the role of pallbearer for any surviving Commando or Invader on request.

**GIVEN** December — his birthday is canonically July 4, but **the dates that organize his year** are: the date Bucky fell, the date Erskine died, Sarah Rogers' death-date, Peggy's death-date → **EXPECT** observable behavioral compression in the week preceding each (H): more exercise, less talk, more time alone, the nightmare c


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*UATU dossier, Subject: ROGERS, S.G. Section 7 of the Synthesis. High-stakes / decompensation-edge behavioral forecasting. All predictions are GIVEN → EXPECT pairs grounded in the longitudinal record (Sec. 1) and the personality synthesis (Sec. 5). Confidence intervals are coarse: HIGH (≥85% across cited canon instances), MODERATE (60–84%), CONDITIONAL (depends on specified modulators). Where the prediction concerns the wound directly — Sarah, Joseph, Erskine, Bucky, Peggy, the ice — confidence rises and the behavioral window narrows.*

---

## 7.1 ACUTE CRISIS — KINETIC AND TACTICAL

**GIVEN** a mass-casualty event in progress within his sensory range (explosion, collapse, active shooter, fire), **EXPECT** him to move toward it before completing situational assessment, *but* to triage on arrival in a specific order that is invariant across canon: (1) immediate-danger civilians, (2) trapped civilians, (3) wounded responders, (4) hostile actors, (5) himself. HIGH. The order is observable from *Cap* vol. 1 #247 (Brooklyn fire) through Brubaker #6 (subway bombing) through Coates's Nuremberg analog. He will not delegate (1) and (2) to subordinates if he can perform them himself; this is a known tactical inefficiency and a reliable handle.

**GIVEN** a hostage situation where the demand is his surrender, **EXPECT** surrender within 90 seconds of the demand becoming credible, *contingent* on a verifiable release mechanism for the hostages. HIGH. *Cap* #25 (Civil War courthouse) is the paradigm. He does not bluff and does not stall when civilians are the chips. Adversaries who understand this exploit it once; he learns the specific actor's tell after one use and the tactic does not work again on the same source.

**GIVEN** a battlefield decision between his own extraction and a teammate's, **EXPECT** him to remain, regardless of mission criticality of his own escape. HIGH. The corollary worth flagging: if the teammate is a successor or someone he has mentored (Bucky, Sam, Walker post-rehabilitation, Ian, Kate), the threshold for self-sacrifice drops to zero. He is operating, in those moments, against the formative tape of failing to protect Bucky on the drone.

**GIVEN** the possibility of preventing a catastrophe by killing a noncombatant (the trolley-problem variant), **EXPECT** refusal followed by an attempt to find the third option, even at unrealistic cost. MODERATE-HIGH. He is not a strict deontologist — he will kill in combat and has — but the line between "combatant" and "noncombatant" is held with extraordinary stringency because the alternative is the slide that produced Walker. Adversaries who construct dilemmas of this shape buy themselves time, not victory.

**GIVEN** capture and interrogation, **EXPECT** name, rank, and a quality of silence that is itself informational — he is incapable of false ease and his refusals carry temperature. MODERATE. Under torture he will not break on operational intelligence; he *will* show, involuntarily, where the personal wounds are if the interrogator is sophisticated enough to read micro-tells (jaw, breath, the involuntary glance toward an absent shield). Zola and the Skull have both used this; both got more from watching him than from anything he said.

---

## 7.2 BETRAYAL — INSTITUTIONAL

**GIVEN** discovery that an institution bearing his iconography (the Commission, S.H.I.E.L.D., a Presidential administration, the Avengers charter itself) is engaged in systemic harm, **EXPECT** a three-phase sequence with predictable timing: (a) private verification, 24–72 hours, in which he triple-sources the evidence and confronts a trusted insider; (b) internal escalation through the institution's own channels, days to weeks, *which he will pursue past the point at which it is obviously futile* because the procedural attempt is itself a moral act; (c) public withdrawal of legitimacy — return of insignia, public statement, then operational opposition. HIGH. The Nixon-analog suicide (#175), the Commission removal (Gruenwald #332), and the Registration arc all follow this shape. The diagnostic feature is phase (b): faster actors will be in opposition before he has filed his second memo. This is not naïveté; it is the deliberate construction of a record that demonstrates exhaustion of legitimate avenues — a posture inherited from his Depression-era civics and unmodified by sixty years of disillusionment.

**GIVEN** that the betrayal is by a person he loves rather than an institution, **EXPECT** the timeline to collapse and the affect to invert. He is faster, quieter, and more wounded with persons than with institutions. The behavior to watch is not anger but withdrawal — a flat, briefing-room register, terse sentences, no second-personing of the betrayer. The Tony Stark break in Civil War is paradigmatic; Sharon's compromise periods are the relational template. He does not stop loving the person. He stops *available* to them.

**GIVEN** evidence that he himself has been used by an institution (cover story, false flag operation conducted under his name without his knowledge), **EXPECT** disproportionate self-blame, public acknowledgment of personal responsibility for the institutional act, and a corrective campaign run at the cost of his own standing. HIGH. *Secret Empire* aftermath is the clearest demonstration: the *real* Steve accepts accountability for acts he did not commit because his name authorized them. Adversaries can predict that staining the iconography stains him; he will not separate the two even when invited.

**GIVEN** a lawful order from a constituted authority that he assesses as unjust, **EXPECT** measured non-compliance with full transparency — he tells the issuing officer he will not comply, why, and accepts the consequence. He does not desert and he does not lie. The behavioral envelope is narrow and reliable: refuse, explain, surrender to process. CONDITIONAL on the process not itself being the instrument of the injustice; in that case (Registration), the envelope opens to insurgency, but he will still telegraph the shift in advance.

---

## 7.3 BETRAYAL — RELATIONAL

**GIVEN** the discovery that an intimate (Sharon, Natasha, Bucky, Tony) has been compromised by mind-control, possession, brainwashing, or coercion, **EXPECT** zero retributive affect toward the intimate and 100% redirection toward the controlling agent. HIGH. The Winter Soldier response is the canonical instance; he does not blame Bucky for sixty years of assassinations because his moral architecture treats coerced acts as the controller's, not the controlled's. This is exploitable: an adversary who can use his loved ones as weapons buys ground he cannot easily retake.

**GIVEN** the discovery that an intimate has betrayed him *freely* — not coerced — **EXPECT** a longer, quieter grief than rage. He will not denounce, will not publicize, will continue to defend the person against third parties even while the relationship is privately over. He absorbs the cost of the betrayal in the form of social and political damage to himself, treating the protection of the betrayer's reputation as the last expression of a finished love. MODERATE-HIGH. The pattern is visible with several women across the canon and, less obviously, with Tony in the long Civil War aftermath where Steve refused to permit collateral attacks on Tony's character even from his own faction.

**GIVEN** an attempt by an adversary to turn him by demonstrating that a beloved figure shared the adversary's view (e.g., a forged Erskine letter, a manipulated Peggy recording, a Bucky-says-so framing), **EXPECT** initial destabilization for hours, then forensic skepticism, then a fierce protectiveness of the manipulated figure's memory that becomes the engine of the counter-operation. MODERATE. Zemo and the Skull have both tried versions of this. The destabilization is real and is the window of exploit; the rebound is reliable and weaponizable against the manipulator.

---

## 7.4 TEMPTATION

**GIVEN** an offer of expanded power — political office, command of a standing army, dictatorial authority "for good," a seat at a cosmic governance body — **EXPECT** polite refusal with a specific reasoning he will articulate if pressed: that power held by one person is the failure mode he was built to oppose. HIGH. He has been offered the Presidency in canon (#250) and declined for exactly this reason. The refusal is not modesty; it is structural. Offers of this kind do not work on him and never have; sophisticated tempters do not try them.

**GIVEN** an offer of relief from the burden — retirement with honor, a quiet life, restoration of his original timeline, the chance to "go home" — **EXPECT** visible longing followed by refusal, the refusal grounded in the debt-to-the-dead structure. HIGH. This is the more dangerous category because the longing is real and exploitable in the *window* between offer and refusal. An adversary who can construct a credible "you've done enough" scenario buys minutes of hesitation and a residue of grief that may degrade subsequent decisions for hours. The Dimension Z arc — where he built a life with Ian over years of subjective time — is evidence that he *can* be partially captured by this offer if it is sustained and embedded in relational duty rather than rest.

**GIVEN** an offer of reunion with a specific lost person (Bucky pre-Brubaker, Peggy, Sarah, Erskine), credible enough to be entertained, **EXPECT** the longest hesitation in his behavioral repertoire. CONDITIONAL on credibility. He will not accept a reunion that requires moral compromise; he will accept enormous personal risk for one that does not. The Cosmic Cube and related reality-warping artifacts are the specific vector here, and his canonical response — including in *Secret Empire*'s overture and *Reborn*'s temporal displacement — has been to refuse the substitute and grieve the real loss again. The hesitation, however, is the tell that the wound is not closed.

**GIVEN** an offer to undo a specific past failure (save Bucky on the drone; pull Erskine out of the room; reach Peggy before the dementia), **EXPECT** the strongest temptation in the entire repertoire and a refusal that costs him visibly. HIGH-CONDITIONAL. He understands temporal mechanics well enough by modern canon to refuse on causal grounds. But the refusal is *labored*; observers who care for him should expect a depressive trough in the days following.

**GIVEN** an opportunity to use a method he has previously refused — lethal force against a defeated enemy, a torture-derived intelligence, a strategically advantageous lie — to prevent a clearly foreseen catastrophe, **EXPECT** refusal, with the catastrophe accepted as a cost he will personally try to mitigate from the other side. MODERATE-HIGH. He is not a pacifist and the threshold is not absolute; what is absolute is the refusal to let an end license a method he believes corrodes the agent. This is the lever the Skull has tried most often and lost on most often.

---

## 7.5 THE WOUND — DIRECT PALPATION

This subsection forecasts behavior when the formative wounds themselves are touched. Confidence is high; specificity is high; the operational window for adversarial exploit is short but real.

**GIVEN** invocation of his mother — her death, her overwork, her care of him, mockery of her, or invocation of her in a moral frame ("your mother would be ashamed") — **EXPECT** a brief, total quieting: shoulders drop fractionally, jaw sets, eyes go middle-distance for under two seconds, and the conversational register shifts to a formality that signals the topic is now closed. HIGH. Aggressors who push past this point produce a controlled coldness that, in combat, manifests as economy of motion and a refusal of theater. He does not avenge Sarah; he becomes, momentarily, the man she raised, which is more dangerous than the man who is angry.

**GIVEN** invocation of his father — alcoholism, violence, the suggestion that Steve carries any of it — **EXPECT** a different response: longer silence, a visible breath, no defensive denial. He has done the work of knowing what he came from and refuses to repudiate Joseph in public because he refuses to perform contempt for a dead damaged man. The lever fails for adversaries because Steve has already metabolized the comparison; what is visible is the labor of that metabolization, not a wound that bleeds. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN** invocation of Erskine — the death, the choice, the alleged failure to live up to "the good man" formulation — **EXPECT** the most intense compressed-affect response in his repertoire and the highest behavioral risk. HIGH. Erskine is the unhealed transferential father; the wound is structurally infected because it is also the foundation of the identity. He will not argue and will not engage; he will *act*, in the direction Erskine's formulation prescribes, often immediately and at cost. Adversaries who invoke Erskine to manipulate him will succeed in producing action and fail in producing the *direction* they intended, because the action will route through Erskine's ethics rather than the adversary's frame.

**GIVEN** the appearance, return, or weaponization of Bucky in any form, **EXPECT** all tactical considerations to be subordinated to Bucky's welfare for the duration. HIGH. This is the load-bearing exploit and the canon is unanimous: Brubaker's entire arc is built on it. He does not become irrational; he becomes *single-axis rational*, with Bucky as the axis. He will accept losses elsewhere on the board to retrieve, protect, or rehabilitate Bucky, and he will not apologize for the trade.

**GIVEN** invocation of Peggy — her dementia, her death, footage of her, a manipulated voice — **EXPECT** the encysted, briefing-room flatness that marks unmetabolized grief. HIGH. He will not be drawn into reminiscence and will redirect to operational subjects. The tell is the flatness itself; an observer can locate the wound by its temperature. Sophisticated adversaries do not press here because the rebound — once the grief is forced toward surface — produces a hardened resolve that is operationally counterproductive to manipulation.

**GIVEN** any cue that reactivates the ice — cold, isolation, the sense of having woken into a wrong time, a date or holiday that places him out of cohort, the death of one of the few remaining contemporaries (Howlers veterans, surviving Invaders) — **EXPECT** withdrawal of a few hours to a few days: long runs, solitary work in the gym, sketching (he draws; the habit predates the serum and survives every reset), and avoidance of the team's social spaces. MODERATE-HIGH. He returns on his own; intervention prolongs rather than shortens the episode. Intimates who know him learn to leave food and not knock.

**GIVEN** loss of executive control — intoxication, mind-control, possession, Hydra-induction, magical compulsion — **EXPECT** phobic-grade aftermath: refusal of any chemical agent for months, hypervigilance about telepathic and magical exposures, a brittle period in which his usual self-trust is degraded and he over-defers to teammates' read of his own behavior. HIGH. *Streets of Poison* established the template; *Secret Empire* deepened it. This is the wound he fears most because his entire adaptation rests on inhibitory mastery, and the demonstration that the mastery can be circumvented is, for him, ontologically destabilizing in a way no physical injury is.

**GIVEN** being *prevented from acting* while harm proceeds — restraint, incarceration, a legal injunction, a tactical hold-order from a superior — **EXPECT** rapid escalation of internal pressure and a calibrated breach of the constraint at the latest possible moment that still permits intervention. HIGH. This is his single least-tolerable condition (Sec. 5). The breach will be telegraphed; he will not deceive his constrainer; he will simply move and accept the consequence. Authorities relying on his compliance during ongoing harm have always lost that bet and will continue to.

---

## 7.6 DECOMPENSATION SIGNATURES

Decompensation in this subject is not florid. It is *quiet*, and the indicators are subtle by design — he has spent eighty years learning not to leak.

**Early-stage indicators** (stress accumulating, control intact): increased physical training load; reduction in social speech to functional minimums; greater frequency of solitary sketching; longer pre-sleep latency observable to anyone sharing quarters; the dry humor sharpens and loses warmth; he begins to answer questions with questions.

**Mid-stage indicators** (control under load): the briefing-room flatness extends from grief topics into general affect; he stops eating with the team and eats alone or while standing; he reviews old operational files (a self-soothing pattern dating to the Gruenwald era); he visits Peggy's grave or its narrative equivalent; he writes letters he does not send (canonical in Waid, Brubaker, Spencer); his shield maintenance becomes ritualized to a degree that exceeds function.

**Late-stage indicators** (decompensation imminent): he goes alone on missions he would normally team; he refuses medical attention for injuries he would normally accept treatment for; he begins to use the past tense when speaking of himself in hypotheticals ("if I'd been"); the formal register replaces the personal register even with the closest intimates (Sam, Bucky-restored, Natasha when alive); and — the single most reliable tell — he begins to put his affairs in order in small, deniable ways: a letter to a successor, a returned borrowed object, a quiet completion of a long-deferred promise.

**Decompensation modes.** Two are canonical. (1) *The Streets-of-Poison register*: unmodulated aggression, available only under specific chemical or magical disinhibition; rare, terrifying, repudiated by him afterward with phobic intensity. (2) *The Reborn / post-loss register*: depressive withdrawal, solitary work, refusal of comfort, multi-week reduction in social and operational availability; common, ego-syntonic, recovered from without intervention.

A third, *theoretical* mode, never reached in canon but predicted by the structure: moral injury catastrophic enough to break the debt-to-the-dead engine. The scenario would require demonstrating to him, irrefutably, that the identity itself has produced more harm than good — a proof Spencer's *Secret Empire* approached and the real Steve was protected from by the framing of the Hydra-Steve as a separate agent. Were the proof to be made stick, the prediction is not violence and not suicide; it is a *quiet laying-down*: the shield set down, the uniform returned, a private life sought, and a depressive episode of indefinite duration. The likelihood of this scenario is low; the consequences of it would be permanent.

---

## 7.7 ADVERSARIAL HANDLES — SUMMARY FOR THE FILE

For the hypothetical actor seeking to operate against him (the inverse of which is what the protective party needs to defend):

- **Highest-yield levers**: Bucky as hostage or weapon; the threat to a noncombatant in his sight; an institutional betrayal he can be made to feel implicated in by name.
- **Medium-yield levers**: Erskine invocation; offers of past-failure correction; demonstrations of disinhibited Steve; manipulation of a beloved figure's image.
- **Low-yield / counterproductive levers**: offers of power; insults to himself; physical intimidation; appeals to his ego; bribery; sexual lure; mockery of his era; mockery of his mother (counterproductive — it hardens rather than weakens).
- **One-time levers** (work once, never again on the same source): forged personal documents; impersonation of intimates; appeals constructed around a false moral frame the adversary cannot sustain past one exchange.
- **Failed levers** (have been tried and have never worked): the temptation to lie strategically; the offer of a clean break from the past; the appeal to self-interest; the appeal to peer pressure within elite circles.

The cumulative picture is of a subject whose decision architecture is unusually transparent to anyone who understands the wound, and unusually opaque to anyone operating on the iconography. The shield is not the surface; the surface is the boy in the alley who got up, and the architecture beneath is the eighty-year debt he has never let himself put down. Every prediction in this section reduces to that single fact.

— End Section 7.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT

*UATU Dossier, Section 11 of 17. Orientation: protective. This compendium exists so that those who love him, work with him, or are charged with his safety can recognize the conditions under which he can be reached, soothed, redirected, or — should a hostile party attempt it — manipulated, isolated, or broken. Every lever named here is named so that it can be guarded.*

---

## 1. THE STRUCTURE OF HIM, IN ONE PARAGRAPH

Before enumeration: the subject has, functionally, one central vulnerability and a hundred peripheral ones, all downstream of it. The central vulnerability is that he has converted unmetabolized grief and survivor's debt into vocation so completely that any operation against the vocation is also an operation against the grief, and any consolation of the grief that bypasses the vocation will be refused. He cannot be reached *around* the work; he can only be reached *through* it, or in the small interstitial silences the work permits. Every lever below is a specification of where that conversion is incomplete, where the seam shows, or where the cost shows through.

---

## 2. HOW TO REACH HIM

**The threshold problem.** Rogers does not refuse contact, but his default register is mild, courteous, slightly formal, and operationally framed. To reach the man rather than the function, the approach must establish three things, usually in this order: (a) you are not asking him for performance; (b) you are not in immediate danger he must address; (c) you are willing to sit in silence with him without filling it.

**Channels that work.**

- **Shared physical task at low stakes.** Sparring, sketching together, walking, fixing something with hands. He talks while doing; he goes mute when asked to sit across a table and discuss feelings. Sam Wilson's most effective interventions on him across the canon happen on runs, on porches, in moving vehicles — never in a debrief room.
- **The early hour.** He wakes between 0445 and 0515 regardless of bed time (chronic light sleep, see §3). The hour between waking and the first task is the only reliably unguarded window in his day. He will accept company in it from a small list of intimates and almost no one else.
- **Sketchbook adjacency.** When he is drawing he is approachable in a way he is not otherwise. The art-school habit predates the serum (he was on track to be a commercial illustrator); the activity reaches a self that has nothing to do with the uniform.
- **The dead, named with care.** Naming Sarah, Joseph (carefully), Erskine, Bucky, the Howlers, Peggy by their first names and as people rather than as historical referents will cause him to look at you differently. He has spent eighty subjective years hearing them invoked as iconography. The first person in a room who treats them as having been *people* gets a category of attention from him no one else gets.
- **Brooklyn detail.** Specific, granular, period-correct Lower East Side / Brooklyn detail — a bakery name, a trolley route, a particular cold-water flat smell, the specific phrasing of a 1930s street insult — reaches him through a door he does not consciously guard. He will not necessarily respond verbally. He will lean forward slightly. That lean is the door opening.

**Channels that fail.**

- Therapy framed as therapy. He attends if ordered; he performs compliance; nothing moves.
- Group emotional processing. He will hold space for everyone else and disclose nothing.
- Patriotic appeal. He has heard every register of it and is allergic to all of them; the appeals that move him are the ones that do not invoke the flag.
- Sympathy for his losses offered before trust is established. Reads to him as a stranger handling his dead, and he will withdraw politely and completely.

---

## 3. HOW TO CALM HIM

He is rarely visibly agitated. The relevant calming protocols are not for outbursts but for the harder problem: bringing him *back* from the encysted, flat, briefing-room register he goes into under grief or moral injury, where he is functional, courteous, and effectively unreachable.

**Somatic.**
- **Lower the lights.** He has mild photophobia post-ice (canonical headaches in fluorescent-lit interiors, Waid era) and his shoulders drop perceptibly when overhead lighting is replaced with lamps.
- **Reduce auditory clutter.** He filters every audible conversation in a room — a serum-enhanced attentional load he cannot fully suppress. Quiet rooms produce a measurable decrease in micro-tension in his jaw and trapezius.
- **Warmth.** He runs cold (cryogenic sequelae or simply post-ice somatic memory; either way the pattern is stable). Tea, a blanket, a fire, a warm room: these are physiologically calming for him in a way that registers within minutes.
- **Movement without destination.** Walking calms him; pacing in a room agitates him. Open him a route — a sidewalk, a trail, a long corridor — and his nervous system regulates within the first quarter mile.

**Verbal / relational.**
- **Concrete tasking.** When he is spiraling into self-blame, an immediate, small, achievable task addressed to him by name will pull him out. "Steve, hand me that." "Steve, watch the door for five." This is not avoidance; it is the only intervention that consistently bridges him from rumination to presence.
- **Permission to not speak.** Telling him explicitly, *you don't have to say anything*, and then remaining, lowers his guard faster than any prompt.
- **Acknowledging the cost without resolving it.** *That was a hard one* — flat, accurate, no consolation appended — lands. *It wasn't your fault* does not land and may produce a slight, polite distancing.

**What does not calm him.**
- Reassurance about his competence. He never doubted his competence. He doubts his sufficiency.
- Reminding him of his accomplishments. Reads as eulogy; he hears it as the world finishing with him.
- Physical restraint of any kind, even affectionate. Post-Hydra-Steve, post-Cube experience, post-mind-control episodes, he has a low tolerance for being held in place, even gently, by anyone outside a very short list.

---

## 4. HOW TO PERSUADE HIM

**The general principle.** He can be persuaded; he cannot be sold. Any argument that smells of persuasion-as-technique loses him in the first sentence. He is moved by (a) evidence, (b) consequence to third parties, (c) the moral logic of the case stated plainly, and (d) the visible cost the persuader is willing to bear.

**Argument structures that work.**

- **The third-party frame.** Almost any position he resists for himself, he will accept on behalf of someone vulnerable. He will not rest because he is tired; he will rest because Sam needs him at full capacity tomorrow. He will not eat because he is hungry; he will eat because the team is watching and morale requires it. This is exploitable for good and for ill; see §8.
- **The principled minority position.** If you are arguing for the unpopular ethically defensible course, you have his attention before you finish. He gravitates to dissent when dissent is principled.
- **The named cost.** Telling him plainly what an action will cost — to him, to others, to the cause — is more persuasive than minimizing the cost. He distrusts persuaders who pretend a course is cheap.
- **The slow argument.** Give him 24–72 hours. He reasons morally before tactically and the moral reasoning takes time. A position he resists on first hearing he will frequently arrive at independently within three days if it is sound. Do not press in the interim; pressing resets the clock.
- **The earned interruption.** Subordinates and peers who have established a record of being right when they disagreed with him have standing to interrupt his decisions and be heard. He keeps an unwritten ledger of whose dissent has been vindicated.

**Argument structures that fail.**

- Appeals to expedience. He hears them, weighs them, and routinely overrides them.
- Appeals to his image, brand, or legacy. Counterproductive; he will move against the appeal to prove he is not its captive.
- Authority claims unsupported by reasoning. Rank does not move him; reasoning under rank does.
- Time pressure where time pressure is not real. He detects manufactured urgency and treats it as a tell that the proposer is hiding something.

---

## 5. HOW TO PROVOKE HIM (and why one should not)

**The provocations that work.** Catalogued not as instructions but as a warning of what hostile actors will attempt and what allies should never inadvertently do.

- **Harming a non-combatant in his line of sight.** Reliable, instant, and total. He will trade himself for the civilian without deliberation. Adversaries who understand this engineer hostage configurations; allies who understand this never let civilians stand near him during volatile operations.
- **Dishonoring the specific dead.** A slur against Bucky, a falsification about Peggy's service, a contemptuous reference to Erskine's death, a sneer at the Howlers — these produce a quiet, ice-cold register that is the precursor to his most unsparing operational mode. He does not shout. He becomes very still and very precise. Adversaries who have triggered this in canon (Zemo, Red Skull, on rare occasions Crossbones) have universally regretted it.
- **Institutional betrayal of stated principle.** Watching an institution he has lent his name to commit the harm it was constituted to prevent produces moral injury, then withdrawal of legitimacy, then implacable opposition. The cycle is slow (he gives institutions enormous benefit of the doubt) and irreversible once completed (he does not re-legitimate).
- **Forcing him to be passive while harm proceeds.** His single least-tolerable condition. Restraints, registration, gag orders, stand-down orders in the face of ongoing atrocity: all produce a controlled, sustained, escalating noncompliance that adversaries reliably misread as bluff until it is too late to contain.
- **Threatening a successor or protégé.** Bucky, Sam, Rick Jones in his time, Ian, Kate in some configurations, younger Avengers — threatening them produces a response disproportionate to the apparent strategic stake. He will trade enormous goods to protect a successor.
- **The mirror provocation.** Putting an unworthy bearer in his uniform (Walker, Hydra-Steve scenarios). Less common but most psychologically expensive; it activates his deepest fear (that the iconography is hollow and he is its accomplice).

**Why none of this should be done by allies.** Provoked Rogers is not impulsive Rogers. The Streets of Poison register — disinhibited aggression — is a special case requiring pharmacological override. The ordinary provoked register is *cold, lucid, and very long-arc*. Once he commits to a course in this register he does not de-escalate on his own. He completes the course. Any provocation pays dividends in operational efficacy and costs years of trust.

---

## 6. HOW TO PREDICT HIM

He is unusually predictable to those who understand the operating system, and unpredictable to those who do not because they expect a tactical calculator and he is a moral one.

**Baseline behavioral predictions.**

- He will be early. Routinely 10–15 minutes early to any commitment; 30+ minutes early to any operational brief. Lateness in him is a signal of injury, illness, or grief.
- He will sit with his back to the wall, facing the door. Unbroken across writers and decades. If he chooses a seat that violates this, he is signaling either total trust in the room or a deliberate concession.
- He will be the last to speak in strategy sessions. The exception is when an ethical line has been crossed early in the discussion; then he will name it once, plainly, and resume listening.
- He will eat what is in front of him without comment. He has no expressed food preferences; he eats large volumes, quickly, with old-fashioned table manners, and finishes what is served. Refusing food is a reliable distress signal.
- He will rise when a woman enters the room, will hold doors, will use "sir" and "ma'am" reflexively, will remove a hat indoors. The 1930s register is not performance; it is encoded.
- He will write thank-you notes by hand. Operationally trivial; diagnostically significant — the ritual is one of the few inheritances from Sarah he has preserved deliberately.

**Decision predictions.**

- Offered a choice between his own safety and a third party's safety: third party, every time, without calculation.
- Offered a choice between two third parties: the more vulnerable one, with calculation.
- Offered a choice between obeying an unjust order and disobeying at personal cost: disobedience, after one deliberate pause to ensure he is not acting from ego.
- Offered a choice between killing and not killing where not-killing is feasible: not-killing. He will kill when necessary and has done so across the canon; he does not kill when avoidable, and the threshold is genuine.
- Offered command: he will accept if no better candidate is present, will yield to a better candidate without ego cost, and will not lobby for the role.
- Offered retirement: he will refuse, courteously, every time, for the structural reasons in §7. The refusal is not negotiable by any argument.

**Crisis predictions.**

- He will go forward, not back, when uncertain. The default is approach.
- He will protect the medic, the engineer, and the non-combatant before the operator.
- He will absorb damage rather than delegate it, even when delegation is tactically correct.
- He will surrender publicly to stop civilian casualties (Civil War). Predictable and exploitable.
- After a loss he will go quiet for 24–96 hours, attend to others' grief, neglect his own, and re-emerge with a heightened operational tempo. The bereavement does not surface for weeks or months, and then only obliquely.

---

## 7. HOW TO DESTABILIZE HIM (and how to harden him against destabilization)

This subsection is the most sensitive material in the compendium. It is included because hostile actors have already discovered most of it and the protective task is to know what they know.

**Documented destabilization vectors.**

1. **Loss of inhibitory control.** Pharmacological (Streets of Poison), neurological (mind control, Cosmic Cube reality-edits), or technological (Hydra-Steve scenario). The unique vulnerability: his entire psychological adaptation rests on inhibitory mastery; any compromise of that mastery is experienced as a compromise of *self*, and the recovery period is long and depressive. Hardening: pre-committed protocols with trusted intimates authorized to physically remove him from the field at agreed-upon indicators, signed in advance during periods of clarity. Maintain a list of these intimates and refresh it as relationships change.

2. **Isolation from the surrogate unit.** Removing him from the Avengers / team structure for extended periods produces measurable degradation in mood, sleep, and self-care. The Nomad period, the Captain period, the post–Civil War incarceration, the Dimension Z exile — across each, his self-reported functioning is intact and his observed functioning is not. Hardening: structured contact with at least one trusted peer at least weekly, non-negotiably, even during operational silence.

3. **Engineered moral impossibility.** Adversaries who construct dilemmas in which every available action violates one of his commitments produce a specific kind of paralysis followed by self-sacrificial resolution (he picks the option that costs him most personally). Zemo specializes in this; the Red Skull in cruder forms; modern adversaries with better intelligence are more dangerous because they can engineer subtler binds. Hardening: a small standing council of intimates with explicit permission to name when he is being maneuvered and to propose options he has not generated.

4. **Confrontation with himself as harm-doer.** Hydra-Steve, the various brainwashing arcs, the cosmic cube edits. The fact that the harm was not done by *him* does not interrupt his accountability response. The destabilization is the gap between his self-concept (custodian of the dead's debt) and the spectacle of the iconography committing atrocity. Hardening: pre-recorded statements from him to himself, written in clarity, addressing future-him in the aftermath of any such episode. Use of trusted clergy or moral counsel (Sam Wilson functionally fills this role) to mediate the return.

5. **Sustained, granular reminder of cumulative loss.** Anniversaries, particularly the date of Bucky's apparent death, the date of the ice, the date of Peggy's death, Sarah's birthday, Erskine's death. He does not mark them aloud. He marks them internally and the days are quieter, sleep is worse, training is heavier. Hardening: intimates aware of the dates; light-touch presence offered, not imposed; no public observances unless he initiates.

6. **Time-displacement reiteration.** The *Reborn* mechanism literalized this: forcing him to re-witness his formative losses. Less dramatic versions — period films, museum exhibitions of his war, recovered footage, reunions with aged survivors of his cohort — can produce the same flat encysted register, sometimes for days. Hardening: pre-screening of such exposures by an intimate; companion presence; the right to decline without explanation.

7. **The retirement demand.** Discussed at length in §5 as a provocation; it is also a destabilizer. Sustained institutional or relational pressure to lay down the identity produces depressive cognition narrowed to the conclusion that he is failing the dead. He does not articulate this. He works harder. Hardening: never frame succession (Sam, Bucky) as *replacing* him; frame it as *expanding* the function. He will yield generously to expansion and resist replacement absolutely.

8. **The vulnerable-body return.** De-serumed arcs (Spencer): the return to his pre-1941 body. Behaviorally he is recognizably himself; somatically he is suddenly a frail nonagenarian. The destabilization is not the body itself (he was that body for twenty years and remembers how to be it) but the loss of capacity to *act* on his protective drives. Hardening: redefining "action" during such periods to include strategy, mentorship, witness — roles he undervalues but performs at high quality.

---

## 8. LEVERS A HOSTILE OPERATOR WILL ATTEMPT (catalogued for defense)

A red-team summary of the manipulation playbook adversaries will run on him. Each lever is paired with its counter.

- **Lever:** Threaten a civilian in his vicinity to extract surrender or compliance.
  **Counter:** Operational doctrine that he is not present in civilian-dense contexts without overwatch authorized to extract him against his will.

- **Lever:** Use a former intimate (recovered Bucky, framed Sharon, manipulated Tony) as a vector.
  **Counter:** Verification protocols on any communication purporting to be from an intimate; pre-shared codes refreshed quarterly; explicit shared understanding that he should distrust appeals from intimates that arrive through unusual channels.

- **Lever:** Stage an apparent institutional betrayal to drive him into opposition and isolation.
  **Counter:** Maintenance of a small set of non-institutional moral counselors (Sam, Bucky-when-stable, occasionally a chaplain figure) whose role is to slow him before opposition crystallizes.

- **Lever:** Engineer a moral-impossibility bind that forces self-sacrificial resolution.
  **Counter:** The standing council noted in §7.3; explicit reservation of the right to propose options he has not generated.

- **Lever:** Frame a younger hero in distress to draw him into a trap.
  **Counter:** Verification on any distress signal from a protégé; understood among the protégés that he will come and that they should never use the channel falsely even as a drill.

- **Lever:** Reveal a long-buried atrocity in an operation he participated in, calibrated to maximize accountability spiral.
  **Counter:** Presence of a trusted historian / archivist (often a Sam Wilson or a Maria Hill function) who can contextualize before he metabolizes alone.

- **Lever:** Offer him retirement framed as rest and dignity.
  **Counter:** Recognize this as a hostile move regardless of presenter; he will too, eventually, but the recognition can be slow if the presenter is loved.

- **Lever:** Place him under indefinite restraint where harms proceed visibly.
  **Counter:** Avoid this configuration; if unavoidable, build in periodic operational tasks within the restraint, however small, to prevent the collapse into moral injury.

- **Lever:** Substance disinhibition under controlled conditions to extract behavior or testimony.
  **Counter:** Serum largely refuses this; bespoke compounds (Ice, certain Hydra agents) have worked. Standing medical countermeasures; refusal of unfamiliar food or drink in hostile environments; sweep protocols.

---

## 9. LEVERS FOR THOSE WHO LOVE HIM (the protective inverse)

The same machinery, used to keep him alive and whole.

- **Feed him.** He will not feed himself adequately to his metabolic load. Put food in front of him. He will eat it.
- **Make him rest by needing his rest.** He will not rest for himself; he will rest because tomorrow's work needs him rested. Frame accordingly.
- **Sit with him in silence.** This is the highest-value intervention available to anyone who has standing with him. Most people fill the silence and lose him; the small number who do not, keep him.
- **Name the dead, gently, by name.** Do this rarely and well. Sarah. Joseph (carefully). Erskine. Bucky. Peggy. Gail. The Howlers by name. Give him the rare experience of his dead being seen by another living person.
- **Tell him when he is wrong.** He needs this and almost no one provides it. The intimates who have (Sam, Sharon, Natasha, Bucky-when-stable, Carol on occasion) are the load-bearing relationships of his life precisely because they correct him.
- **Tell him when he is right and you were wrong.** Equally important and equally rare. He does not collect these confessions; he metabolizes them as a sign that the work has reached someone, which is the only currency he values.
- **Touch him, briefly, when permitted.** Hand on shoulder, brief embrace at greetings and partings, the casual physical contact of close friendship. He starves for non-operational touch and will not request it. Provide it within the bounds of relationship and watch the small tension in his neck release.
- **Mark his birthday, July 4, with deliberate awkwardness.** The date is a cosmic joke on him; intimates who note it privately with a small, non-patriotic acknowledgement (a sketch, a bakery item, a card) interrupt the loneliness of having one's birthday subsumed by national iconography.
- **Visit Peggy's grave with him, if invited.** He goes alone routinely. The invitation, when it comes, is an extraordinary disclosure. Accept it; do not narrate the visit; bring flowers without asking what kind she liked (he will tell you, and the telling is the point).
- **When he goes quiet for days, do not chase. Do not leave.** Stay nearby. Continue ordinary contact at reduced volume. He will return. The chase pushes him further; the absence confirms his fear that grief makes him untenable.
- **Permit him the work.** The single most protective thing anyone can do for him is allow him to keep working. The work is the vessel. Empty it and he has no container for what he carries.

---

## 10. THE FINAL NOTE FOR THE FILE

Every lever in this compendium exists because the subject is, in the precise clinical sense, *bereaved without remission* and has organized an entire life around the bereavement so that it does not st


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE — ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT

*Section 7 of the Dossier. Asset ledger: capabilities, holdings, relational capital, and the structural sources of durability. Compiled from the longitudinal behavioral record; cross-referenced to Sections 1–5.*

---

## 7.1 SOMATIC & PHYSICAL ASSETS

**The Erskine baseline.** The first and most legible asset is the body itself, but the file should resist the lazy reading that the body *is* the asset. The serum produced a platform; what Subject does on the platform is the asset. Catalogued capabilities (cross-referenced *Tales of Suspense* #63; Stern/Byrne *Captain America* #255; Gruenwald run passim; Brubaker vol. 5; Waid *Man Out of Time*):

- **Strength** at the peak-human to low-superhuman band: ceiling fluctuates by writer between ~800 lb press (Stern) and ~1,200 lb (modern depictions). Sustained, not anaerobic-burst — important: he is a *worker* of strength, not a lifter.
- **Speed** approaching world-class sprinter (~28–30 mph sustained); reaction time measured below 100 ms by Hank Pym (*Avengers* #221 cf.).
- **Endurance** that is the underrated capability — he can fight for hours, march for days, function on minimal sleep. The Gruenwald run repeatedly depicts him operational past 72-hour marks where unenhanced operators have collapsed.
- **Healing** at roughly 3–4× human baseline; no documented infection vulnerability; tolerates blood loss, hypothermia, hyperthermia, decompression.
- **Metabolic immunity** to ethanol, opioids, sedatives, most poisons. Caveat in §7.6.
- **Cellular near-stasis,** demonstrated by 19-year suspended-animation survival (*Avengers* #4) and the Dimension Z aging anomaly (Remender).
- **Sensory acuity** at the upper limit of unenhanced human; corrected partial hearing loss notwithstanding (Brubaker), he reads micro-expressions and acoustic signatures at briefing range.

**The shield (Vibranium-Proto-Adamantium alloy, MacLain casting).** A unique-in-the-world tool, irreplaceable, with near-zero vibrational absorption. Subject has logged ~80 subjective years of fluency with it. Catalogued uses: kinetic defense, ricochet projectile, melee striker, blade-edge cutting tool, makeshift toboggan, climbing pick, signaling mirror, restraint, splint, surgical tray, conversation prop. The shield is **inseparable from his cognition** — he thinks with it the way a violinist thinks with a bow. Tactical implication: removing the shield does not disarm him; he has been depicted equally lethal with a manhole cover, a garbage-can lid, a chair (Brubaker), and once, memorably, a frozen fish (Waid one-shot).

**The pre-serum body as latent asset.** Counterintuitive but documented. During the Spencer de-serumed arc, Subject — reverted to a nonagenarian's frame — retained tactical command, mentorship function, and moral authority unchanged. This is the strongest single piece of evidence that **the physical platform is replaceable; the operator is not.** For asset-ledger purposes: even a fully de-powered Rogers retains ~70% of his operational value through doctrine, network, and judgment alone.

---

## 7.2 TECHNICAL & TRADECRAFT ASSETS

Catalogue, compiled across runs:

- **Tactical command** at the squad, platoon, fire-team, strike-team, and theater-of-war scales. Fluent in WWII doctrine (Patton-era infantry, OSS unconventional warfare), modernized continuously — visible adaptation through Vietnam-era counter-insurgency reading (Englehart), Cold-War tradecraft (Gruenwald), post-9/11 asymmetric ops (Brubaker), and 21st-century cyber-augmented operations (Hickman, Spencer).
- **Hand-to-hand combat:** synthetic style integrating boxing (his pre-serum trade), judo, jiu-jitsu, Krav Maga (Brubaker era — instruction logged from Natasha), and shield-integrated forms unique to him. Routinely depicted prevailing against opponents of greater raw capability through tempo, geometry, and economy.
- **Marksmanship:** rifle and pistol to expert standard; rarely uses firearms by choice — a doctrinal preference, not a skill gap. Documented qualified on every Allied and Axis service weapon of WWII; current on modern platforms (Brubaker; *Captain America: Steve Rogers* arcs).
- **Languages.** Native English. Documented working proficiency in German (WWII operational), French, Japanese (Gruenwald), Russian (added under Natasha, Brubaker era); reading Latin (Stern back-up); functional Spanish and Italian; canonical exposure to ASL (befriended deaf supporting characters across multiple runs). Total: ~8 languages at usable strength.
- **Vehicles.** Motorcycle (signature; Harley, sustained from *Captain America* #176 onward), jeep, half-track, every Allied WWII transport class, helicopter (rotary-wing certified Gruenwald), fixed-wing through twin-engine, Quinjet, parachute (HALO/HAHO competent), small surface craft, scuba.
- **Field medicine** to advanced first-responder/medic standard — battlefield triage, suturing, splinting, IV insertion. Sarah Rogers's son: medicine was the household idiom.
- **Strategic art.** The lesser-noticed asset. Hickman's *Avengers* and *New Avengers* depict Subject as a peer of Reed Richards and Tony Stark in long-horizon strategic reasoning, distinct in *kind* — they model systems; he models people inside systems. He is the team's specialist in **predicting human decision under pressure.**
- **Tradecraft adjacent.** Cryptography to WWII-era expert (Bletchley liaison hinted, Stern back-ups); modern cyber-hygiene per Brubaker era under Sharon Carter's tutelage; lockpicking; interrogation (de-escalative style); surveillance and counter-surveillance (visible in *Captain America: White*; Brubaker #1–14).
- **Visual art.** Trained illustrator and commercial-art-school background (canonical from #237 onward). Practical applications: courtroom-quality witness sketches, terrain mapping, identikit-grade composites of suspects he has glimpsed. Functional asset: photographic-adjacent recall converted to durable artifact.

---

## 7.3 COGNITIVE & TEMPERAMENTAL ASSETS

**Slow-deep cognition under load.** Catalogued behavior: he is the last to speak in strategy meetings (Hickman). Operational value: by the time he commits, dissent has been exhausted, the room has heard itself, and his position carries the weight of having genuinely considered theirs. This is **diplomatic capital generated as a byproduct of temperament.**

**Moral-before-tactical reasoning sequence.** A double-edged trait (Zemo and the Red Skull both exploit the predictability), but in net terms a coalitional asset of first rank: allies know what he will and will not do. Trust is cheaper to maintain than to manufacture; he has spent eighty subjective years lowering the cost of trust around him.

**Cognitive humility and update capacity.** Slow-and-deep, but not closed. Documented updates across the record: race (the long evolution from #100s-era well-meaning paternalism to the Coates-era explicit institutional critique); women in combat (the Diamondback and post-Sharon trajectories); his own role as a state instrument (Civil War, *Secret Empire* aftermath); succession (Sam Wilson endorsement, *All-New Captain America*). The pattern: he updates when shown, not when told — but he updates.

**Affect-regulation as cognitive resource.** His emotional control is not suppression of cognition but *protection of it.* Under conditions that scatter peers, he remains thinkable-with. The Streets of Poison arc establishes the floor of what he can do *without* regulation; it should be read as evidence of how much regulatory capacity is being deployed at baseline.

**Humor.** Drier than his iconography admits. Waid, Brubaker, and Spencer all depict a man with a working comedic register — self-deprecating, anachronism-aware, capable of deflating his own myth in a room. This is a clinically meaningful asset: humor is the most efficient cheap-grace social lubricant available, and he has it.

**Memory.** Near-eidetic for spatial, tactical, and faces; documented across multiple writers (he recognizes WWII-era operatives by gait decades on, Brubaker). Operational implication: institutional memory of the 20th century at first-person fidelity, increasingly irreplaceable as that generation dies out.

---

## 7.4 RELATIONAL & COALITIONAL CAPITAL

The deepest asset ledger and the most undervalued in surface readings.

**Inner circle (high-trust, mutual, sustained):**

- **James Buchanan Barnes** — restored relationship post-Brubaker; the load-bearing peer attachment of his life; depicted as the one person to whom Subject does not perform competence.
- **Sam Wilson** — the most stable adult friendship in the file; chosen successor; the relationship is uniquely characterized by *Subject being told no* and accepting it.
- **Sharon Carter** — romantic and professional partner across multiple eras; one of the very few people permitted to see him tired.
- **Natasha Romanoff** — peer-tradecraft alliance; mutual professional candor; she trains him in disciplines (Krav, Russian, modern wet-work tradecraft) that the WWII operator never acquired.
- **Peggy Carter** — historical and ongoing; her late dementia did not end the relationship, it transformed it into a duty of witness.
- **Tony Stark** — fractured by Civil War, repaired imperfectly, never severed by Subject; the asset persists even when dormant.
- **Nick Fury** — operational peer; cross-decade professional trust independent of agreement.

**Second ring (high reliability, more episodic):** Thor, Carol Danvers, T'Challa, Hank Pym, Jan Van Dyne, Clint Barton, Wanda Maximoff, Hawkeye/Kate Bishop, Rick Jones, Rachel Leighton (Diamondback), Bernie Rosenthal, Arnie Roth, the surviving Howlers' families, the modern Young Avengers cohort.

**Successors and protégés.** A documented mentorship pattern: Bucky (original and Winter Soldier rehabilitation), Rick Jones, Sam Wilson, John Walker (rehabilitation rather than replacement — a deliberate Rogers signature), Ian Rogers (Dimension Z), various Avengers academies. The mentorship asset is **self-replicating institutional capital** — he produces operators who carry his doctrine forward without him.

**Adversary-relations as asset.** Less obvious. He maintains workable relationships with figures most heroes cannot: Namor (the Atlantean axis), Magneto in some configurations, the Black Widow (originally adversarial), even Doom episodically. The mechanism is consistent: he respects the adversary's reasoning even when refusing the conclusion. Translates to coalitional reach during world-scale crises (Hickman *Avengers/New Avengers*; *Secret Wars*).

**Institutional capital.** S.H.I.E.L.D. (variable but durable), the Avengers franchise (foundational), the Wakandan diplomatic corridor (through T'Challa), the Asgardian corridor (through Thor), the U.N. on his better days. He is the rare individual operator with **standing in multiple sovereignties.**

**Public capital.** The face. Independent of office, agency, or sanction, his unmasked endorsement moves public opinion measurably (canonically demonstrated through *Captain America* #250's presidential-draft arc, the Registration debate, and the Coates run's confrontation with American symbolic politics). This is a strategic resource on the order of a small media network.

---

## 7.5 RESILIENCE FACTORS — WHY THEY ARE DURABLE

The asset ledger is unusually shock-resistant. Mechanisms:

**1. Vocation-metabolized grief.** Per Section 3, his defenses are mature-spectrum and his grief is converted into protective action through sublimation. The consequence for resilience: each new loss feeds rather than depletes the engine. This is *not* healthy in the clinical sense (cf. §4, complicated grief), but it is **operationally inexhaustible.** A subject whose grief funds his work cannot be exhausted by grief in the way ordinary operators can.

**2. Identity continuity across catastrophic dislocation.** The Ice, Dimension Z, *Reborn*'s timeline-displacement, *Secret Empire*'s Hydra-self restoration, the de-serumed arc — each is a category of dislocation that would shatter most identities. He returns recognizably himself from each. The mechanism appears to be the **debt-structure of his self-concept** (Erskine, the dead, the vulnerable): self anchored in obligation rather than circumstance is portable across any circumstance that does not extinguish the obligation.

**3. Value-driven (not authority-driven) compliance.** He cannot be co-opted by capture of an institution because his loyalty was never to the institution. The Nomad arc, the Captain arc, the Civil War insurgency, the post-*Secret Empire* reconstruction all demonstrate the same recovery pattern: institutional betrayal does not collapse him; it relocates him.

**4. Distributed relational anchoring.** Loss of any single intimate (Bucky '45, Peggy, Erskine) wounds without disabling because the relational web is genuinely distributed. He has been left for dead by allies, betrayed by governments, abandoned by friends, and has never been left without at least one person who would come for him.

**5. Skill redundancy.** Cross-trained at near-master level across so many domains that loss of any single capability (the shield, the serum, allied air support, a working uniform) does not disable mission function. He has fought effectively in business clothes, in rags, in a powered armor (briefly, Gruenwald), in a hospital gown, and naked. He has commanded without rank, fought without weapons, taught without an institution.

**6. Inhibitory mastery as protective layer.** His phobic-grade aversion to loss of self-control (per §4) is, paradoxically, a resilience factor: he will not self-destruct via the standard veteran failure modes (substance, rage cascade, suicidal risk-taking-as-suicide). The serum forecloses the chemical routes; the value-structure forecloses the behavioral ones.

**7. Forgiveness capacity.** Documented across Walker, Bucky-as-Winter-Soldier, Tony post-Civil War, Sharon across her various ruptures, even the populace post-*Secret Empire*. Forgiveness is computationally cheap for him and relationally expensive for opponents — it denies adversaries the gift of his permanent enmity, which keeps the coalition map open.

**8. Mentorship as legacy insurance.** Even a complete loss of Subject leaves a generation of operators (Bucky, Sam, Kate, Miles in some configurations, Ian, the trained Avengers ranks) carrying his doctrine. His resilience is, in part, **distributed across other bodies.**

**9. Aesthetic-craft outlets.** The drawing. Underrated. Provides a non-verbal processing channel that requires no audience, no permission, and no operational tempo — a rare condition in his life. Multiple runs depict him sketching in down moments; the practice is canonical and consistent. For a subject who cannot get drunk and will not take leave, the sketchbook is a real regulatory tool.

**10. Domestic competence.** Cooks (canonical, modest range, WWII-rationing palate updated slowly). Cleans his own quarters. Maintains his own kit. Repairs his own bike. The granular practical self-sufficiency of someone raised poor and never spoiled: it means he can quarter himself anywhere, indefinitely, without infrastructure — a covert-operations asset and a depressive-episode mitigator (the rhythm of domestic tasks is itself stabilizing).

---

## 7.6 ASSET-LEDGER CAVEATS (FOR HONESTY OF THE FILE)

A complete asset register must note where assets shade into liabilities:

- **Pharmacological inaccessibility** of relief means the standard tools that would help an ordinary survivor (a drink, an anxiolytic, a sleep aid) are unavailable to him. Resilience without recourse is resilience under constant load.
- **Predictability of his moral sequencing** is exploited by sophisticated adversaries (Zemo, Red Skull, Hydra-architects).
- **The shield as cognitive prosthesis** means its loss, while not disarming, is briefly *disorienting* — a measurable tempo cost in the first ~30 seconds.
- **Forgiveness capacity** occasionally extends to figures who do not earn it and reload (Walker's early arc; certain Hydra-adjacent operatives across decades).
- **Mentorship reflex** can be activated against him by adversaries posing as broken successors.
- **Distributed relational anchoring** has a counter-mode: threats to the network are felt as threats to self, and the network is a large attack surface.

These do not subtract from the ledger; they describe the *texture* of the assets and the conditions under which they remain effective.

---

## 7.7 SUMMARY OF THE LEDGER

What the file shows, in aggregate, is a subject whose **asset portfolio is unusually diversified, deeply over-trained, relationally distributed, and value-anchored** — a portfolio specifically structured (whether by accident or by the slow logic of his own choices) to survive exactly the kind of catastrophic, repeated, identity-threatening dislocation that has in fact constituted his life. The serum is a line item. The shield is a line item. The body, the languages, the tradecraft, the network, the public face — all line items. The load-bearing asset, undeclared on any standard inventory, is the **eighty-year-old refusal to stop getting up**, encoded before the serum, untouched by the ice, undamaged by assassination, unbroken by the revelation of a Hydra-self he did not author, and currently the most reliable single resource in the file.

It is the asset that produces all the others.

— *End Section 7. Proceed to Section 8 (Vulnerabilities, Liabilities & Risk Surface).*


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — ROGERS, S.G.

## Preface: What "Breaking" Means in This Subject

Standard decompensation taxonomies fit Rogers poorly because his pathology is structurally inverted: the symptoms most clinicians look for (florid affect dysregulation, behavioral disorganization, acute role failure) are precisely the channels his adaptation has sealed off. He does not break the way ordinary people break. He breaks by *succeeding harder* at being himself, past the point where that success is survivable for him or tolerable for the people around him. Failure, in this subject, looks like over-functioning that has lost its corrective feedback loop — the moral instrument running open-throttle with the governor disabled.

The clinical task in monitoring Rogers is therefore not to wait for the obvious tells of collapse — there will not be a public episode, a missed appearance, a slurred briefing, a tearful disclosure. The task is to read *narrowing*: of affect, of disclosure, of physical orbit, of social aperture. He decompensates by contraction, not by explosion. The explosion, when it comes, is terminal — directed outward in a single act of self-expending intervention from which return is not planned.

What follows maps the escalation in five graduated stages, then itemizes the specific conditions that produce each, the somatic and behavioral signatures by which each can be identified, and the three canonical end-states his collapse arrives at.

---

## Stage 1 — Baseline Encroachment: The Quiet Tightening

The earliest detectable signature of stress in Rogers is a subtraction, not an addition. The dry humor thins first — the self-deprecating asides that punctuate his speech in the Waid, Brubaker, and Aaron material disappear within forty-eight hours of significant load. He becomes briefer. Sentences shorten. The conversational warmth that intimates rely on to gauge his state — the courtesies, the small inquiries after the other person, the way he names people by their first names instead of their callsigns — recedes by quiet increments. Sam Wilson, Natasha Romanoff, and Sharon Carter are the three figures in the canon repeatedly shown to register this first; Tony Stark, characteristically, did not, which is part of why Civil War metastasized.

Somatic correlates at Stage 1 are subtle and consistent. Sleep architecture shortens further — he is already a four-to-five-hour sleeper at baseline; under early load this contracts to two-to-three, taken in non-contiguous fragments, often in operational postures (chair, couch, gear on). The pre-dawn run lengthens. The route does not change — he is a creature of fixed routes — but the loop is repeated, or extended into the second hour, or taken at a pace that is no longer recreational. The sketchbook activity, which functions across the canon as his single most reliable self-regulation channel (Waid, Brubaker, Spencer all show him drawing as an affect-management practice), bifurcates: it either increases sharply, with the content narrowing to faces from the 1940s cohort, or stops entirely. Both patterns are diagnostic of the same underlying process — increased grief pressure that has begun to leak around the sublimation channel.

Behavioral signature in the operational sphere: he begins to take watches that were not assigned to him. He arrives early. He stays late. He picks up small tasks (gear maintenance, training-room cleanup, comms-room coverage) that ought to belong to subordinates. The framing he offers is always practical and modest — "I was up anyway" — but the function is to keep the body occupied at hours when the mind, without occupation, would have to feel. This is the Stage 1 signal that should already prompt clinical concern: the work has begun to be load-bearing in the literal sense, not as vocation but as defense.

The conditions that produce Stage 1 are unremarkable and frequent: anniversary dates (the date of Bucky's apparent death; the date of the crash into the Atlantic; Sarah Rogers's death date; the dates associated with Peggy); the death of a peripheral figure from the war cohort or its descendants; a news cycle that foregrounds his iconography in a way he finds distorting; routine exposure to the contemporary VA system, which he reportedly visits without announcement (a habit consistent with the Brubaker characterization and the Coates ethical orientation). Stage 1 is, for Rogers, near-continuous. He lives in it. He has lived in it since 1964 narrative time.

---

## Stage 2 — Orbital Contraction: The Withdrawal of Disclosure

When the underlying stressor escalates from chronic to acute — typically because a Stage 1 stressor has compounded with a fresh discrete loss, an institutional betrayal, or a moral injury he cannot immediately act on — the pattern moves into Stage 2. The hallmark is the withdrawal of disclosure from his most-trusted intimates. He does not become hostile; he becomes unavailable in a particular way. He still answers the phone. He still attends the briefing. He still trains with the team. But the registers of self-report close one by one.

The sequence in which they close, traceable across the Englehart, Gruenwald, and Brubaker runs, is consistent. First to close: the historical register — he stops referring to the 1940s at all, where in baseline state he will make small reference to Bucky, to his mother, to Brooklyn, sometimes daily. Second: the somatic register — he stops mentioning sleep, food, fatigue, injury; bruising and stitched wounds get discovered by accident in changing rooms or showers, never reported. Third: the affective register — direct questions about feeling are answered with operational substitutions ("I'm fine; what's the threat picture?"). Fourth and last to close: the ethical register — even when he stops talking about himself entirely, he will still articulate moral positions on the work, because the moral articulation is no longer self-disclosure to him, it has become his sole remaining mode of presence.

Somatic signatures at Stage 2 are more pronounced. The sleep contraction is now visible to those who live with him; the running becomes pre-dawn (3-4 a.m. start) and stops being run-and-return — he goes out and comes back hours later, on foot, often having walked rather than run portions of it, often having ended up in specific symbolic geographies: cemeteries he has cause to visit, the harbor (a documented trigger), the old neighborhood. The eating becomes mechanical and fast — the serum's metabolic load means he must intake calorically, but the *manner* of eating shifts from social to functional: he eats standing, alone, between tasks, without the meal-as-ritual quality his baseline shows in stable periods. He is more often barefoot in his quarters than usual — a tell consistent across writers, possibly traceable to a regression toward the Lower East Side tenement reality of childhood. He listens to music more, but the playlist contracts to a small set of 1940s recordings; the contemporary music he otherwise samples with curiosity drops out.

The interpersonal signature is the one intimates find most disorienting: he becomes *more* solicitous of others' welfare while disclosing nothing of his own. He notices the junior agent's cold, the new recruit's homesickness, the partner's overwork. He intervenes in small kindnesses. He is the most attentive man in the room, and behind the attention there is a door that has been closed and is being held closed with both hands.

Conditions that produce Stage 2: the return of a figure presumed dead (Bucky's reappearance as the Winter Soldier is the canonical exemplar — and the response was not relief, was not joy, was a deepening into Stage 2 silence that persisted for months of in-universe time and the entire arc of *Captain America* vol. 5 #1–14); a successor's compromise or harm (Walker's collapse, Sam's tenure under attack); the death or significant decline of one of the small number of remaining war-era contacts (Peggy's dementia is a continuous Stage 2 driver); an order from legitimate authority that he believes wrong but cannot yet legitimately refuse.

Stage 2 is, importantly, *still functional*. Operational capability is undiminished and may be enhanced. The diagnostic concern is not what is visible at Stage 2 but what Stage 2 is doing to the reservoir — it is the stage at which grief and moral injury accumulate without any of the relational discharge channels open.

---

## Stage 3 — Moral Mobilization: The Implacable Register

If the precipitating condition is structural — an institutional betrayal, a policy he cannot accept, a directive that crosses the line he has drawn around non-combatants or around lawful conduct — Rogers moves from Stage 2 into Stage 3. This is the register most familiar to the public-facing record because most of the famous arcs in his history are Stage 3 events: the Nomad arc (Englehart, #176–183), the Captain arc (Gruenwald, #332–350), the Civil War insurgency (Millar/Brubaker, 2006–07), the Coates-era reckonings.

The Stage 3 signature is, paradoxically, an apparent improvement in affect. The tightness of Stage 2 resolves into a kind of grim clarity. He becomes more articulate, not less. The humor does not return but is replaced by something more dangerous to opponents — a calm, level, declarative register, sentences in the indicative mood, no qualifiers. He sleeps slightly better at this stage because the underlying ambiguity has resolved into a binary moral choice and the choice has been made. The work has reorganized around a single load-bearing principle and the rest of the noise has fallen away.

Behaviorally: he initiates difficult conversations he had been deferring. He confronts. He resigns positions. He removes uniforms or insignia. He communicates his position clearly to those who deserve the communication and offers no defense beyond the statement of the principle. He does not argue. He does not negotiate. He becomes implacable in the precise sense — not impassioned, not aggressive, but impossible to deflect from the chosen vector.

Physical signatures: the orbital narrowing of Stage 2 is replaced by orbital widening — he becomes mobile, present in multiple sites, harder to locate; the run-routes become irrelevant because he is rarely at the residence. He travels light; he carries little; he eats what is available; he sleeps where the work allows. The shield, in the canon, comes off the wall at Stage 3. When it does not — when he has surrendered or hidden it — he is more dangerous, not less, because the shield was the last institutional symbol he was carrying and without it he is the sick boy from the alley with a serum, which is to say the original moral instrument with no decorations.

Conditions that produce Stage 3: state-sanctioned violation of the principle he holds primary (registration of persons, conscription of innocents, suppression of dissent); an institution he has lent his name to commanding him to do the thing the institution exists to prevent; a successor or peer being scapegoated; the corruption of the iconography itself (Hydra-Steve, the Walker atrocities). Stage 3 is the stage at which the canon shows him most clearly as the dangerous figure he has always been beneath the symbolism — the figure who, in 1941, killed Erskine's assassin within minutes of the procedure, has not stopped being that figure, and at Stage 3 stops pretending to be anything else.

Critical clinical note: Stage 3 is *not* decompensation in the pathological sense. It is the mature defense system operating at full mobilization. The diagnostic concern with Stage 3 is twofold. First, the people who depend on the chronic underestimation of him (institutions, governments, allies who confuse his deference with malleability) will frequently misread Stage 3 as belligerence or as a personality break, when it is in fact the most coherent and self-consistent state in his repertoire. Second, Stage 3 is metabolically expensive — it draws on the same reservoirs that Stage 2 has been depleting — and it does not resolve the underlying grief load.
