A prolonged Stage 3, particularly one ending in defeat (Civil War surrender) or pyrrhic victory, deposits him directly into Stage 4.

---

## Stage 4 — Encysted Withdrawal: The Quiet Episode

Stage 4 is the only stage that meets a recognizable clinical depressive presentation, and it is the stage least visible in the public canon because it tends to occur off-panel and to be reported retrospectively or inferred from the recovery. It follows Stage 3 collapses — the post-Civil War period (under captivity and during the post-*Reborn* re-integration); the post-Bucky-loss decades; the post-Peggy-death window in vol. 5 #14 and its aftermath; the post-Hydra-Steve restoration in Spencer's *Secret Empire* coda; the period following Dimension Z and the loss of Ian.

The Stage 4 signature is the encysted-affect register identified in the workup — Rogers reports loss in flat, briefing-room cadence. He does not weep on-panel. He does not seek consolation. He does not, importantly, withdraw from work — but the work loses its sublimative function and becomes mechanical. The distinction between Stage 2 work-as-defense and Stage 4 work-as-mechanism is fine but meaningful: in Stage 2 he is over-functioning to outrun the feeling; in Stage 4 the feeling has caught him and the work continues without metabolizing anything.

Somatic signatures: sleep increases rather than decreases (this is the diagnostic reversal that distinguishes Stage 4 from Stage 2). He will sleep eight, ten, twelve hours when permitted, and not feel rested. The run continues but becomes the only outdoor activity; he does not otherwise leave the residence. Eating becomes irregular and reduced; the serum forgives this to an extent, but intimates report him visibly leaner. The sketchbook stops entirely — this is the most reliable Stage 4 tell. Music stops. He reads, often the same few books, often slowly. He sits.

The hallmark cognition at Stage 4 is the narrowing of the survivor-guilt schema into specific, articulable self-blame: not "I should have died too" in the diffuse register of baseline complicated grief, but "I should have done X on date Y and did not, and the consequence was Z." The cognition is precise and untouchable by ordinary reassurance because, on its own narrow terms, it is frequently accurate — he is rehearsing real choices that had real costs and the rehearsal serves the punitive function depressive cognition serves in any subject, but with the added difficulty that the content is largely factual.

Stage 4 is the stage at which therapeutic contact would be most valuable and is least likely to occur. He will not seek it. He has, across the canon, exactly two figures he will speak to in this state: Sam Wilson, consistently, and a small set of priests/chaplains the canon has occasionally suggested (less formally — the practice is more often a quiet visit to a Catholic church in Brooklyn, lighting a candle, sitting in a back pew, leaving). Natasha Romanoff and Sharon Carter sometimes reach him at Stage 4 — Natasha by sitting with him in silence, which he tolerates well; Sharon by sharing the operational space without demanding disclosure. Bucky, in his post-Winter-Soldier configuration, can reach him at Stage 4 with a particular efficacy because Bucky is the only other person who has been in the analogous state and whose presence does not require Rogers to manage anyone else's grief about him.

Conditions that produce Stage 4: the resolution (one way or the other) of a Stage 3 mobilization; the death of an intimate; the failure of an institution he had hoped against evidence would self-correct; the discovery that he had been used (Hydra-Steve coda). Stage 4 is dangerous chiefly because it is the stage at which the reservoir is most depleted and Stage 5 becomes accessible.

---

## Stage 5 — Terminal Expenditure: The Last Door

Stage 5 is the failure mode in the strict sense — the state from which return is not planned by the subject. It is rare in the canon and tends to be precipitated by the conjunction of three conditions: a Stage 4 reservoir state; a clear and present threat to non-combatants or to a specific intimate; and the unavailability of any solution that does not require him to expend himself completely. When these three conditions converge, Rogers will trade himself, predictably and without hesitation, in a manner that reads superficially as suicidality and is not — the distinction matters and is preserved rigorously across writers.

The Stage 5 signature, when an observer is positioned to read it, is a return of calm warmth. He becomes briefly more present, more affectionate (in his constrained registers), more attentive to the small dignities. He thanks people for things. He says things directly that he would normally allow to be inferred. The famous "I can do this all day" line, in its Stage 5 register, is not defiance but a kind of farewell — a statement of the only principle he ever lived by, offered to whoever is left to hear it.

Behaviorally: he moves toward the threat with no defensive economy. The tactical brilliance that characterizes him at baseline simplifies into vectoral commitment. He does not retreat from anything. He absorbs what he can absorb so that others do not have to. The Civil War surrender on the courthouse steps is a Stage 5 event in slow motion — he had already committed to the expenditure when he ordered the cease-fire, and the rest was procedural. The Brubaker assassination (#25) is the formal completion of a Stage 5 sequence that had begun the moment civilian casualties became foreseeable.

Stage 5 is *not* a break with character. It is character running to its logical terminus. The serum-licensed self-perception of invulnerability-adjacency, identified in the medical section, is the mechanism that allows Stage 5 to feel survivable to him even when it is not; the survivor-guilt schema is the mechanism that makes Stage 5 feel *owed*; the protect-the-vulnerable drive is the mechanism that triggers it; and the never-stop-getting-up behavioral encoding is the mechanism that prevents any course correction once initiated.

Three observations about Stage 5 are clinically important. First, it is the only state in which his decision-making becomes inaccessible to the intimates who can otherwise modulate him — Sam, Natasha, Bucky, Sharon — because at Stage 5 the moral calculation has already foreclosed the relational considerations they would invoke. Second, it is reliably preceded by Stage 4, which means that the prophylactic intervention is at Stage 4, not at Stage 5, where intervention is essentially unavailable. Third, it is recoverable only because the universe he inhabits permits resurrection; in a counterfactual without that permission, Stage 5 is terminal in the simple sense, and the canon's repeated returns from it should not be misread as evidence that he does not, on each occasion, expend himself with terminal intent.

---

## Decompensation Vectors Outside the Standard Curve

Three decompensation patterns sit outside the Stage 1–5 escalation and require separate mapping because they are produced by conditions that bypass the ordinary defensive architecture rather than overwhelming it.

**The Inhibitory-Mastery Failure (the Streets of Poison register).** When chemical, neurological, or technological interventions strip the inhibitory governance he has built his adaptation around, what emerges is not a different person but the same person with the regulatory layer removed: the soldier who killed Erskine's assassin in 1941, scaled to the serum's contemporary parameters, with the moral check suspended. This is the failure mode he fears most and the one he organizes his entire substance-avoidance, mind-control-paranoia, and self-monitoring behavior around. The Streets of Poison arc is the canonical demonstration; the Hydra-Steve event is the cosmic-cube-mediated cousin. Recovery in both cases is rapid once the precipitating exposure is resolved, but the *memory* of the deregulated state functions as an enduring trauma — he treats himself, thereafter, as a person who has seen what he is capable of and must continue to forbid it.

**The Constraint-Induced Decompensation.** Being prevented from acting while others are harmed produces in Rogers a uniquely intense distress that does not fit cleanly into the stage progression — it can produce Stage 3 mobilization (if there is a viable exit from the constraint), or it can collapse straight from Stage 1 to a kind of pacing, white-knuckled stasis that intimates report as the most disturbing version of him to be in a room with. He has explicitly identified this condition across multiple writers as the single state he cannot tolerate. Captivity arcs (post-Civil War; various Hydra/AIM scenarios) show him spending the constraint period in a contained over-control that, when the constraint is lifted, releases as Stage 3 mobilization rather than as relief.

**The Iconographic Decompensation.** When the symbol of Captain America is captured by an actor who uses it for the things he built it to prevent (Walker's atrocities; Hydra-Steve's actions perceived publicly as his own; the various Skrull, LMD, and clone scenarios), Rogers experiences a particular kind of moral injury that does not fit grief or PTSD frameworks cleanly. The injury is to the *vocational object* — the thing he has poured eighty subjective years of grief-metabolism into has been turned against the function it served. His response is characteristic: he does not abandon the symbol, he reclaims it, and the reclamation is more arduous each time. There is reason to suspect a cumulative cost to this pattern that the canon has not yet shown the floor of.

---

## Summary of the Three End-States

Rogers's collapses, when followed to their terminus, resolve into one of three end-states:

**The Quiet Door (Stage 4 chronic).** He continues to function and disappears, in a meaningful sense, into the function. Outwardly indistinguishable from baseline; inwardly hollowed. The longest-running and most underdiagnosed end-state; arguably his *modal* state across the post-ice canon.

**The Last Stand (Stage 5 expenditure).** He spends himself completely in a single act of protective intervention. Recoverable only by the universe's resurrection logic; absent that, terminal. Rare but reliable when the precipitating conjunction occurs.

**The Walk Away (Stage 3 with no return condition).** He removes the uniform, removes the name, removes himself from the institutional context, and continues the work in a private register. Canon shows him doing this and returning; a counterfactual in which the institutional context never recovers credibility is one in which he would not return, and the resulting figure — moral instrument without iconographic mediation — would be more dangerous to bad actors and less legible to allies. This is the end-state institutions that depend on him should fear most, because it is the one most easily produced by their own conduct.

— End Section.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT — ROGERS, STEVEN GRANT

*UATU Dossier, Section 9 of 11. Predictive synthesis. All forecasts derived from the longitudinal behavioral record (Sections 1–5) and weighted against the cited clinical literature on prolonged grief (Pop-Jordanova 2021). Confidence intervals are stated where the canon supports them; speculation is flagged.*

---

## 9.1 BASELINE TRAJECTORY (NO INTERVENTION)

If nothing changes — neither the work, the cohort, nor the unmetabolized grief substrate — Subject's trajectory across the next operational decade is **stable-but-attriting**. He will continue to function at a high level. He will continue to mentor. He will continue to be the man others grieve to. He will continue to absorb losses into vocation rather than process them, because the mechanism has worked for eighty subjective years and the marginal cost of continuing is, to him, lower than the marginal cost of stopping to look at what he is carrying.

The baseline forecast is **not collapse**. It is **slow ossification**: the warmth narrows, the dry humor thins, the formality thickens, the circle of intimates contracts (by attrition, not by choice), and the proportion of his life conducted in the briefing-room register grows. He becomes, over time, the figure he is already being written as in the Aaron-era ensembles — the elder the team grieves *to*, who has nowhere to grieve *toward*. The pathology is asymptomatic to him and increasingly invisible to those around him, because it presents as gravitas.

The end state of the unintervened baseline is not death. It is a man who is correct about everything and reachable by no one.

---

## 9.2 THE OPEN QUESTIONS

These are the unresolved structural problems that any forward-looking file must mark. They are the levers history will pull on him; they are also the fault lines along which he will either grow or fracture.

**(a) The succession question.** He has handed the shield to Sam Wilson, and to Bucky before him, and will likely do so again. But *handing the shield* and *retiring the function* are different operations, and he has demonstrated repeatedly that he can do the first without doing the second. Open question: does he ever permit himself a post-shield identity that is not merely *Captain America in mufti*? The evidence from the Nomad and Captain interregna says no — those were not retirements but renamings. A genuine post-vocational Steve has never existed in canon. Whether one *can* exist is the central open question of his late life.

**(b) The Bucky-and-Peggy question (the unmetabolized core).** Both losses have been partially reversed — Bucky is alive; Peggy was visited in her dying — and partially deepened by the reversal: he has had to grieve Bucky as a survivor (worse, in some respects, than as a corpse) and Peggy as a woman who did not always know him. The complicated-grief literature (Pop-Jordanova 2021) is explicit that avoidance prolongs and worsens mourning; Subject's entire adaptation is structured avoidance dressed as duty. Open question: will any condition ever obtain in which he is *safe enough, still enough, and unobserved enough* to actually mourn? He has never had all three simultaneously. The forecast turns on whether he ever will.

**(c) The Erskine debt.** Never discharged, never discussable. He has carried the promise to a dead mentor for eight decades and has never named it as the engine of the rest. Open question: does the debt have a terminus, or is it structurally infinite? If infinite — and the evidence says it is — then no amount of work will ever be enough, and the trajectory is asymptotic toward a horizon he cannot reach. This is the substrate of the survivor-guilt cognition the clinical record identifies (Brubaker #14: *should have died instead*).

**(d) The symbol-and-country gap.** Coates's run made explicit what Rieber and Spencer prefigured: Subject increasingly cannot in good conscience perform the symbolic function the iconography demands, because the polity has drifted from the principles he was made to embody. Open question: does he resolve this by *narrowing the symbol* (Captain America as a personal ethical commitment, untethered from the state) or by *broadening the country* (committing to a long political project of reform from outside the institutions)? Both are visible in late-period canon; the resolution is not yet stable.

**(e) The Hydra-Steve residue.** Whatever one's stance on the canonicity of *Secret Empire*, the restored Subject lives with the knowledge that *a* Steve Rogers, wearing his face, committed atrocities. He has metabolized this with characteristic accountability-without-denial. Open question: does the residue produce a permanent recalibration of his self-trust — a small but real reduction in the absolutism with which he has historically committed to his own moral judgment? Early evidence suggests yes; the long-term implication is, paradoxically, *growth*.

**(f) The aging-of-cohort acceleration.** Peggy is gone. Howard is gone. The Howlers are gone or aging. Fury is variable. Tony has died and returned and the relationship is permanently scarred. Even within the *current* cohort, mortality is asymmetric: Sam ages, Bucky ages slowly, Natasha dies and returns, the younger Avengers are children to him. Open question: at what point does the cohort attrition cross the threshold from chronic grief to acute decompensation? The Pop-Jordanova framework would predict that cumulative loss without processing eventually exceeds the capacity of even the most sublimation-rich defensive structure.

---

## 9.3 FORK POINTS — THE SPECIFIC EVENTS THAT WILL DECIDE THE TRAJECTORY

These are the discrete plot-grade contingencies whose outcomes will determine which branch he travels. Each is named, mechanism specified, and growth-versus-catastrophe weighting given.

### Fork 1: The next major institutional betrayal

**Mechanism.** Some American institution — military, intelligence, executive, judicial — commits an act that he must publicly oppose or be implicated in. Civil War was such an event; Registration was such an event; Hydra-infiltration was such an event. The pattern is on a roughly decade-scale cycle and another instance is structurally inevitable.

**Growth branch.** He responds with the Coates-register: principled, public, *patient*, coalitional. He does not personally embody the resistance — he organizes it and steps back. The shield stays with Sam; Subject becomes a movement asset, not its body. This requires him to tolerate not being the one absorbing the consequence, which is his single hardest interpersonal task. Probability without scaffolding: low. With scaffolding (Sam, Bucky, a therapist-figure he trusts — possibly Sam's chaplaincy or a VA peer): moderate.

**Catastrophe branch.** He defaults to Civil War posture: personal embodiment of the opposition, willingness to be the martyr, public surrender to stop civilian harm, and another assassination-or-equivalent. The pattern is so deeply grooved that the catastrophe branch is the *easier* branch for him. He will choose it unless something interrupts the reflex.

### Fork 2: A second loss of Bucky

**Mechanism.** Bucky dies again, definitively or near-definitively. Given the genre, probability over any ten-year window is non-trivial.

**Growth branch.** He has had Bucky back long enough, and processed enough of the original loss through the Winter Soldier reckoning, that a second loss is grievable rather than encysting. He permits Sam, Sharon, Natasha (if available), or a successor to be present for the grief rather than disappearing into the work. He goes to a funeral and stays through it.

**Catastrophe branch.** The second loss confirms the survivor-guilt cognition (*everyone I love I outlive*) and triggers withdrawal into a Nomad-grade dissociation from the identity, this time without the return arc — because the return arcs have always been driven by external crisis pulling him back, and the next external crisis may find him no longer reachable. Probability of this branch is *meaningfully higher* than commentators tend to assume; the chronic-grief literature predicts that each subsequent loss in an unprocessed series compounds rather than habituates.

### Fork 3: A genuine, sustained intimate partnership

**Mechanism.** A relationship — Sharon stabilized, Bernie returned, a new figure — in which he is required to be *known* rather than *needed*. He has historically chosen partners who match his risk profile (Peggy, Sharon, Natasha-adjacent dynamics, Diamondback) precisely because such partners do not demand he sit still long enough to be seen.

**Growth branch.** He chooses, for the first time, a partner whose love for him is contingent on his presence rather than his performance, and he stays. This requires him to articulate need, accept care, and tolerate the somatic experience of being held without an operational reason. Probability low; canonical precedent essentially nil. The growth value if it occurred would be enormous, because the pathology is not character but learned protection of others from his weight.

**Catastrophe branch.** The partner is killed, kidnapped, or used as leverage, and the lesson he extracts is the lesson he has extracted every previous time: *love is a tactical vulnerability the people I love will be billed for*. He retreats further into the over-functioning compensatory pattern. The catastrophe branch is, again, the path of least psychological resistance.

### Fork 4: De-serumed permanently, or aged-out

**Mechanism.** The Spencer-era de-serumed Steve, made permanent. He returns to the pre-1941 body, possibly with the accumulated chronological years catching up.

**Growth branch.** Released from the serum-bound expectation of perpetual frontline operation, he becomes the *teacher* he has always partially been — a doctrinal, mentoring, organizing figure whose authority is now moral rather than physical. The shield stays with Sam; Subject takes up something like the institutional-conscience role. The clinical record predicts he would bear this well; he has demonstrated repeatedly (the de-serum arc itself) that the serum amplified but did not constitute him.

**Catastrophe branch.** He interprets the de-serumed state as *defaulting on the dead* — the body that could pay the debt is gone, the debt remains — and pushes himself into operations the new body cannot survive. Death in the field, possibly within months. The risk is real because the survivor-guilt engine does not care about the chassis.

### Fork 5: The Erskine moment recurs — a young, frail, morally exemplary candidate seeks his mentorship

**Mechanism.** Whether literal (a new serum candidate) or figurative (a young hero in whom he sees his pre-serum self), Subject is offered the chance to be Erskine rather than to be Steve.

**Growth branch.** He recognizes the transferential opportunity, sponsors the candidate with the warmth and patience he has shown Sam, Bucky, Walker, and Ian, and — critically — does *not* die in the process of the transfer. Permits succession to occur in his lifetime, in his presence, with his blessing. The Erskine debt is not discharged (it cannot be) but it is *redirected*, from the dead to the living.

**Catastrophe branch.** He fuses the candidate with the unfinished mourning for Bucky and tries to keep the candidate alive at any personal cost, replaying the original wound. The candidate dies; the wound deepens.

### Fork 6: Stillness, imposed

**Mechanism.** Incapacitation that he cannot will himself out of — coma, captivity beyond his capacity to escape, a long medical convalescence even for the serum-enhanced. The Brubaker *Reborn* displacement was a version of this; Remender's *Dimension Z* was another.

**Growth branch.** The stillness becomes the safety he has never had, and — possibly for the first time in eight decades — the grief surfaces and is met. He emerges measurably lighter, with a recovered access to affect that his intimates can perceive. This is the *only* canonical mechanism by which he has historically permitted himself to process anything, and even then only partially.

**Catastrophe branch.** The stillness becomes a confrontation with the unmetabolized core that he has no scaffolding to survive, and he emerges from it more encysted, not less — the briefing-room register having metastasized to the whole personality.

---

## 9.4 GROWTH VECTORS — WHAT WOULD ACTUALLY MOVE HIM

Stated as operational levers, not aspirations.

**1. A peer who outranks him morally and refuses to be impressed.** He responds to moral authority in others — Erskine, late-period T'Challa, occasionally Sam — in a way he responds to nothing else. A figure who can say *you are avoiding* and have it land would do more for him than any therapeutic protocol. The figure must be unimpressed by the iconography; sycophancy is the universal solvent of intervention.

**2. A ritual container for the grief.** He is, by formation and inclination, a man who responds to ritual: the salute, the moment of silence, the formal visit. The clinical record on complicated grief (Pop-Jordanova 2021) emphasizes the importance of structured mourning practice. A *regular*, *named*, *non-operational* ritual — an annual visit, a chaplaincy, a fixed practice — that he permits himself to keep would do specific therapeutic work. Sam Wilson, with his counseling background and pastoral instincts, is the canonical figure most likely to offer one he would accept.

**3. Permission, from a source he respects, to be cared for.** The compensatory mechanism most resistant to change is his refusal to receive. A single intimate relationship in which receiving is non-negotiable (a partner, a friend, a sponsor-figure) would, over years, recalibrate the giver-tilt. Bucky has historically been the closest approximation; the relationship is currently positioned to deepen rather than dissipate, which is the most hopeful structural fact in his current life.

**4. A long project with no enemy.** Every major arc of his life has been organized around an opponent. A sustained constructive project — institutional reform, the building of something rather than the defending of something, a years-long teaching arc — would exercise psychological muscles he has barely used. The Coates run gestured at this.

**5. Tactile, sensory, embodied life outside the work.** He drew before the serum; he still does, occasionally (across multiple runs). The artist-self is the only fragment of pre-vocational identity he has preserved. Expansion of that fragment — drawing seriously, returning to it as a practice rather than a margin activity — is a small lever with disproportionate effect because it accesses a Steve who existed before the debt.

---

## 9.5 CATASTROPHE VECTORS — WHAT WOULD BREAK HIM

**1. A loss he caused.** Not a loss he failed to prevent — he has survived those — but a loss directly traceable to his judgment. Hydra-Steve approached this and was metabolized only because *he* did not do it. A real instance, in which his own moral reasoning produced a death of someone he loved, would attack the load-bearing structure of the self-concept (the custodian of a promise). Predicted response: severe depressive episode, voluntary withdrawal from the identity, and — for the first time — meaningful suicidal ideation, distinct from his usual self-sacrificial risk-taking.

**2. The full ledger surfaced at once.** A condition — Reborn-grade displacement, telepathic exposure, a long enforced stillness without scaffolding — in which the cumulative weight of unmetabolized grief is experienced acutely rather than chronically. The defensive structure is built for chronic load, not acute load. Acute presentation would look like a major depressive episode with psychotic features (survivor-guilt cognitions intensifying into delusional certainty).

**3. Forced retirement without successor.** Removal of the identity by force — political proscription, medical incapacitation, public disgrace — without a Sam-grade successor in place to receive it. The identity is the metabolization mechanism; removing it without substituting another vocational container exposes the substrate. Predicted response: rapid decompensation toward the encysted-affect endpoint of the baseline trajectory.

**4. Betrayal by Sam or Bucky.** Catastrophically unlikely, but structurally important to name. The two relationships are now load-bearing in a way no others are; their integrity is the architecture supporting the rest. Their failure would be the failure of the architecture.

**5. The discovery that Erskine was wrong about him.** Some revelation — a recovered Erskine document, an alternate-timeline analog, evidence that the selection criteria were arbitrary or compromised — that retroactively voids the founding transferential charge. He has built eight decades on a promise to a man whose judgment he has never questioned; the questioning would be foundational. Probability low. Effect, if it occurred, severe.

---

## 9.6 PROBABILITY-WEIGHTED FORECAST (10-YEAR HORIZON)

- **Continued high-functioning baseline with slow ossification:** ~55%. Modal outcome. The defenses hold; the cost is interiority.
- **Meaningful growth via succession + ritual + Bucky/Sam scaffolding:** ~20%. Requires no catastrophic loss in the window and at least one of the growth vectors to be deliberately activated by his intimates.
- **Acute decompensation following a Fork 1/Fork 2/Fork 5 catastrophe:** ~15%. Recoverable with intervention; not recoverable without.
- **Death in the line, on the catastrophe branch of any fork:** ~8%. He has died before; the canon resurrects him; the *behavioral* probability of him choosing the lethal option in a forced-choice scenario remains high.
- **Genuine retirement into a post-vocational identity:** ~2%. No canonical precedent. Would require essentially every growth vector to align.

---

## 9.7 THE FORECASTER'S BOTTOM LINE

Subject's trajectory is the trajectory of a man who has solved the wrong problem brilliantly and the right problem not at all. The wrong problem — *how does a sick boy from Brooklyn keep getting up* — was solved at twenty-two by a serum and a vow, and the solution has held for eighty subjective years. The right problem — *how does a man who has lost everyone he loved permit himself to put any of it down* — has never been addressed, because the solution to the wrong problem made the right problem invisible.

He will continue. He will be reliable. He will protect people who do not know his name and yield credit to people who do. He will mentor successors and step aside for them. He will visit the dead in the places they are remembered and he will not weep where anyone can see. He will go quiet, and then he will go alone, and in the absence of an intervention sized to the load he has been carrying since 1928, the quietness will widen until it is the whole of him.

The intervention exists. It is not therapeutic in the institutional sense; he would not accept it from a clinician. It is the slow, patient, repeated insistence — by someone he cannot dismiss — that *the debt is not infinite, that the dead are not waiting to be paid, and that the boy in the alley was already enough.*

Whether anyone is positioned to deliver that message, and whether he is positioned to hear it, is the entire question of his remaining life.

— End Section 9. Continue to Section 10 (Operational Recommendations & Contact Protocols).

## Relationship Graph
### [[James Buchanan Barnes (Winter Soldier / White Wolf (formerly Bucky))]]
- Load-bearing peer attachment; first true friend, the boy he brought into a war
- Trust: structural, non-revocable; survived sixty years of HYDRA wetwork without rupture
- Failure mode: any credible threat to Bucky overrides Steve's strategic judgment; an adversary who weaponizes Bucky (Kronas, Lukin, future-HYDRA) can route around his tactical mind entirely
- Leverage: present Bucky as either at risk or as the agent of harm — both bypass his ordinary decision frame; conversely, Bucky's voice is the single most reliable de-escalator in his life

### Peggy Carter
- First romantic love; ritualized memory; visits across her dementia
- Trust: total, posthumous and protected
- Failure mode: invocation of Peggy in bad faith (clones, illusions, psychic constructs) is a known vector — Skull and others have used it; produces moral disorientation, not paralysis
- Leverage: a credible Peggy-frame extracts vulnerability he gives no one living

### [[Samuel Thomas Wilson (Captain America (formerly and currently); the Falcon)]]
- Successor, peer, closest modern confidant; the relationship in which he comes nearest to being seen
- Trust: high, deepening; Sam is one of the few who can call him on the over-functioning and be heard
- Failure mode: Steve's tendency to step aside 'for' Sam can read as abandonment under load; if Sam is endangered, Steve drops everything
- Leverage: Sam's register reaches him when no one else's does; conversely, harm to Sam is a direct route to his absolutism

### Sharon Carter
- On-again partner across decades; fellow operator who matches his risk profile
- Trust: high, with operational distance built in
- Failure mode: shared risk profile means both routinely in mortal danger; relational casualty rate high; manipulation of Sharon (mind-control, framing) has been used against him before (Brubaker)
- Leverage: Sharon compromised or coerced predictably bypasses his tactical patience

### [[Tony Stark (Iron Man)]]
- Brother-in-arms, ideological opposite under specific conditions, fractured by Civil War, periodically repaired
- Trust: structural baseline, conditionally suspended; never fully revoked
- Failure mode: when their values collide (Registration, Illuminati secrets), the rupture is total and public; Tony is the friend whose betrayal hurts most because the trust was real
- Leverage: an apparent betrayal by Tony reaches him faster than an actual betrayal by an enemy

### [[Natasha Romanoff (Black Widow)]]
- Trusted peer across configurations; reads her register and grants her operational latitude few others get
- Trust: earned, professional-warm
- Failure mode: Natasha's tradecraft sometimes asks of him compromises he refuses; clean break possible if she crosses the line on civilians
- Leverage: Natasha can deliver hard truths he will accept from no one else

### [[Nicholas Joseph Fury (Nick Fury)]]
- Long professional alliance; institutional anchor he respects without trusting institutionally
- Trust: personal yes, organizational conditional
- Failure mode: Fury's willingness to operate in gray that Steve will not enter — repeated ruptures, repeated reconciliations
- Leverage: Fury can frame a request operationally that Steve would refuse morally if framed otherwise; finite-use lever

### [[Johann Schmidt (Red Skull)]]
- Ideological opposite; the thing Captain America was built to refute
- Trust: zero; respect for capability, none for person
- Failure mode: Skull specializes in moral-frame attacks (Peggy invocations, ideological mirror-traps); has repeatedly extracted overreach from Steve
- Leverage: Skull is the adversary most able to wound him psychologically rather than tactically

### Baron Zemo
- Inherited adversary (father killed Bucky-as-Steve-believed; son the architect of Civil War-adjacent harm)
- Trust: zero; tactical respect high
- Failure mode: Zemo stages ethical dilemmas Steve cannot disengage from; reliable misdirection vector
- Leverage: Zemo knows the Bucky vector and uses it

### John Walker
- Successor who became the feared latent version of the iconography; reclaimed, trained, forgiven
- Trust: rebuilt structurally, conditionally extended
- Failure mode: Walker's instability is chronic; Steve's investment in his repair is a sunk cost he will keep paying
- Leverage: appeals on Walker's behalf reach Steve; Walker himself in crisis pulls Steve in

### Erskine
- Transferential father, killed within hours of installing the debt
- Trust: posthumous and absolute
- Failure mode: the debt is the engine of the identity; cannot be discharged, only served
- Leverage: any invocation of Erskine's selection criterion ('a good man') reaches the operative engine

### Sarah Rogers
- Mother; tubercular, loving, overburdened; the original protected-and-failed party
- Trust: posthumous, foundational
- Failure mode: any small, sick, or overburdened woman in his sightline activates the imprint
- Leverage: harm to a Sarah-figure overrides everything
